Typographic Conventions
American English is the standard used in this handbook. The following
typographic conventions are also used.

Type Style Description

Example text Words or characters that appear on the screen. These
include field names, screen titles, pushbuttons as well
as menu names, paths, and options.
Also used for cross-references to other documentation
both internal (in this documentation) and external (in
other locations, such as SAPNet).

Example text Emphasized words or phrases in body text, titles of
graphics, and tables

EXAMPLE TEXT Names of elements in the system. These include
report names, program names, transaction codes, table
names, and individual key words of a programming
language, when surrounded by body text, for example
SELECT and INCLUDE.

Example text Screen output. This includes file and directory names
and their paths, messages, names of variables and
parameters, and passages of the source text of a
program.

Example text Exact user entry. These are words and characters that
you enter in the system exactly as they appear in the
documentation.

<Example text> Variable user entry. Pointed brackets indicate that you
replace these words and characters with appropriate
entries.

Course Overview
This course will provide an instructional overview of the processes Supply,
Refinery and Trading, organizational structures, master data and reports that
support the basic processes in Oil and Gas industry. Throughout this course, you
will have the opportunity to enhance your skills in system functions by completing
exercises at the end of each lesson. The exercises are based on the requirements
of the case companies, an International company and a Local affiliate company,
which are completing SAP for Oil&Gas implementation. You will join the
implementation team as a business analyst. The exercises will therefore ask you to
check, test and analyze various aspects of the industry supply chain and refinery
processes. Have fun in your new position!
The first unit gives you a brief overview of the organization structures in SAP
that are relevant to build up Oil company structures in the system.
The second unit deals with functions within Physical Oil and Gas Commodity
Trading, such as deal capture, trade management and trading commodity pricing.
The third unit covers business scenario International Export/Import Operations
(raw material). You become acquainted with processing of supply contracts
in sales and purchasing cycles. Next step is Bulk scheduling and operation
which is performed via Transportation and Scheduling Workbench (TSW) and
considers voyage scheduling, nomination and ticket processing. The scenario also
covers Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI) and interaction between Materials
Management and operations in TSW. Freight management part includes basics of
Transportation and Distribution (TD)
The fourth unit describes scenario Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound
Distribution). The steps of the scenario covers bulk pipeline scheduling, TSW
master data and operational inventory management.
The fifth unit describes silo management, refining, internal movements. The
scenario goes trough Hydrocarbon Inventory Management (HPM) to Refinery
processing and Reporting of internal movements.
The sixth unit covers business scenarios of exchange business and operations with
finished products. Within exchange business the scenario includes, master data,
agreements, operations management and settlement.
The seventh unit describes secondary distribution of finished products and covers
the whole range of functions in Transportation and Distribution (TD): basics,
master data of transportation units, shipment scheduling, loading and discharging,
shipment costs calculation and settlement.
The eighth unit is about processes based on service station retailing. It contains
fuel pricing, fuel stock management, tank management, payment settlement
(payment card, cash, fuel card) and dealer settlement

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. vii



Course Overview IOG100

The ninth unit consists of Reporting and Analytics for bulk supply chain. It is
described how to retrieve and analyze relevant for supply, refinery and trading
information using various reporting tools

business scenarios.
ï Gain understanding on application area of SAP for OIL&GAS functions (the

course does not cover customizing of the system).

Course Objectives
After completing this course, you will be able to:

ï Explain the realization in SAP for OIL&GAS basic functions of Supply,
Transmission & Trading and Refining.

ï Understand the purpose and assignment of enterprise structures required
for processing documents

Unit 1
Oil Company Structure and Logistics

Unit Overview
This unit gives brief overview of the typical structure and organizational levels of
International Oil Company. At the organizational level of Local Oil Company the
structure of Supply & Distribution Department is carefully explained. The unit
describes organization elements (units) and master data used in the modeling
process of company structure using standpoint of Primary and Secondary
Distribution with SAP for Oil&Gas.

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Explain the structure and organizational levels within an international oil
company

ï Explain the logistics and supply chain in a local oil company
ï Name the organizational elements in the logistics process
ï Define the enterprise structures in SAP for Oil&Gas

Unit 1: Oil Company Structure and Logistics IOG100

Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain structure and organizational levels within an international
oil company. You will study the organization elements and master data used in the
modeling process of a company structure. The lesson also gives you information
on the relationship between organizational elements and master data in logistics.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain the structure and organizational levels within an international oil

company
ï Explain the logistics and supply chain in a local oil company
ï Name the organizational elements in the logistics process
ï Define the enterprise structures in SAP for Oil&Gas

Business Example
One of the initial steps of an implementation project is modeling the company's
organizational structure. The project team has to build up the organizational
structure and master data in an international oil company and the German oil
company VOIL DE in compliance with SAP for Oil&Gas Primary and Secondary
Distribution.

Supply Chain Organizations
Organization varies by company and within a company structure, supply chain
management (SCM) may be referred to as supply, refining & supply, supply &
distribution, or refining & marketing, depending on the department.
Here we willl use the term supply & distribution (S&D) for the department with
the major supply chain management process that covers crude, feed stocks,
semi-finished products (blend stocks and rerun products), and ñ in terms of
production and distribution ñ finished products. Supply & distribution usually
needs the full scope of SCM.

2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics

Figure 1: S&Din an International Oil Company

In most oil companies, SCM is also applicable within individual departments for
specific product lines, such as liquefied petroleum gas (LPG); lubes (including
or excluding base oil); jet fuels (aviation gasoline, kerosene, and lubes); asphalt
(regular or oxidized); or coke (regular or calcinate). There may be also SCM for
specific customers handled by individual departments, including industrial and
wholesale customers (usually heating oil, diesel, or heavy fuel oil) or marine
(diesel, bunker fuel, or lubes). The scope of SCM within these departments varies
according to specific business requirements.
There may be interactions, for example, Aviation and Marine just sell and S&D
and Lubes provide the products. Here there is a shared SCM process. In many
companies, Aviation and Marine are organized globally with their own global
sales systems. Companies may decide to interface these systems to capture
local movements and inventory in SAP. Billing may be captured as well, that is,
accounting is handled in SAP, and order taking and scheduling are outside of SAP.

Subdivisions in a Typical S&D Department
A typical S&D department is divided into business units.
Planning and optimization
This unit is responsible for the different planning cycles (yearly, monthly, and
weekly for day-to-day business; long-term for strategic decisions). It may include
planning optimization but usually only partially, for example, refinery production

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 3



Unit 1: Oil Company Structure and Logistics IOG100

or lubes blending. This business unit could also be responsible for product
exchange and term contract (purchase and sale) economics. Guidance is given on
inventory handling, minimum/maximum, and targets.
Trading
Trading is responsible for purchases and sales as per planning signals, using
term contracts plus necessary spot deals to balance. Depending on the company
philosophy, third-party trading is used to optimize, with or without hedging to
secure wet deals. Usually, there is also a close link to upstream for production
trading, that is, sales of surplus production or sale and purchase to optimize
supplies (for example, to minimize transportation costs).
Scheduling
Scheduling handles daily operations within planning cycles (usually weekly and
monthly cycles). This includes tanker, barge, rail, truck, and pipeline programming
for crude, feed stocks, semi-finished products, base oil transfers, purchases,
and sales (primary distribution). The resulting slates (basically shopping lists)
bridge trading and transportation, that is, they are the basis for all nominations to
suppliers (or vendors), customers, terminals, inspection companies, and so on.

Figure 2: S&D Departments and Responsibilities

Transportation

4 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics

Transportation is responsible for negotiation of transportation term contracts to
cover basic transportation requirements. This covers programming of available
transportation units based on slates from scheduling; in (or out) chartering
of capacity to balance coverage; safety and environmental issues; and vessel
screening (ship, crew safety status, technical condition, and ship safety record).
Terminal Operations (including refinery distribution terminals)
Terminal operations handles coordination of loading and discharging of different
transportation units (berth/loading rack scheduling). Terminal maintenance
includes tanks, racks, berths, pipes, gauging systems, and so on. Terminal
operations is also responsible for posting of issues and receipts and physical
inventory measurements, and gain/loss management.
Administration
Administration is responsible for term and spot contract administration (purchase,
sale, exchange); claim handling (contract pricing, product gain/loss, demurrage );
and inventory management (reconciliation and physical inventory adjustments).

Note: Inventory management may be handled by controllers rather
then S&D. This is a common Change Management issue in SAP
implementations.

The same structure is applicable (either fully or partially) to other departments,
such as Lubes or industrial and wholesale customers.

S&D Busines Partners
The supply & distribution department interacts daily with business partners
represented by internal and external parties.
External: Third Party

Crude oil supplier, location Saudi Arabia, Dharan
Crude oil supplier, location UK, London
Crude oil, Feed stocks trader, location Switzerland, Geneva
Exchange partner, location Germany, Hamburg
Cargo inspector, international
Shipping agent, international
Forwarding agent, international
Supply sales customer, location Germany, Frankfurt
Supply sales customer, location Czechia, Prague
Crude pipeline operator, location Triest (terminal) and Munich (headquarter)
Product pipeline operator, location Frankfurt

External: Own International Company (but different entities)

SCM Logistics Example for the S&D Business
Organization
The logistics organization of primary and secondary distribution in German Oil
contains organizational units allocated in Europe. Following the supply chain of
crude oil into the refinery via a pipeline, and oil products out of the refinery via
different means of transportation, the supply & distribution department has to
monitor logistic operations as follows:
ï Multiple crude or feed stocks purchasing terminals (1)

ñ International locations operated by supplier (or vendor) or third party
ï Crude terminal (pipeline head) Triest (2)

ñ International (on coast) location
ñ Joint venture operated by third party (pipeline operator)
ñ Joint storage for all shippers, that is, by grade, not by ownership
ñ Receipt and storage of crude and feed stocks on behalf of shippers.

ï Crude pipeline Triest ñ Ingolstadt (3)
ñ Movement of crude and feed stocks from crude terminal to refinery

(across border).
ñ Joint venture operation with third-party pipeline operator

ï Refinery Ingolstadt (represented as terminal) (4)
ñ Domestic (off coast) location operated by S&D. This terminal is not

identical with the refinery distribution terminal. The distribution
terminal receives the products listed under output from the refinery.

ñ Input into the refinery: crude and feed stocks (condensate, naphtha,
distillate, vacuum gas oil, atmospheric residue)

ñ Output from the refinery: gas, semi-finished products (naphtha,
vacuum gas oil, atmospheric residue, base oil, solvents), and finished
products (LPG, gasoline, distillate, fuel oil, asphalt, coke)

Organizational Elements in the Logistics Process
Organizational elements are structures that represent the legal or organizational
views of an enterprise. You can design your company structure based on your
business processes. Defining organizational levels is an essential step in your
project and is vital for all subsequent activities.
Analyze the organizational structures and process structures in your company and
match them with SAP structures. Once you have decided on an organizational
structure, it is very difficult to change it.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 9



Unit 1: Oil Company Structure and Logistics IOG100

Figure 5: Organizational Elements in the Logistics Process

Each client contains its own organization elements, master records, and set of
tables. SAP systems use the client concept to allow legally and financially
independent entities to coexist in a system. Clients are part of the defining
technical structure of the SAP system. From a business perspective, the client
forms a corporate group. System transactions provide special functions for
working with clients.

Note: Client names are always numeric.

10 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics

The procurement process uses the following organizational elements:
ï As the smallest organizational unit in external accounting, the company

code represents an independent accounting unit. This includes entry of all
accountable transactions and the creation of all proofs for a legally required
individual account closing. Documents such as balance sheets and profit and
loss statements are created at company code level.
An examples of a company code might be a company within a corporate
group or a subsidiary.

ï The plant is an organizational element within a company.
Materials management is primarily concerned with the flow of materials.
From a materials management point of view, a plant is, above all, a location
where material stock is kept. A plant can be a manufacturing facility or a
warehouse distribution center.
In production, a plant can represent a manufacturing facility. In sales and
distribution, a plant represents the location from which materials and services
are distributed and corresponds to a distribution center. The relevant stocks
are kept here. A plant can, for example, represent a grouping of storage
locations in physical proximity. If you sell a service, a plant can represent
the location from which services are rendered (such as an office).
A plant must be uniquely assigned to a company code. The assignment
between sales organizations and plants does not have to be unique. The plant
is essential for determining the shipping point.

ï The storage location allows the differentiation of material stocks within a
plant. Inventory management on a quantity basis is carried out at storage
location level in the plant. Physical inventory is carried out at storage
location level.
Plant and storage location are organizational units that can be used by all
logistic areas.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 11



Unit 1: Oil Company Structure and Logistics IOG100

Figure 6: Organizational Elements in Procurement and Inventory
Management

The purchasing organization is responsible for the enterpriseís purchasing
requirements. This unit is structured to negotiate the general conditions of
purchase for one or more plants or companies. Pricing conditions are set at
the purchasing organization level. You can incorporate purchasing into the
company structure by assigning the purchasing organization to company codes
and plants. This means that you can determine whether or not purchasing is
organized centrally in your company. You can distinguish between plant-specific,
cross-plant, and cross-company-code purchasing.
The purchasing group represents a buyer or a group of buyers who is responsible
for certain purchasing activities. This cannot be assigned to a purchasing
organization.
The sales organization is an organizational unit in logistics that groups the
enterprise according to the requirements of Sales and Distribution. A sales
organization is responsible for distributing goods and services. Therefore, it is also
liable for sold products and is responsible for the customers' rights of recourse.
The sales organization is also used, for example, to take a regional, national, or
international subdivision of the market into account.
A sales organization is uniquely assigned to a company code. More than one
sales organization can be assigned to a company code. If you use Sales and
Distribution, you need at least one sales organization. You maintain your own
master data for a sales organization. In the sales statistics, the sales organization

12 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics

is the highest summation level. All items in a Sales and Distribution document,
that is, all items of an order, an outbound delivery, or a billing document, belong
to a sales organization.
A distribution channel is a means through which saleable materials or services
reach the customer. Several distribution channels can be assigned to a sales
organization. If you use Sales and Distribution, you need at least one distribution
channel. The distribution channel is used to:
ï Define responsibilities
ï Achieve flexible pricing
ï Differentiate sales statistics
A division is used to group materials and services.
A sales organization can have several divisions assigned to it, for which it is
responsible. If you use Sales and Distribution, you will need at least one division.
The system uses the division to determine the sales areas to which a material or
a service is assigned. A division can, for example, represent a product group.
Therefore, you could restrict price agreements with a customer to a certain
division. You can also conduct statistical analysis by division.
The sales area is a combination of the sales organization, distribution channel,
and division. It defines which distribution channel a sales organization uses
to sell products from a certain division. Each Sales and Distribution document
is assigned to exactly one sales area, and this assignment cannot be changed. A
sales area can belong to only one company code. This relationship is created by
assigning the sales organization.
During the processing of Sales and Distribution documents, the system accesses
various master data, according to the sales area. This master data includes, for
example, customer master data, material master data, prices, and discounts. In
addition, the system carries out several checks concerning the validity of certain
entries according to the sales area.

Note: A simple organizational structure can be better than a complex one.
For example, it simplifies master data updates. Do not define complex
organizational structures just to have detailed reporting options. Use fields
on the master data screen instead.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 13



Unit 1: Oil Company Structure and Logistics IOG100

Figure 7: Organizational Elements in Sales and Distribution

The shipping/receiving point is the highest-level organizational unit that controls
your shipping activities. Each inbound or outbound delivery is processed by one
shipping point. The shipping point can be a loading ramp, a mail depot, or a
rail depot. It can also be, for example, a group of employees responsible for
organizing urgent deliveries.
You assign a shipping point at plant level. A shipping point is a physical place and
should be near the delivering plant. More than one shipping point can be assigned
to a plant. You can also assign several shipping points to a plant. This would be
appropriate for plants in physical proximity.
Shipping is an integrated module of logistics executive processing.
A loading point is a place in a shipping point where goods are loaded or
discharged.
Business partners are legal or natural persons with whom you have a business
relationship. Customers and vendors are business partners with whom you have a
relationship involving the transfer of goods and services.
Business partners have a number of different functions, described as partner
functions, in connection with your company. You use partner functions to define
the rights and responsibilities of each partner type in a business transaction.
Different business partners may carry out one or more partner functions. For
this reason, you can assign individual business partners to a number of partner
functions. Data on business partners is managed in master records. Data on partner
functions is stored in these master records and used in financials and logistics.

14 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics

A business partner can be a customer and a vendor at the same time if, for
example, your customer also supplies goods to you, or if a vendor is also one of
your customers. In this case, you must create a customer master record and a
vendor master record for the business partner. You can create a link between the
two master records by entering the vendor number in the customer master record
and the customer number in the vendor master record.
The vendor master record contains information about a vendor from a purchasing
and accounting perspective. Data in the vendor master record is structured into
three categories:
ï General data: This includes the vendor communication data, address and

bank details, for example. This data is valid for the entire corporate group
(client).

ï Company code (accounting) data: This comprises data such as the number
of the reconciliation account and the payment methods for automatic
payment transactions. This is maintained at company code level.

ï Purchasing data: Data on the vendor is managed separately for each
purchasing organization, for example, payment conditions. This includes the
purchase order currency, Incoterms, and the vendor's tax data.

General data, for example, address data, is also relevant to purchasing. There
are other levels for purchasing data that are optional, such as plant and vendor
sub-range.
In accounting, the vendor is regarded as the companyís crediting business partner.
The vendor master record is therefore maintained by accounting and purchasing.
You can use the authorization concept to define how data maintenance should be
organized in the vendor master record. Each department can maintain general
data, as well as purchasing and accounting-specific data, centrally or decentrally.
Often, purchasing also maintains data at corporate group level.
You can block a vendor master record, for example, if the quality of the vendor's
products is poor. You can block a vendor for an individual material via the source
list.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 15



Unit 1: Oil Company Structure and Logistics IOG100

Figure 8: Business Partners

The customer master groups data into categories such as general data, sales area
data, and company code data.
The customer master includes all data necessary for processing orders, deliveries,
invoices, and customer payments.
General data is relevant for Sales and Distribution and for accounting. It is
stored centrally (client-specific) to avoid data redundancy. It is valid for all
organizational units within a client.
Company code (accounting) data is relevant for accounting. It is valid for the
respective company code.
Sales area data is relevant for Sales and Distribution. It is valid for the respective
sales area (sales organization, distribution channel, and division).
Examples of other business partners in the SAP ERP system are:
Contact persons are people in a business partner company with whom you are
in contact by telephone, mail, or in person to perform business transactions. You
store detailed information on contact persons in business partner master records.
Because the contact person is part of the business partner company, you enter
contact person data in the respective customer or vendor master record. You do
not need a separate master record for contact persons. You assign a new number to
each contact person in a master record. You can enter as many contact persons as
desired for each business partner. The data for the contact person can be used in
the associated functions in logistics and financials.

16 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Enterprise structures and Logistics

During their day-to-day activities, your sales personnel in the field and in the
office have the opportunity to gather information about competitors. You can
record this competitor data in the system as master data. In sales support, you can
maintain master records for each of your competitors. You can store information
about competitive products in a special kind of material master. You maintain
master records for competitors in the same way as you maintain customer master
records. You can store the competitor's address, information about the marketing
profile, and key people in the competitor master record. By using texts (which you
can tailor to your own requirements), you can also record extensive information
about each competitor's activities.
The material master record is the main source of material-specific data in an
enterprise. It is used by all logistics modules. The integration of all material
data in a single database object prevents the problem of data redundancy. Every
area, such as purchasing, inventory management, materials planning, and invoice
verification can use the stored data.
Since materials are processed by various user departments within a company, and
each department stores different information for the materials, the material master
is grouped by user departments (functions). Each user department has a different
view of the material master record and is responsible for maintaining the data
to support its function, for example:
ï Basic data relevant for all areas: Valid for all organizational units within

a client
ï Purchasing data for ordering
ï Sales organization data relevant for Sales and Distribution: Valid for the

respective sales organization and the distribution channel
ï Plant data relevant for Sales and Distribution: Valid for the respective

delivering plant
ï Inventory management data for posting goods movements and managing

physical inventory
ï Accounting data for material valuation upon goods movements or in invoice

verification
ï Materials planning data for material requirements planning (MRP)
There is additional data for several other areas, which is valid for various
organizational units. The data maintained within a view may be valid for more
than one organizational level.

Unit 2

Trading

Unit Overview
In the trading environment, it is necessary to control and organize the flow of
materials and services from vendors to customers. The principle of the business
is to match demand from the customer with supply from the vendor. This type
of business is known as back-to-back business. The industry defines this type of
business as business where purchasing and sales are carried out in parallel, in the
same international / regional trading department. The unit illustrates Trading &
Operations Business Landscape which is available with SAP for Oil&Gas.

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï List the typical business process in the global trade of oil commodities
ï Describe the major functions in trade management with GTM
ï Recognize the document flow to be generated under trade contracts
ï Operate logistics transactions in GTM with SAP for Oil&Gas

Lesson: Global Trade Management
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain some typical business process of physical oil and gas
commodity trading and will identify Trading & Operations Business Landscape,
which is available with SAP for Oil&Gas. The lesson focuses on Global Trade
Management (GTM) and illustrates the document flow to be generated under a
trade contract. You will learn major functions in trade management with GTM,

and position management.

Lesson Objectives

Business Example
International Trade VOIL INT (company code 1000) arrange a quarterly volume
for certain type of crude oil to be purchased from supplier Saudi Arabian Oil
(vendor 400003) to fulfill the requirements of VOIL DE (customer 300000).
International Trade processes the deal with crude oil. It only takes ìflash titleî
of ownership, meaning that the commodity is sold immediately after purchase.
Both deals are concluded on a Free On Board (FOB) basis in a port of origin
(Sidi Kerir in the Mediterranean Sea).
There are logistics and financials transactions to be performed to execute this
back-to-back deal, such as goods receipt, goods issue, invoice verification, and
customer billing.

Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading
Physical oil and gas commodity trading is usually considered in the context of
international trade, which is the economic interaction among different nations
involving the exchange of goods and services, that is, exports and imports. The
guiding principle of international trade is comparative advantage, which indicates
that every country, no matter their level of development, can find something that it
can produce cheaper than another country.

In the trading environment, it is necessary to control and organize the flow of
materials and services from vendors to customers. The principle of the business
is to match demand from the customer with supply from the vendor. This type
of business is known as triangular business, principal business, or back-to-back
business.
The industry defines this type of business as business where purchasing and sales
are carried out in parallel, in the same international or regional trading department.

Business Scenario: Supply Wet Barrels
It is common practice to negotiate term purchase contracts with major suppliers
of crude, such as Aramco, Saudi Arabia or Statoil, Norway. These deals are
usually concluded by global or regional headquarter trading organizations, that
is, different entities within the company. There may be also term contracts with
upstream entities. This organizational structure is driven by company needs and
may be different for major oil companies. Because of this, the purchase process of
crude becomes a transaction chain of supplier to international trading to receiving
affiliate. This transaction is also called a trade or back-to-back deal.
The pricing is nearly 100% based upon a pricing formula, using officially
published quotes on commodity exchange to reflect real market conditions.
Quotes are published for standard products by location (market) and for some
crudes (marker crudes) and feed stocks. Crude without published quotes is linked
to marker crudes plus differentials for quality and location differences. The
formula structures are, in general, highly complex.
Contracts are concluded for a specified period (usually a year). They may be
also concluded as ìevergreenî contracts with renegotiation dates (usually every
year). There may be also term contracts with third-party trading companies for
crude (exceptions) and feed stocks (more common). Spot purchase contracts are
concluded for various reasons with all potential suppliers (major crude and feed
stock suppliers, competitors, other trader, and so on). These are one time deals,
usually with one delivery only, to cover unplanned requirements. The pricing is
mostly formula or quotes-based as well, but may be also agreed at a fixed price.
International / regional trading is responsible for vendor management with
international or upstream crude suppliers. The local affiliate concludes a standard
purchasing agreement with the company trading entities. The terms are variable,
but usually the trading company sells at acquisition price plus a fee for the service
provided.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 35



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

Figure 15: Business Scenario - Supply Wet Barrels

Figure 16: Business Scenario - Supply Contracts

International / regional trading is responsible for proper handling of risks related
to changes in market prices for crude oil and currency exchange rates. Hedging
provides a way to protect company profit and control or limit risks. There are

36 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

a number of hedging scenarios. A typical example for a ìshort hedgeî is the
purchase (by a trader) of foreign crude (long haul from Arabian Gulf), to be
delivered to the United States Gulf Coast and sold at prevailing spot prices.
The trader fears that prices will fall before delivery can be made. To protect his
purchase (wet barrels), the trader sells futures contracts (paper barrels) to fix his
sales price, thereby fixing his resale margin.
Hedging transactions must be linked to the related purchase or sale of wet barrels
to determine the net profit or loss for the whole scenario of securing a wet trade by
the futures market. The transactions are standardized per exchange (NYMEX, IPE
London). Contracts or lots represent a specific volume, for example, 1 NYMEX
contract: 1,000 barrels.
A hedging scenario for currency is applied when the contract currency is different
from domestic one of international / regional trading. Thus a certain amount
of currency has to be purchased or reserved by the due time of payment under
the contract to avoid risks related to failing or rising domestic/contract currency
exchange rates. International / regional trading purchase currency option to
acquire certain amount of currency at fix price on the future date.
Futures transactions in commodity/currency hedging do not represent physical
movements, that is, there is only financial accounting. Proper hedge accounting is
essential so that futures losses can be properly balanced with cash market gains,
and cash market losses with futures gains.

Global Trade Management
In the SAP system, this type of business process, in which sales and purchasing
processes are carried out simultaneously, is defined as a trading business. A
trading contract is used to handle this ordering process. Subsequent transactions,
such as goods receipt, inventory management, goods issue, invoice verification,
and customer billing are maintained in the standard Sales and Distribution (SD)
and materials management (MM) components.
The trading contract enables you to implement various different business
transactions to integrate sales and purchasing documents. For example, you
receive a sales order from a customer, search for the best vendor to fulfill the
customer's requirements, and issue a purchase order, all in one transaction. You
coordinate shipping, transportation, and customs clearance for the goods. The
vendor then delivers the goods directly to the customer. The trading company
receives an invoice from the vendor, and bills the customer. Finally, you receive
payment from the customer and make a payment to the vendor.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 37



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

Figure 17: Global Trade Management

Trading contracts are documents in the SAP System that integrate multiple legal
contracts between customers and vendors. With the trading contract, both sales
and purchase contracts or orders can be maintained using a single transaction.
In a trading company, one person or department usually carries out both buying
and selling procedures. The simultaneous sales and purchasing data entry screen
is necessary to avoid redundant data entries and reduce missed operations.
With one trading contract document, the system creates follow-on sales-side
documents and purchase-side documents after releasing. In the contract document
header, you can maintain sales-side data that is copied to each item line. Then you
maintain purchasing data in each item line. You can create multiple purchase
orders to fulfill one sales order if necessary. The trading contract can be used as
one-sided contract, such as a purchase-only contract or a sales-only contract.
Using position management, you can manage the material position and subsequent
process of a one-side contract item.
The trading contract component is a center of trading business. It incorporates
sales orders, purchase orders, and vendor billing documents for trading expenses.
Users can monitor the processing status of all subsequent transactions associated
with the trading contract via extended document flow.
The trading contract also provides accurate profit simulation report, including all
the costs and revenue elements.
After the deals are completed and all the data is transferred to accounting, you can
use the trading contract number to check the actual profit.

38 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

Supply with Title Transfer
The trading contract is an order-processing document that integrates sales and
purchasing information in one transaction. It is used as a basic document for the
entire trading process. Trading execution, the follow-on process of the trading
transaction, and expense handling are based on the trading contract.
In the trading contract, you enter both sales and purchasing information: customer,
vendor, material, sales and purchase unit, sales and purchase price, and so on. In
addition, you can also enter planned expenses relative to the trading contract.

Figure 18: Document Flow - Supply with Title Transfer

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 39



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

Figure 19: Document Flow - Supply with Title Transfer without MM

In the scenario, you create a pre-trading contract to maintain a trade agreement
that contains long-term sales and purchase arrangements. You also can use a
trading contract to maintain just one part of an arrangement, either sales orders or
purchase orders, depending on your requirements. During processing, you create
sales and purchase-side trading contracts with reference to an existing pre-trading
contract. This is useful in cases where you want to create a contract referencing a
previous contract for the same customer or referencing a pre-contract at item level.
If the document status is set to approved, subsequent documents, such as a sales
order and a purchase order, can be automatically generated in the background
while the system creates a trading contract.
Subsequent trading transactions such as goods receipt, inventory management,
goods issue, invoice verification, and customer billing are initiated via the Trading
Execution Workbench and are maintained in Sales and Distribution (SD) and
materials management (MM). The follow-on process of expense handling is based
on the trading contract and is initiated via the TWE as well.

The Trading Execution Workbench
In global trade, you often need to process several different kinds of transactions at
the same time. The TEW is used to process all follow-on documents related to a
trading contract. It provides a central cockpit where traders can process trading
contracts and their subcomponents, such as purchase orders, sales orders, and

40 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

follow-on documents. In addition, the TEW automates a large part of the data
entry, making processing quicker, easier, and more error-free. You can call the
position management and trading expense functions directly from the TEW.

Figure 20: Trading Execution Workbench

the role-based layout of the TEW is Customizable to support different lines
of business (for example, crude oil or feedstock). Smart functions anticipate
which tasks you want to perform and suggest the appropriate source and target
documents automatically. The system remembers your selection settings from
one session to the next.
You can process multiple documents on one screen (including creating deliveries,
shipping notifications for customs clearance, posting goods issue, and so on). A
document flow diagram helps you keep track of what follow-on documents you
have already processed and what remains to be done. A message area on the
screen displays all errors, warnings, and information messages that you receive
during the current session.
Constraints
If you process a document in the TEW, you cannot use standard SD/MM
transactions to make changes to it, as this could lead to data inconsistency.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 41



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

To process documents on the initial Trading Execution Workbench screen, choose
the TEW mode that represents your line of business. You have to define the
following selection criteria:
ï Group: This represents a group of steps, or tasks, involved in processing

a given kind of trading (for example, tasks involved in export, domestic,
back-to-back trading, and so on).

ï Step: This indicates the target document you want to create (for example,
delivery document).

ï Mode: This indicates the action you want to perform (for example, create,
change, copy with reference).

ï Prestep: This indicates the document you want to use as your data source
(for example, sales order).

Trading Contract: Price Determination
In trading contracts, you use price determination to maintain both purchase and
sales prices efficiently. You can enter the purchase and sales price per unit directly
in the item if the price per unit is already known when you create the trading
contract. If the sales price is not known, it is possible to simulate the sales price
using the purchase price. Retail pricing can be used to calculate sales prices using
the determining purchase price and a markup.
Purchase and sales price determination sequences for retail and standard pricing
are defined in the Customizing settings. You can therefore use your own
calculation schema if those specified in the SAP standard system do not meet
your business requirements.
With SAP for Oil&Gas there is another option available. Formula and average
pricing (F&A pricing) uses external quotations such as Platts, Reuters, The
Oil Market Report, and The European Oil Telegram to determine the price of a
material. It can be used both on the purchasing side and on the sales side.
The purpose of formula and average pricing is to enable the calculation of product
prices with the help of external quotations over a set period of time. The price can
be further modified with company-defined calculation rules before it is used. The
system also takes into account currency fluctuations within the time period.
Price quotation data can be entered manually or it can be entered via a remote
connection to a data provider using the data feed function of the external quotation
interface. The external quotation interface automatically makes real-time market
data available for F&A pricing. The interface accesses and accepts published
prices, rates, and commodities from providers of financial information, such as
Reuters, Platts, or Telerate.

42 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

Figure 21: Trading Contract Price Determination (1)

Figure 22: Trading Contract Price Determination (2)

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 43



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

The options for price determination in a trading contract are:
ï Direct purchase and sales price entry
ï Price determination using the SAP standard calculation schema (standard

pricing)
ï Price simulation using trade pricing (retail pricing)
ï Price determination using SAP for Oil&Gas formula pricing (F&A pricing)

Trading Expenses
Trading charges linked to the trading contract can be processed using the trading
expense function. The trading expense function enables you to handle various
costs and commissions incurred by a trading business. There are various types of
expenses in the trading environment, all of which are realized at different times
and posted to different accounts, and these are often not synchronized with the
main flow of a trading contract.
Trading companies must efficiently control trading-related expenses, such as
inland/ocean freight, loading charges, storage costs, insurance, customs duty and
commission. It is important to accurately assess costs, including purchasing costs
and all trading charges associated with the trading contract.

Figure 23: Expense Overview - Types of Expense

The trading expense function is fully integrated with the trading contract so that
you can centrally maintain purchase related expenses and selling related expenses.

44 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

Planned expenses can be entered in the trading contract and accrued. You
can maintain an estimated expense value in a trading contract. This value is
included in the contract price calculation as the system automatically transfers the
planned value to the contract pricing schema. You can then see the entire planned
profitability of a contract.
You can maintain the planned expenses until the contract is completed.
Unplanned expenses can be linked to the trading contract at a later stage when
you receive invoices from service providers, freight forwarders, insurance
companies, and customs offices. It is thus possible to assess accurate profitability
as costs and revenue elements are linked to the trading contract. During trading
contract processing, you can post expenses without referencing any planned data.
The vendor billing document is used to process unplanned expenses. After the
trading contract is released, unplanned expenses can be created. Both sales and
purchasing expenses can be posted.

Figure 24: Expense Posting Process

The above figure depicts the relationship between the trading contract process and
the trading expense process.
The new process flow gives you more flexibility in maintaining expense data. In
trading contract processing, you can maintain planned expenses, which are treated
as pricing conditions in the contract pricing schema. You can reference them when
you post expenses in other processes.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 45



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

When logistics documents are processed, you can post expenses to a specific
account. The vendor billing document is used to post expenses. It has an
additional function that enables you to post expenses to both accounts payable
and accounts receivable.

Position Management
Position management reduces inventory risk and selling loss. Position
management has two main functions. The first is to control the values entered
during contract creation. The second is to create links between sales and
purchasing data at the item level. Supporting this, two main functions have been
created: portfolio management and association management

Figure 25: Risks from Independent Supply and Demand Chains

Portfolio Management.
A special key is dynamically assigned to the contract item. This is used to
optimize the sales and purchasing balance. If position management is active in
your system, one portfolio master record is assigned to each trading contract item.

46 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

Portfolio management contains a function that monitors the item position. In
Global Trade Management, a portfolio is defined as a predefined selection group
that makes finer item classification possible. The main purposes of portfolio
management are to:
ï Classify the trading contract items
ï Report similar product lines
ï Control important materials, countries, customers, or vendors in view of

risk consideration
Portfolio determination is executed when trading contract items and quantities
are fixed. The system determines which portfolio to assign when you confirm
the material, its quantity, and its and value in an item line. The system searches
for the appropriate portfolio master record using the condition technique. The
portfolio is assigned automatically when maintaining a trading contract; however,
the assigned portfolio can be changed manually when alternative portfolio records
exist. If multiple records are selected, the system processes according to the
determination rules (manual/automatic determination). The assignment method
depends on the Customizing settings. You can also customize the timing of the
portfolio assignment

Business Benefits of Position Management
Association Management.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 47



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

When you want to associate a sales item with a purchasing item, the system
searches for the target item using the item portfolio master record as the key.
The system tracks item position information The main purposes of association
management are to:
1. Create and maintain a document item link

The system searches for the appropriate association partner list, based on the
assigned portfolio. You can create new associations between items with the
same portfolio.
Association maintenance is possible in both the trading contract and the
logistics document. In the trading contract, you can call association functions
either manually or automatically. In the logistics document, you cannot see
the association directly using the document. It is maintained separately using
the Trading Execution Workbench, or by creating the logistics document.

2. Update open quantity information
Once a portfolio is assigned to a contract item, the system checks the item
position and authorizes processing of the item with the associated quantity.
You can refer to the open quantity and value status report in the contract.

3. Update the contract item position
Depending on document transition, the contract item position also changes.
It is automatically updated when you process the document using the Trading
Execution Workbench. You can refer to the association status report to see
how far the contract has been processed and which association partner it has.

48 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

Figure 26: Business Benefits of Position Management

During trading contract processing, the association function can be started during
the following processes:
1. Creating a trading contract
2. Creating a new logistics document (only in the sales processes)
3. Changing an item quantity during logistics document processing (only in the

purchasing process)
4. Maintaining the association independently using the Trading Execution

Workbench
Associations can be maintained soon after a portfolio is assigned to a contract
item. You can customize when the association maintenance function is called. It
can be called automatically or manually. Association maintenance is possible only
if there is an open item quantity in the contract.
The association can be maintained during sales document processing using
the TEW. This function is called at the point of follow-on sales document
maintenance. The system requires you to check association data before proceeding
to the document maintenance screen. You must complete the association step
before you proceed.
The selected document must be in Released status. Only a contract with follow-on
logistics document processing can be selected as a source document. A portfolio
record must have been assigned during contract creation.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 49



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

You can maintain the association of the existing document using the Trading
Execution Workbench. You can see and maintain the association relationship
independently of any logistics process. The item position is updated automatically
as association maintenance takes place.

SAP GTM Scenario: Supply Wet Barrels
The trading contract enables you to implement various business transactions for
integrating sales documents and purchase documents.
As an example scenario, International Trade VOIL INT (company code 1000)
arranges a quarterly plan volume for certain crude oil type to be purchased from
supplier Saudi Arabian Oil (vendor 400003) to fulfill the requirements of VOIL
DE (customer 300000). The simultaneous entry of sales and purchasing data is
necessary to avoid redundant data entries and reduce missed operations.
Actual operations under this pre-trade contract are positioned as back-to-back
deals on an FOB basis in a port of origin (Sidi Kerir in the Mediterranean Sea)
and posted in the system with purchase and sales trading contracts. Approval
of a contract initiates creation-relevant MM and SD orders to manage logistics
operations.

Figure 27: SAP GTM Stock Scenario for Supplying Wet Barrels

Subsequent transactions such as goods receipt, inventory management, goods
issue, invoice verification, and customer billing are maintained in SD and MM via
the Trading Execution Workbench. Logistics operations with flash title transfer

50 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Global Trade Management

through International Trade VOIL INT is posted with goods receipt and goods
issue. Financial execution and management is performed with invoice verification
and customer billing.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 51



Unit 2: Physical Oil and Gas Commodity Trading IOG100

ï Execute a business process in the TEW for the sales side of the contract
ï Display the complete document flow created under the trade contract

Business Example

volume for certain crude oil type to be purchased from supplier Saudi Arabian
Oil (vendor 4900##) to fulfill the requirements of VOil DE (customer 3900##).
The trading contract nables you to implement different business transactions to
integrate sales and purchase documents. The simultaneous entry of sales and
purchasing data is necessary to avoid redundant data entries and reduce missed
operations.

Unit 3
International Export/Import

Operations

Unit Overview
The International Export/Import Operations of raw materials have to comply all
the international laws and rules that have been agreed and taken into consideration
in the Trading phase (Incoterms). The flow of materials and services from vendors
to customers is theoretically controlled and organized by Schedulers who are
responsible for daily operations as per planning cycles (usually the weekly/monthly
cycles). Tanker-, Barge-, Rail-, Truck- and Pipeline-programming for crude, feed
stocks, semi-finished products, base oil transfers, purchases and sales (primary
distribution). Resulting slates (basically shopping lists) are bridging Trading and
Transportation, i.e. they are the basis for all nominations to suppliers (or vendors).

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Understand Tradeŕs and Scheduleŕs interaction
ï Explain typical business process in International Export/Import Operations

(Marine scenario)
ï Supply contracts
ï General understanding of Bulk Scheduling Management (TSW ñ Trader's

and Scheduler's Workbench)
ï Nomination processing and document flow when Bulk Marine Voyage

Scheduling
ï Explain concept of Transport Unit and Vehicle
ï Understand the tasks and operations to be executed under Freight Contract
ï Explain Laytime and Demurrage Calculation
ï Explain the concept of Stock Projection Worksheet (SPW)
ï Operate with TSW document flow
ï Understand the purposes of Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI)

IOG100 Lesson: Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule Management

Lesson: Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule
Management
Lesson Overview
Lesson Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule Management explains the
Business Scenario of Supplying crude oil by means of Marine transportation.
Supply contracts must exist between with Vendors where terms and conditions as
quantities, materials, validity periods, payment terms and pricing are defined. This
is handled by Contract Operations Management. Once the contractual conditions
are define, the Scheduling and Transportation of the raw material is realized using
SAP for Oil&Gas (TSW ñ Trader's and Scheduler's Workbench). TSW provides
the relevant master data to model the supply chain. The stock projection, planning,
and nomination processes enable the scheduler to schedule bulk shipments while
taking into account supply, demand, and available transportation.
You use the marine scheduling functions to plan marine shipments, including the
loading and unloading of product, handling the use of lightering vessels, and
numerous ship-shore events. The information supplied by the marine scheduling
functions, includes the most recent data concerning nominations, vessel progress
during a voyage, terminal and port status, and the inventory at each location.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Understand Tradeŕs and Scheduleŕs interaction
ï Explain typical business process in International Export/Import Operations

(Marine scenario)
ï Supply contracts
ï General understanding of Bulk Scheduling Management (TSW ñ Trader's

and Scheduler's Workbench)
ï Nomination processing and document flow when Bulk Marine Voyage

Scheduling

Business Example
Continuing with the scenario started in the previous Unit (UNIT 02: Physical Oil
and Gas Commodity Trading) where International Trade VOil INT (Company
code = 1000) arrange a quarterly volume for certain type of crude oil to be
purchased from supplier Saudi Arabian Oil (Vendor = 400003) to fulfill the
requirements VOil DE (Customer = 300000). The receiving terminal is Triest.
The raw materials (crude oil) is shipped from the different load ports called
origin locations O (eg. Location = Sidi Kerir in Egypt) to Triest destiny location
D (Location = TRIEST) with chartered tankers (Transport system: MARINE
INT). The tanker size varies but cannot exceed a maximum according to the

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 81



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

constraints of the receiving installations and the constraints of the Triest harbour.
It is stored jointly with the same grades of other shippers, i.e. there is no dedicated
storage for the individual shipper. The 3rd party operator plans and decides on
behalf of the shippers. Each shipper has to observe rules related to the maximum
allowed inventory and storage time in Triest. The shippers are only allowed to use
the tankage in Triest for buffering the required stocks for pipeline shipments in
batches, not for long term storage. Non observance of these rules leads to waiting
time and demurrage for the future tanker arrivals of the relevant shippers.

Supply of Crude Oil based on Contracts (Trade)
It is common practice to negotiate term purchase contracts with major suppliers of
crude (e.g. Aramco, Saudi Arabia; Statoil, NorwayÖ). These deals are usually
concluded by Global and/or Regional Headquarter Trading organizations, i.e.
different entities within the company. This transaction is also called a TRADE and
has been studied in the previous unit.
Oil International has several contracts with different suppliers on a term basis.
Beside the term deals spot contracts are concluded as required.
Purchase Contracts of Oil International
The receiving plant for all this deals is the underlying plant of transport system
MARINE INT representing a virtual location where the ëflash titleí of Oil
International passes through.

Figure 30: Supply of Crude Oil based on Contracts (Trade)

82 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule Management

International Trading negotiates with the receiving Local Affiliate at Triest a
Purchase Contract for the Crude oil that has been purchased in the international
market.
Sales contract Oil International where the buyer is Oil Local Affiliate
The customer here is Oil Local Affiliate. There are also similar contracts with
other affiliates in reality. Oil International trading allocates the purchased crude
according to the crude economics of the corporation and the economics of the
affiliates.
The sales are performed out of the underlying plant of transport system MARINE
INT (as for the purchase contracts before).
Purchase contract of Oil Local Affiliate where the vendor is Oil International
Normally this contract is not matching the sales contract Oil International to Oil
Local Affiliate in terms of number of items because of the Incoterms. Depending
on the conditions agreed, if the final buyer (Oil Local Affiliate) is responsible for
the transport or if the supplier of Crude is responsible for the transport different
Incoterms apply, the business is different and the follow on transactions in SAP
are different.
The purchase of Oil Local Affiliate is done into plant 1107 (TRIEST terminal)
so that the scenario is the second case described, the supplier is responsible for
the transport.

Contract Operations Management
Different agreements take place between the different parties: Supplier, Oil
International and Oil Local Affiliate for the Supply of the Crude to the Terminal.
In these agreements conditions and responsabilities of the deals are fixed. These
conditions have to be considered by Schedulers as well as all the results coming
from the Planning and Optimization area. Global headquarters provides official
publisher information, i.e. quotes from Platts, Reuters, Argus, LORÖ, for the
international business (copy right, needs to be purchased). There are also local
quotes available like OMR in Germany.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 83



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Figure 31: Contract Operations Management

Merchants tend to use short expressions, such as FOB and CIF, to clarify the
distribution of functions, costs and risks related to the transfer of goods from seller
to buyer. But unfortunately misunderstandings frequently arise with respect to the
proper interpretation of these expressions. It was considered important to develop
rules for the interpretation of the trade terms which the parties to the contract
of sale could agree to apply. Incoterms ñ for international commercial terms ñ
constitute these rules of interpretation.
The pricing is nearly 100% based upon a pricing formula, using officially published
quotes, in order to reflect the real market conditions. Quotes are published for
standard products by location (market) and for some crudes (marker crudes) and
feed stocks. Crudes without published quotes are linked to marker crudes plus
differentials for quality and location differences. The formula structures are in
general high or medium complex. Sometimes they are very complex involving
price escalation based upon crude quality (API gravity, Sulfur, ViscosityÖ). It is
also common to use specific price out periods for individual crude grades
Transfer Pricing
Transfer prices are usually market based relative to industry/competitive supply
sources. The transfer price to marketing should match 3rd party market alternative
in the region or around a terminal. Price timing and volumetric flexibility should
be consistent with 3rd party deals. Rack prices should be used where possible (if
available). All major oil companies have defined fairly complex ìBest Practicesî.
Transfer Prices are usually quoted in standard temperature and base unit of
measure and in local currency. This requires the correct conversions for mass /
volume and currency exchange rates.

84 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule Management

Scheduling Business tasks & SAP for Oil&Gas (TSW)
Handling and Confirmation of Movement
Scheduling is responsible for the coordination of a movement from source to
destination. This implies a high degree of communication (telephone, fax, telex,
e-mail), verifying contracts, provide load- / discharge data, fulfill tax and legal
reporting.
Nominations
Tanker, barges, and Trains (high volume transportation) need to be nominated to
suppliers, customers, terminals, pipelines, and rail companies. Rail companies
may only provide the engine and schedule the movement for their rail network. In
case of cross border movements multiple rail companies may be involved.
Each operator (in- or external) has nomination rules that are defined as general
rules or specific for a deal in the contract. Not complying with these rules may or
may not create additional costs (demurrage, overtime, higher pumping tariff Ö).
Nominations are also required for required services like cargo inspection,
forwarding agent, vessel agent Ö
Also in the nomination processes the scheduler needs the highest possible degree
of automation to send out standard nomination documents for the individual
movement or service.
Tanker Scheduling
Based upon the crude pipeline schedule a tanker program (usually called slate)
has to be determined. The slate starts off with already purchased cargoes and the
related tanker. The cargo may already be in transit at sea. If the crude purchase
is confirmed, but not yet loaded and no vessel assigned, the volume is slated
without ship, using the term TBN (to be nominated) for the vessel with the volume
purchased. The timing used is based upon the agreed loading date range and the
anticipated sailing time. Finally the open requirements are determined and the
required arrival range in the pipeline terminal. As a placeholder the crude grade
with the best economics is used and with the highest possible volume to reduce
freight costs. If the actual purchase volume does not match the slated volume, all
succeeding open requirements must be re-scheduled.
Crude and Feed Stock Slate
Based upon the final batch program, the actual and planned cargo arrivals and
the resulting stock projection, the open crude and feed stock requirements are
determined. They are listed on the slate and form the ëpurchasing listë for Global /
Regional / S&D Trading.
Barge Scheduling

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 85



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

The barge schedule is driven by the demand of the receiving distribution terminal,
plus demand of supply sales to customers. There may be a common schedule for
S&D (responsible for deliveries to distribution terminals) and I&W (responsible
for delivered sales to industrial and wholesale customers). The main scenario is the
transportation of purchased product to receiving locations along a major waterway.
Barge Slates
Depending upon the number of barge movements, this slate is done or not. If there
is a limited number, nominations only will do (individual or for a period).

Figure 32: Scheduling tasks: VOIL INT business

86 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule Management

Figure 33: Scheduling tasks: VOIL DE business

Trader's and Scheduler's Workbench (TSW) provides functions for stock projection
and for planning and scheduling bulk shipments using nominations. TSW provides
the relevant master data to model the supply chain. The stock projection, planning,
and nomination processes enable the scheduler to schedule bulk shipments while
taking into account supply, demand, and available transportation.

TSW Overview: Push-Pull Model
Trader push - trading is performed based on market opportunities that the trader
recognizes at least partially independently of the supply chain dynamics at any
given time. These ìdealsî are then placed as scheduling requirements on the
scheduler, who views them in the SPW. That is, these deals are ìpushedî into
the supply chain by the trader.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 87



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Figure 34: TSW Overview: Push-Pull Model

Scheduler pull ñ the supply chain dynamics drive the trader to buy and sell based
on the inventory positions (from the SPWs) within the supply chain, for example,
at the request of the scheduler. That is, the supply chain ìpullsî product from
the trader.

TSW Master Data Overview
TSW allows you to model the supply chain of an oil company, including pipeline
systems, marine routes, customers, vendors, and plants.
Transport system
Transport systems are TSW master data objects that represent stock holding
objects to which you can assign locations. They represent pipelines or marine
routes as they exist in the real world. A transport system is a single, in-transit,
stock-holding object used for inventory management purposes. Depending on
individual requirements for modeling a supply chain, the transport system can
represent a fixed supply route, a supply region, or a mode of transport. Examples
of transport systems are a pipeline system or a marine route.
One of the functions of a transport system is to link the locations in the supply
chain. A transport system should always have two or more assigned locations.
During scheduling, you must assign a transport system to a nomination. A location
can either be an origin for the transport system (supplies product into the transport
system), or the location can be a destination for the transport system (receives

88 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Contract Operations and Bulk Schedule Management

product from the transport system). You can also define a location as both an
origin and a destination. As a result, the supply network is defined in terms of
injection and discharge points for each transport system.
Location
A location is a fixed point on the supply chain where goods are handled (such as
plants, warehouses, supply sources, and markets). Locations are nodes along a
transport system. You define the business purpose behind a location by assigning
partners to them.
You can also define planning locations, which represent a collection of a number
of real locations, for example a region. This aids scheduling at earlier stages
when schedules need to be generated but specific locations or partners are not yet
definite. Note that planning locations may overlap, that is, a real location may be
included in multiple planning locations, thus providing optimum flexibility when
creating planning views.
Partner role
Using the partner role concept, you can assign certain functions to the different
TSW objects. A location is either a plant, a customer location, or a vendor location
in the real world.
You define TSW partner roles in the master data record used to define business
partners. The partner role includes information about the activities that the
business partner can perform and where the business partner performs these
activities. You can also define stockholding objects, such as plants and storage
locations as partner roles.
You define partner roles based on existing System master data records, such as
a vendor, customer, or plant. Because the partner role defines the activities that
a business partner performs in the TSW supply chain, you must assign transport
systems or locations to the master data record of each partner role.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 89

Marine Scenario: Real World versus Document Flow
Schedulers in VOIL INT typically plan marine voyages weeks in advance in
order to ensure that long-term contract based demands for crude from different
customers at various locations Worldwide can be satisfied. For some of these
voyages, VOIL INT manages the necessary master data and organizes the
shipments. For this purpose, nominations are sent to a marine carrier. For other
cases, the sale takes place at the time of loading and therefore VOIL INT is not
concerned with arranging the shipment. Once a movement is executed, a ticket is
created and the movement is posted in system.

Figure 37: Marine Scenario: Real World versus Document Flow

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 91



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

The complete scenario could include all these documents as it is shown in the
slide but not necessarily, it depends on terms and conditions. Document Flow
can consists of a number of documents: Deal, Contract, Nomination, Ticket for
loading (official note sent by a partner containing information about a product
movement, that is real product movement), MM Call-off, TD Shipment, Ticket for
discharging, Sales Call-off, Delivery, Goods Issue.

TSW Nomination
A nomination is the scheduling document used to communicate between TSW and
the carrier. You use the nomination to schedule bulk shipments. The system uses
nominations as the basis for generating subsequent SAP system documents, such
as deliveries and shipping notifications. A nomination typically has several line
items, which you create or change according to stock levels and planning proposals
displayed in the SPW. The TSW nomination supports several movement scenarios.

Figure 38: TSW Nomination

The nomination involves the following activities:
ï Creating and changing planned material shipments, which the system

uses when generating the SPW for locations, thus enabling the planned
replenishment of locations.

ï Communicating with the carrier, customer and all other parties which are
related with the transport.

ï Providing the necessary information to other SAP System processes, such
as to generate ñ Transportation and Distribution (TD) shipments as well
as all other associated documents.
