Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Lesson: Vehicle Concept and Freight Contract
Lesson Overview
Trader's and Scheduler's Workbench (TSW) includes functions to support
the process of Marine Scheduling. The following functions are included in
marine scheduling: Berth Scheduling, Fleet Management, Freight Contracts,
Measurement Comparison, Laytime and Demurrage Calculation. Within this
lesson functions Freight Contracts and Laytime and Demurrage Calculation will
be considered.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain concept of Transport Unit and Vehicle
ï Understand the tasks and operations to be executed under Freight Contract
ï Explain Laytime and Demurrage Calculation

Business Example
VOil DE has purchased the raw material (crude oil) on FOB basis in a port of
origin and wants to deliver it to the port of destination. The raw material (crude
oil) is shipped from the load port (Location = SIDI KERIR) to Triest unload port
(Location = TRIEST) with chartered tankers (Transport system: MARINE INT).
Freight Contract stores information about the agreements made with a carrier
regarding the movement of product. There are two subtasks to be covered: Freight
agreement and Laytime agreement.

Marine Scheduling ñ Freight Contract
Trader's and Scheduler's Workbench (TSW) includes functions to support the
process of Marine Scheduling. The functions support the scheduling of marine
vessels, handling of port events, tracking of voyages, and arrivals at a port or
terminal.
You use the marine scheduling functions to plan marine shipments, including the
loading and unloading of product, handling the use of lightering vessels, and
numerous ship-shore events. The information supplied by the marine scheduling
functions, includes the most recent data concerning nominations, vessel progress
during a voyage, terminal and port status, and the inventory at each location.
The following functions are included in marine scheduling: Berth Scheduling,
Fleet Management, Freight Contracts, Measurement Comparison, Laytime and
Demurrage Calculation.

104 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Vehicle Concept and Freight Contract

Within this lesson functions Freight Contracts and Laytime and Demurrage
Calculation will be considered.

Figure 39: External service - Transportation

Figure 40: Vehicle structure

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 105



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

In Traderís and Schedulerís Workbench, freight contracts represent agreements
with a vessel carrier and contain the agreed upon terms, conditions and rates for
bulk shipments. You can create freight contracts to represent agreements, such as
time charters, voyage charters, or contracts of affreightment.
Freight Contracts store information about the agreements made with a carrier
regarding the movement of product. Freight Contracts provide data for other
TSW functions, such as the calculation of laytime and demurrage, as well as the
calculation of despatch.
Laytime and Demurrage
Laytime is the time period during which a vessel is at a port or berth. Demurrage
is the contractually agreed penalty that is due when a vessel remains too long at a
location during loading or discharge operations.
The Freight Contract contains the agreed amount of time the vessel is allowed to
spend at a location and the subsequent demurrage rate to be charged when the time
is exceeded. Additionally, the Freight Contract contains the agreement on how
to handle events that can influence laytime, such as delays due to bad weather or
equipment that is out of service on shore.
The Laytime Calculation function calculates laytime based on a freight agreement
and the events you enter in a nomination. If the contractually agreed laytime is
exceeded, the system automatically calculates the potential demurrage liability.
Using the default function for laytime terms, you can define sets of laytime terms
that you can then reuse when creating freight contracts. In this way, you can avoid
having to recreate laytime terms that are frequently used.

Transport Unit Type - Marine
A vehicle is the means by which you transport product from one location to
another. In TD, a vehicle is defined in a master data record. This is done for
the following reasons:
ï Each vehicle is unique and consists of a fixed number of transport units
ï Each transport unit is unique and consists of a fixed number of compartments
ï Each compartment is unique and is used as the basis to schedule and load

product for transport.
ï The vehicle type defines the mode of transport, such as marine and other

vehicle attributes. When creating a vehicle you must first choose a vehicle
type.

106 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Vehicle Concept and Freight Contract

Figure 41: Vehicle structure

The vehicle is defined as a logical combination of transport units within the
vehicle master data record. The vehicle type determines what type of transport
units can be assigned to a vehicle. A vehicle consists of transport units. At least
one transport unit must have loading capacity. The mode of transport of the
vehicle type must match the mode of transport of the transport unit type for each
transport unit assigned to the vehicle.
Certain vehicle attributes are stored in the vehicle master data record, while other
vehicle attributes are defined for the vehicle type in Customizing and are copied
into the master data record when creating a vehicle. Vehicle attributes pertaining
to the physical dimensions of the vehicle are defined when creating vehicle master
data. The maximum weight and volume are calculated from the transport units and
their compartments. Physical dimensions (height, length, width) can be defined.

Freight Contract processing
The maintenance transactions for sales and purchase contracts include data
fields where you can maintain freight contract information, such as charter
party, laytime, and demurrage agreements. For example, to create a freight
contract for chartering a vessel, you create a purchase contract and add the freight
contract information in the TSW Details. You access the TSW Details dialog box
from the maintenance transactions for sales and purchase contracts. The TSW
Details dialog box includes tabs and fields for freight contract information. In
Customizing you can also define a customer-specific tab.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 107



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Figure 42: Freight Contract - TSW relevance

You can view TSW Details at item level of sales and purchase orders, sales and
purchase contracts, and returns. If you double-click on the document number
in the nomination, you can navigate directly to the documents assigned to a
nomination item.
You access TSW Details by choosing TSW Dtls at the bottom of the screen. The
TSW Details dialog box appears. TSW Details are on the following tab pages:
ï Scheduling
ï Nomination
ï Charter 1
ï Charter 2
ï Laytime
ï Laytime Terms

Freight Contract - TSW Details
Scheduling
The following data is displayed in the Scheduling section of TSW Details:
ï TSW relevance indicator
This determines if the document is relevant for stock projection. When the system
finds an order that has been set as TSW relevant in Customizing, this indicator is
set automatically. When the system sets the relevance indicator, you can no longer

108 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Vehicle Concept and Freight Contract

change the relevance indicator. If the indicator is not set automatically, you can
manually set the indicator. You can set the relevance indicator so that you can
reference the document item in the nomination.
ï Reference document number
ï Date range (deal validity periods) for SD or MM document items
ï Location or planning location
You can enter a TSW location or planning location in TSW Details.
ï Multiple modes of transport (MoT)
You can assign multiple MoTs to the order or contract item. Depending on
the Customizing settings for TSW nominations, you may need to specify the
scheduling MoT in the Multiple MoT dialog box in TSW Details.
ï Events
You can assign events to order or contract items and you can assign a Mandatory
or Not allowed attribute to events. This determines whether the event in the
nomination is mandatory or not allowed for the location you have entered. The
time, for which the event is mandatory, is either added to or subtracted from the
number of days entered.
ï Deal information
ï Tolerances for prorate calculation
For prorate calculation, you can enter upper tolerances, no tolerances, or unlimited
tolerances.
ï Amendment control for Location Balancing
You can allow amendment control in Location Balancing. You can enter
tolerances, within which it is possible to amend quantities.
If you want to activate Group Amendment, you must also activate Amendment
Control.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 109



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Figure 43: Freight Contract - Ship Charter

Charter 1
Details on charter agreements, such as:
ï Laydays start (the first day when the ship arrives according to charter

agreement) must fall before Laydays end (the last day when the ship arrives
as stated in the charter agreement).

ï You can determine or exclude locations for loading or discharging.
ï You can set whether or not products or product groups can be transported on

the chartered vehicle.
Charter 2
Details on charter agreements, such as:
ï Declarations by the parties to the agreement; here, for example, the owner or

the charterer can determine the availability of the vessel.
ï Cargo size; here, you can determine, for example, the minimum quantity that

is to be transported.
ï Performance; here, you can determine data such as speeds.
ï Bunker; here, you can enter various consumption rates.
Laytime
Laytime and demurrage details are used to calculate the laytime and demurrage
in a nomination.

110 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Vehicle Concept and Freight Contract

Laytime Terms
The detailed data on laytime terms is used to calculate the laytime in the
nomination.

Laytime and Demurrage Calculation
Laytime is the time period during which a vessel is at a port or berth. Demurrage
is the contractually agreed penalty that is due when a vessel remains too long at a
location during load or discharge operations.
Laytime Calculation
The laytime calculation is a function that uses the laytime agreement from freight
contracts and the specific laytime events saved in the carrier nomination. In
the freight contract you maintain information about the allowed laytime of a
vessel during loading, discharging, or lighterage. In the carrier nomination you
maintain the events that are relevant for laytime calculation. Additionally, you can
customize how the system handles events that can influence the allowed laytime,
such as weather conditions or facility down time at the port.
The system takes the following into account for the calculation of laytime:
Actual laytime: for the calculation of actual laytime (and demurrage), the system
checks the events from the carrier nomination.
Potential laytime: the system calculates potential laytime based on the quantity in
the nomination and the pump rate given in the contract or in the nomination.
The system uses the formula: Laytime potentially subject to demurrage = Total
laytime incurred - (allowed laytime + excludable delays).

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 111



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Figure 44: Laytime and Demurrage Calculation

Demurrage Calculation
Demurrage is the contractually agreed penalty for exceeding the laytime (the
time allowed for loading, discharging, or lighterage). The system calculates the
demurrage fee based on the potential or actual laytime, the contractually allowed
laytime, and the demurrage fee maintained in the freight contract.
The system uses the formula: Demurrage costs = net demurrage time X net
demurrage rate X demurrage factor.
You maintain the demurrage rates and demurrage factors as pricing conditions
in Customizing. If the contractually agreed laytime is exceeded, the system
automatically calculates demurrage. You can configure the system to show the
demurrage amount as a work list item.

IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management
Lesson Overview
This Lesson explains the stock projection process which is concerned with the
operational level monitoring and management of stock positions throughout
the supply chain. This includes stock at locations such as terminals and bulk
plants, refineries as well as in-transit. This includes updating current stock
positions with book or physical values; projecting stock positions forward into the
future; taking all inbound and outbound forecasts, schedules and movements into
account; consideration of tankage constraints; stock simulations; and nomination
triggering. During the stock projection process, you can calculate, change, and
simulate inventory forecasts using the Stock Projection Worksheet in Traderís
and Schedulerís Workbench (TSW).

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain the concept of Stock Projection Worksheet (SPW)
ï Operate with TSW document flow
ï Understand the purposes of Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI)

Business Example
VOILl DE operates with crude supply network planning, analyzes via Stock
Projection Worksheet situation with inventory positions on different locations
(Location = TRIEST) and calculates the inventory forecast for a date or time period
and for combinations of material, location, transport system, and valuation type

Bulk Operational Inventory Management
During the stock projection process, you can calculate, change, and simulate
inventory forecasts using the Stock Projection Worksheet in Traderís and
Schedulerís Workbench (TSW). The Stock Projection Worksheet calculates and
shows the inventory forecast for a date or time period and for combinations of
material, location, transport system, and valuation type.
A combination of system settings determines what data the Traderís and
Schedulerís Workbench (TSW) uses and in what way the data is used to generate
the Stock Projection Worksheet. Settings made for master data, inventory data,
and Customizing form the basis for generating the Stock Projection Worksheet.
The Stock Projection Worksheet shows the projected stock for the selected
combination of transport system and material or location and material
combinations. You can also designate a material and valuation type to include
the owner of the material in the Stock Projection Worksheet. You can carry out

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 125



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

ìwhat-ifî simulations of incoming and outgoing bulk shipments to see the effect
of these shipments on the projected inventory. You can also apply selected what-if
shipments to the schedule directly from the Stock Projection Worksheet. In the
Stock Projection Worksheet you can change forecasted rack issues and see the
changes to the projected inventory.
The Stock Projection Worksheet is divided into a selection or filter area on the
left and a results area on the right side of the screen.
Selection Area
The data you enter in the selection area for location, material, transport system,
and valuation type (owner) determine the Stock Projection Worksheet results that
the system displays in the tabstrip on the right. Also, you can select the subtract
heel and accumulate negative inventory functions in the selection area.

Figure 45: Stock Projection Worksheet (SPW)

Results Area
You can view the projected stock and the settings used to generate the Stock
Projection Worksheet on the following tabs:
Stock Projection
The Stock Projection tab displays the projected inventory for all the dates within
the rolling period including quantities for the base inventory, what-if simulation,
bulk receipts, bulk issues, and forecast figures for rack issues. The following
columns on the Stock Projection tab display the stock projection figures:

126 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

1. Period
The Date column always displays the date of each Stock Projection
Worksheet line and the Day column always shows the day of the week
for the date.

2. Inventory
2.1. What-If Simulation

The results of the what-if calculation are displayed in the Inv.What-If
column. You can enter what-if figures in the Stock Projection Worksheet to
simulate the effects on the inventory. The actual quantities are not changed
during what-if simulation.

2.2 Base Inventory
The Inventory column displays the most accurate inventory figures
available. The Stock Projection Worksheet calculates the base inventory
quantities using actual quantities when possible, but uses scheduled
quantities where actual quantities are missing or are incomplete. The base
inventory quantities are highlighted, if there is a corresponding TSW
Worklist item.

3. Bulk Goods Receipts and Goods Issues
3.1. Proposed Quantities

For bulk receipts, the REC-Proposed column shows the replenishment
proposal generated by the planning engine. These are the proposed
quantities to cover replenishment needs not covered by existing
nominations. You can open a dialog box from the bulk receipts item to see
the corresponding bulk issues item which is displayed at the same date line
minus the offset. For bulk issues, the figures in the ISS-Proposed column
are the same as the corresponding receipts proposal. The quantities are
highlighted, if there is a corresponding TSW Worklist item.

3.2. What-If Quantities
In the REC-What-If and the ISS-What-If columns you can manually enter
quantity figures, such as from nominations to simulate results from the
current day forward. The system also displays document quantities that
are not yet assigned to nominations. You must define this in Customizing
for simulated schedules. Here you select stock projection as the simulation
application and documents in stock projection as the schedule category.
You can save the what-if figures so that they are used as part of the stock
projection data that the system uses for subsequent scheduling.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 127



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

3.3. SAP Documents
For Bulk Receipts the unscheduled quantities from documents, such as
contracts, quoatations, purchase requests, and purchase orders are displayed
in the REC-Doc.Qty column. You define the use of SAP documents in stock
projection using various customizing and system settings for document
relevance. For Bulk Issues the unscheduled quantities from the sales order
are displayed in the ISS-Doc.Qty column. In both cases the quantities are
the difference between the document quantity and the scheduled quantity.
When all order items have been scheduled, no figure is displayed in this
column. You can view details about the assigned documents by selecting
the quantity figure in the REC-Doc.Qty column or ISS-Doc.Qty column.
A dialog box appears containing the document number, line item number,
item quantity, and unscheduled quantity. You can navigate to the document
by double-clicking on the document number in the dialog box.

3.4. Scheduled Quantity
The REC-Sched. and ISS-Sched. columns display the quantities scheduled
in a nomination on a particular date. The corresponding nomination
number is displayed in the REC-Nomination or ISS-Nomination column. If
there are multiple items scheduled in the nomination for the same date, the
quantities are added and the total quantity is displayed. You can view the
quantity of each item by selecting the nomination number and selecting
Nomination References on the toolbar. A dialog box appears showing each
item of the nomination. When multiple nominations are relevant to one
scheduled quantity, the word Multiple appears and you can navigate to the
individual batches. The quantities are highlighted, if there is a relevant
TSW Worklist item.

128 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

3.5. Nomination Number and Status
The REC-Nomination and ISS-Nomination columns show the identifier for
the nomination that corresponds to the Stock Projection Worksheet item.
The REC-Nom Status and ISS-Nom Status columns show the overall status
of the nomination. A nomination can be scheduled but not actualized,
partially actualized, or completely actualized. Actualized nominations
contain line items that have been confirmed through tickets.

3.6. Actual Quantity
The REC-Actuals and ISS-Actuals columns show the sum of all actualized
quantities (quantity from a nomination or nomination item for which a
ticket exists). The system ignores these quantities when the projected
inventory is calculated for the Stock Projection Worksheet. Actual
quantities are displayed for the current date or days in the past.

3.7. The REC-Ticket and ISS-Ticket columns show the sum of all ticket
quantities for a particular date (corresponds to the ticket end date). You can
view all the tickets that correspond to the quantity by double-clicking on
the ticket field.

Attributes
On the Attributes tab you can view the data used to generate the Stock Projection
Worksheet, such as the rolling period, days in past, Stock Projection Worksheet
unit of measure, conversion factor, book inventory, and relevant planning
parameters, as well as, the parameters used to calculate the forecast figures for
rack issues.
1. Starting Date: The starting date is the first day used when the system

generates the Stock Projection Worksheet.
2. Rolling Period: The Stock Projection Worksheet uses the days in past values

and rolling period values from the master data record of the transport system
or location. The Rolling Period is used to define the number of days for
which the Stock Projection Worksheet is displayed. In conjunction with the
days in past value, this defines the start and end date for the Stock Projection
Worksheet.

3. Stock Balancing: The stock balancing function is used to balance the
incoming and outgoing movements in terms of projected stock figures.

Physical Inventory
You can use physical inventory figures as the basis for stock projection. You can
view the physical inventory data by selecting the Physical Inv. tab in the Stock
Projection Worksheet. You can maintain physical inventory data for a location,
material, and valuation type.
Quality Calculation

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 129



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

The Quality calc. tab displays the results of the Reid Vapor Pressure (RVP)
calculation. When you select the Quality calc. tab, the system calculates the
average weighted RVP based on the bulk receipts and their RVP value. To include
RVP calculations in your stock projection, you must maintain RVP values in
nominations.
During the calculation for weighted RVP, the system multiplies the Stock
Projection Worksheet inventory by the RVP value before receipts, adds the
scheduled receipts multiplied by the RVP value in the nomination, and divides that
figure by the inventory plus the scheduled receipts.

Stock Projection Worksheet ñ Inventory Management
You can use the What-If functions of the Stock Projection Worksheet to simulate
different affects on the inventory. You can perform stock projection for the
following types of inventories.
Base inventory
The SAP book inventory is generally the basis for calculating the base inventory.
The system calculates the base inventory by taking into account all actual and
expected incoming and outgoing movements. However, in Customizing you can
define the physical inventory as the basis for calculating the base inventory. In
this case, the Stock Projection Worksheet uses the latest update of the physical
inventory as the starting inventory.
What-If inventory
The basis for calculating the what-if (simulated) inventory is either the physical
inventory or SAP book inventory. The calculation of the what-if inventory
considers all the actual and expected incoming and outgoing movements including
what-if figures entered in the Stock Projection Worksheet.

130 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

Figure 46: Inventory Management

Physical Inventory
You can use the physical inventory as the basis for generating the Stock Projection
Worksheet. In this case, the system calculates the base inventory using the
physical inventory. Also, the what-if inventory for future days is based on the
latest update of the physical inventory. The starting inventory for a particular date
is initially calculated using the first inventory quantities received for that date, for
example the last reported gauge readings. In the Stock Projection Worksheet, the
base inventory column displays physical inventory and the column for the planned
inventory displays the what-if quantities.
You maintain physical inventory data for a locations, materials, and valuation
types. You can also maintain the physical inventory for a location and the tanks
assigned to a location.
In the master data records for locations and materials, you activate the stock
projection based on the physical inventory of the location and material.
You can view the physical inventory data that you entered for a location, tank,
material, and valuation type by selecting the Physical Inv. tab in the Stock
Projection Worksheet.
You can also perform a historical analysis of the physical inventory for alternate
materials to track, for example, the seasonal changeovers of materials.

TSW document flow ñ Ticket
Ticket

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 131



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

This object is an official notice sent by a partner, such as a carrier, that is sent by
fax or E-mail and contains information about the movement of product. Tickets
are entered in Traderís and Schedulerís Workbench (TSW) either automatically
by electronic interchange using the Intermediate Document (IDoc) format, or by
manually entering the ticket data in the system. If you receive incomplete tickets
as IDocs from the carrier, you have to process these manually.
The various TSW movement scenarios are triggered by the receipt of a movement
ticket from an external source, such as a pipeline carrier. TSW has a holding
structure for tickets and controls the subsequent processing when a ticket is
entered in the system.
You can define customer-specific functions using junction functions in
Customizing to control the processing of documents after a ticket is posted
(actualized). You can group these functions into function groups and assign the
applications relevant for processing.
Each TSW movement scenario has a corresponding junction function group to
control the document processing related to posted tickets.
Ticket Transaction
The ticket transaction allows you to:
ï Process multiple ticket items such as inspector reports, measurement

documents, tickets that can be posted, or tickets created by prorate
calculation.

ï Use the quantity conversion interface (QCI) from the Hydrocarbon Product
Management (HPM) component in ticket transactions. This allows you to
calculate the actual quantity for each ticket in multiple units of measure
(depending on the unit of measure group assigned to the material) and save
the quantities and corresponding conversion parameters in the new ticket
tables.

ï Issue a bill of lading, certificate of origin, or delivery tickets at item level
in nomination maintenance.

132 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

Figure 47: SPW - Inventory Management

Figure 48: TSW document flow - Ticket

Ticket Types

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 133



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

You can define different ticket types. You use ticket types to start certain actions
in the system or prevent the system from performing these actions. When defining
a ticket type, you can assign processes, such as ticket actualization, prorate
calculation, or measurement comparison, and set permissions and enter default
values.
You can also include a base unit of measure, which allows the system to use a
uniform unit of measure during loading. As a result, the values issued by the
quantity conversion interface (QCI) are consistent (for example, L15, BB6) for all
physical measurement tickets.
Ticket Validation and Actualization
You can save the ticket directly without validating it.
To validate a ticket, choose Validate. The system checks the values in the ticket
against the nomination items, such as the scheduled quantity and actual quantity,
and against documents that have already been created. You define which checks
the system performs in Customizing. To actualize a ticket, choose Actualize. The
system checks the data in the ticket. If the check is completed without any error
messages, the system starts the routine for generating subsequent documents, such
as call-offs, goods issues, and goods receipts. The movement scenario to which
the nomination item is assigned determines which steps the system performs
during the actualization process. You make the movement scenario settings in
Customizing.
If ticket actualization is successful, the nomination is updated with the actual
posted quantity, the nomination status is changed, the relevant SAP documents are
generated, and the document flow is created. You can view the document flow on
the Display Ticket: Overview + Details screen by choosing the Doc. flow tab page
in the Item Details section of the screen.

Hydrocarbon Quantity Conversion
Oil and oil products are bulk products in liquid form that are processed and
shipped in large quantities. Even the smallest fluctuations in temperature can
result in considerable fluctuations in volume, and as a result, to significant
fluctuations in value.
Because the measured volume of an oil product is temperature-dependent, volume
correction and density correction are required, because the density of material is
defined as the relation between mass and volume.
For correcting volumes and density, in addition to the SAP Standard quantity
conversion, there is an oil quantity conversion. It allows volumes at ambient
temperature and densities at test temperature to be converted into densities,
volumes and masses at standard temperature. The oil quantity conversion is thus
used to convert the quantity of an oil product into various units of measure.

134 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

From a technical point of view, the oil quantity conversion uses external c-code
programs, which are accessed through an interface within the Quantity Conversion
Interface (QCI). The c-code programs are licensed to SAP customers by The
American Petroleum Institute (API).

Figure 49: Hydrocarbon Product Management

Prerequisites in general settings:
Definition of Units of Measure and Dimensions
The following units of measure are used for the oil quantity conversion:
ï Mass units of measure
ï Volume units of measure
ï Density units of measure
ï You can define the volume units of measurement for a specific temperature.
The L15 unit of measure is defined as ìliters at a temperature of 15 Celsiusî.
Density units of measure can be defined for a specific temperature. The following
density types are allowed for liquids:
ï API gravity (no dimension)
ï Relative density (no dimension)
ï Absolute density (SI unit: kg/m)

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 135



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

If no density unit is specified, the system automatically uses the kg/m SI unit.
Density units of measure for API gravity and relative density are not necessary,
because those units are dimensionless as relations of density units. However,
dimensionless units of measure can be defined and used for documentation
purposes.
For liquid quantity calculation, pressure parameters can be sent to the Quantity
Conversion Interface. Those parameters can be used in customer-specific
functions.

Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI)
Prerequisites in Material Master:
Base unit of measure
You define a base unit of measure (stockkeeping unit) for the material in the
material master record. That is the unit of measure for the stock quantity (base
quantity) in the system. Because that base quantity also determines the valuation
of the material, it is very important to choose a standardized unit of measure as the
base unit of measure.
In addition, you can also save a relation between two units of measure in the
system as conversion factors. The conversion factors are used for all planning
calculations for a material, as long as the real quantities from goods movements
are not known. The unit of measure relation for each material is a sub-definition
of the unit of measurement definition. The unit of measurement definition is valid
globally for all the materials.
Unit of measure group
The unit of measure group is a group of units of measure that is assigned to a
material at plant level and that enables inventory management in multiple units of
measure for the material.
You can define unit of measure groups and their entries (units of measure) in
Customizing If stock has already posted for the material, it is not possible to
change the unit of measure group in the material master.

136 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

Figure 50: Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI)

Assigning a Conversion Group
The Quantity Conversion Interface is activated for a material when a conversion
group is assigned to a material in the material master. The conversion group
also defines which specific external functions are used to calculate the material
quantities and base parameters (base density, base calorific value). The conversion
group contains a connection to external routines that are required for Oil and
Gas quantity conversion.
The conversion group is defined at plant level. In that way, the material is
classified for all plants as an HPM material, which means the conversion group
has to be maintained for all plants for the material. If stock has already been
posted for the material, it is not possible to change the conversion group in the
material master record.

Ticket Processing
IS-OIL-TSW: Ticket Purpose

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 137



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

The ticket purpose is a type of ticket. TSW offers 5 different ticket purposes:
1. Field ticket: This is the standard TSW ticket that shows the actualized

quantity.
2. Correction ticket: This ticket contains the new quantity that needs to replace

the old quantity; see the scenario descriptions for more details.
3. Final confirmation: This ticket contains the remaining quantity that is

delivered; this ticket is the final step to closing the nomination.
4. Internally-generated for posting: When set, the 'Internally Generated'

indicator shows that the ticket was not sent into the system by an IDoc or
based on a physical existing document; for example, book transfers.

5. Reversal Ticket: When you reverse a ticket, you do not change any
data. Instead, you are returning the ticket back to the status it had before
actualization. Depending on the movement scenario and the previously
posted documents, the system performs the following activities during
actualization of a reversed ticket:
Cancel inventory postings (goods issue, goods receipt, transfer posting)
Delete delivery note from the shipment
Delete items from the outbound delivery
Delete items from the purchase call-off

Figure 51: Ticket Processing

138 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

Ticket Deletion
This function enables you to delete actualized tickets after you have saved them.
Prerequisites
You have created and saved a ticket.
You have not actualized the ticket.
Features
When you delete the ticket, the system marks the ticket as parked. When the
ticket has this status, you can no longer actualize it and therefore not trigger any
subsequent documents. If you want to continue to use the parked ticket, you can
recover it.
You cannot delete tickets that have been actualized, because the actualization
process generates SAP subsequent documents and it is not possible to delete
tickets for which a document flow exists.
Ticket Recovering
Prerequisite
You created a nomination and the system generated a ticket.
You deleted a ticket.
Features
The recovered tickets can be processed just as other tickets in TSW.
If you mistakenly recovered a ticket, you can delete the ticket again.

Crude Import Terminal
Crude Import Terminal in MM represented by conception of Stock Transfer from
Plant to Plant
A stock transfer from plant to plant generally takes place within a company code.
It can, however, also take place between two company codes, if the plants are
assigned to different valuation areas, which belong to different company codes.
Unlike a stock transfer from storage location to storage location, a stock transfer
from plant to plant affects both Materials Planning and Financial Accounting, as
follows:
Materials Planning
Materials Planning is affected because a change of plant stock is taken into
account by Materials Planning.
Financial accounting

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 139



Unit 3: International Export/Import Operations IOG100

Accounting is affected if both plants are assigned to different valuation areas. This
means that a stock transfer leads not only to a quantity update but also to a value
update (stock value, G/L accounts). Thus, parallel to the material document for
stock transfer, an accounting document is created.
You can enter this stock transfer using either the one-step procedure or the two-step
procedure, whereby only the one-step procedure can be planned with a reservation.

Figure 52: Crude Import Terminal in MM

Crude Import Terminal in TSW represented by conception of Transfer Scenarios.
TSW movement scenarios determine the Document Processing that the system
carries out for scheduled bulk shipments. In addition to other factors, Document
Processing determines whether sales orders, purchase orders, stock transfer orders,
or other documents form the basis for a shipment. Document Processing also
determines how a nomination is processed, how subsequent documents are posted,
and the effect a ticket reversal has on the underlying documents.

IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Operational Inventory Management

Figure 53: Crude Import Terminal in TSW

Save the nomination and make a note of its number:
a) Create a nomination to schedule the purchase for that sales contract

from your location (Sidi Kerir) by entering the following data:

Unit 4
Bulk Supply Chain Management

(Inbound Distribution)

Unit Overview
VOIL Germany (Virtual Oil Company) buys most raw materials from the groups
trading company VOIL Int Trading, i.e. they are not active in the markets. The
receiving terminal is Triest. The terminal Triest is feeding a crude pipeline
to Austria and Germany with multiple receiving refineries, i.e. Triest and the
pipeline is a joined venture of all connected shippers run by an independent
entity (3rd party operator). For VOIL Germany the receiving installation is the
refinery at Ingolstadt.
Based upon the refinery run plans each shipper sets up a batch program to call
off the raw materials from stock in Triest. The carrier (joined venture pipeline
and terminal operator) works all shipper requests into an overall batch program
considering the required grades, volumes and arrival ranges in the refineries.
Once the batches arrive in the refineries, they are again stored in the refinery
tank farm before the finally are pumped to the atmospheric distillation units for
conversion into intermediate products.

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Use the functions in the system to carry out various business processes and
describe the subcomponents of these processes

ï Explain TSW master data
ï Schedule and execute movements using Nominations, Tickets, Stock

Projection Worksheet (SPW) and Location Balancing.
ï Describe the various system capabilities, such as pipeline shipments

Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution ... . . . . . . . . .162

Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement
Execution
Lesson Overview
Planning, scheduling, and executing the distribution of crude oil and refined
products plays a major role in your company for inbound movements (purchasing),
outbound movements (sales and delivery), and internal transfers (stock
replenishments). You use pipeline means of transport.
You schedule and execute shipments using TSW functions to manage and track
the various goods movements.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Use the functions in the system to carry out various business processes and

describe the subcomponents of these processes
ï Explain TSW master data
ï Schedule and execute movements using Nominations, Tickets, Stock

Projection Worksheet (SPW) and Location Balancing.
ï Describe the various system capabilities, such as pipeline shipments

Business Example
Planning, scheduling, and executing the distribution of crude oil and refined
products plays a major role in your company for inbound movements (purchasing),
outbound movements (sales and delivery), and internal transfers (stock
replenishments). You use pipeline means of transport.
You schedule and execute shipments using TSW functions to manage and track
the various goods movements.
VOil Germany stores crude discharged for the refinery in a joined venture terminal
in Triest. From there the crude is pumped in batches to the refinery Ingolstadt
through a pipeline. The batch size is determined by the receiving tank in the
refinery. The volume received in the refinery is measured by meter and sometimes
by tank dips. The volume difference dispatched at Triest versus received in
Ingolstadt is kept as in transit stock in the pipeline and cleared regularly by the
operator. Pipeline gain/loss is shared between all shippers.
Terminal and Pipeline are operated by 3rd party company TAL.
The crude pipeline in TSW is also a transport system with assigned locations
Triest (origin) and Refinery Ingolstadt (destination).

162 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Bulk Schedule Management
A scheduler in an oil company can optimize daily scheduling activities by using
the extended planning functions to schedule shipments of petroleum products.

Figure 54: Bulk Schedule Management

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 163



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

The planning and nomination processes enable the scheduler to schedule goods
movements and meet demand with a minimum of manual entries and the necessary
visual information to make correct decisions. The following sequence describes a
possible scheduling scenario:
ï You create long-term or spot contracts
ï You generate the SPW to populate the SPW with data (from nominations,

contracts, orders, and tickets).
ï You perform planning by generating replenishment proposals based on the

demand information from the SPW.
ï You generate the Worklist.
ï You create a nomination and assign contracts or orders to nomination line

items.
ï You send the nomination to different partners (such as carrier).
ï You confirm or reject nomination line items, based on information from

the partners.
ï You enter the ticket details based on the carrier ticket and physical goods

movements. You validate the ticket against the nomination line items.
ï The system automatically creates the underlying shipment documents and

postings against the nomination.

TSW Master Data Overview
TSW allows you to model the supply chain of an oil company, including pipeline
systems, marine routes, customers, vendors, and plants.

164 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Figure 55: TSW Master Data Overview

ï Transport systems are TSW master data objects that represent stock holding
objects to which you can assign locations. They represent pipelines or
marine routes as they exist in the real world.

ï Locations are nodes along a transport system. You define the business
purpose behind a location by assigning partners to them.

ï Using the partner role concept, you can assign certain functions to the
different TSW objects. A location is either a plant, a customer location, or a
vendor location in the real world.

ï You can also define planning locations, which represent a collection of a
number of real locations, for example a region. This aids scheduling at
earlier stages when schedules need to be generated but specific locations
or partners are not yet definite. Note that planning locations may overlap,
that is, a real location may be included in multiple planning locations, thus
providing optimum flexibility when creating planning views.

TSW Transport System
A transport system is a single, in-transit stock-holding object used for inventory
management purposes. Depending on individual requirements for modeling a
supply chain, the transport system can represent a fixed supply route, a supply
region, or a mode of transport. Examples of transport systems are a pipeline
system or a marine route.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 165



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

A transport system links locations and therefore it is recommended that you
assign two or more locations to a transport system. During scheduling, you assign
transport systems to nominations.

Figure 56: TSW Transport System

ï One of the functions of a transport system is to link the locations in the
supply chain. A transport system should always have two or more assigned
locations. During scheduling, you must assign a transport system to a
nomination. A location can either be an origin for the transport system
(supplies product into the transport system), or the location can be a
destination for the transport system (receives product from the transport
system). You can also define a location as both an origin and a destination.
As a result, the supply network is defined in terms of injection and discharge
points for each transport system.

ï TSW also provides a special type of transport system to model book
transfers. This transport system imposes different "rules" on the nomination
and subsequent document generation. For example, if you select the shipping
type book transfer for the transport system, the transport system does not
require an in-transit plant or in-transit storage location. Because there are no
physical goods movements for book transfers, the nomination shows that
there was a purchase of material, the sale of the same material with the same
quantity, both at the same location on the same scheduled date.

TSW Location
A location is a fixed point on the supply chain where goods are handled (such as
plants, warehouses, supply sources, and markets).

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 171



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Figure 62: TSW Location

ï A TSW location represents a point on the supply chain model where loading
or discharge events take place and where business partners or stock holding
objects exist.

ï Locations are defined in master data records and are assigned to transport
systems as an origin, destination, or both. One location may be assigned
to many transport systems.

172 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

TSW Location: Details Screen

Figure 63: TSW Location: Details Screen

Assignment of Materials to Locations
You can assign materials to locations in the location master data record. Each
material assigned to a location can be processed with SPW, when you generate
SPW for combination of material and location.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 173



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Figure 64: Assignment of Materials to Locations

ï To assign materials to a location, you must first create a partner role that is
defined as a plant or storage location, and assign a location to this partner
role. The material that you assign to the location must be one that has already
been assigned to the plant or storage location.

ï In the location master data record you maintain all details about the material
that are relevant to the SPW and planning engine. These details includes:
units, cycle duration, and calendars. The supply source data determines the
position of the location in the supply chain.

174 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

TSW Master Data: Partner Role

Figure 65: TSW Master Data: Partner Role

ï You define TSW partner roles in the master data record used to define
business partners. The partner role includes information about the activities
that the business partner can perform and where the business partner
performs these activities. You can also define stockholding objects, such as
plants and storage locations as partner roles.

ï You define partner roles based on existing SAP System master data records,
such as a vendor, customer, or plant. Because the partner role defines the
activities that a business partner performs in the TSW supply chain, you
must assign transport systems or locations to the master data record of each
partner role.

Bulk Pipeline Scheduling
To fulfil requirements of Ingolstadt Refinery, a batch of crude oil must be shipped
from the Terminal on Tries along the Pipeline operated by 3rd party company

Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Figure 68: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling

Nominations

ï The Nomination is the central planning application in TSW to schedule,
group and communicate bulk movements and transportation within a Supply
Network. You use nominations to:
ñ Capture movement schedules based on demand and supply data, such

as from sales, purchase, or transfer documents
ñ Navigate to and validate against master data, such as the transport

systems, locations, partners, or vehicles
ñ Handle status (confirmation process)
ñ Navigate to the TSW Worklist and update the SPW
ñ Automatically generate subsequent documents, such as deliveries, bulk

shipments, goods movements, or billing documents
ñ Show document flow
ñ Integrate with SAP inventory management

Pipeline Scenario: Stock transfer

Figure 73: Pipeline Scenario: Stock transfer

ï The first line item of the nomination reflects a movement from the origin
location Triest (Terminal) into the pipeline.

ï The second line item represents a movement out of the pipeline into
destination location Ingolstadt.

ï The first movement increases the in-transit stock. The posting of a ticket
with the actual delivered quantity results stock transfer movement out of
pipeline into refinery tank, which decreases the in-transit stock and increases
stock in the refinery.

ï In this scenario, the system generates the following SAP system documents
when the ticket is actualized:

ï Loading:
ñ Reservation, TD Bulk Shipment, Load Confirmation

ï Discharge:
ñ Reservation, TD Bulk Shipment, Shipment Delivery Confirmation

ï You can reference sales or purchase documents in nominations.

automatic).

which triggers the document generation process.
ï In conjunction with the TSW trading interface, these movement scenarios

simplify the deal scheduling processes.

Pipeline Batch Handling

Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Bulk Operational Inventory Management

ï The Stock Projection Worksheet calculates and shows the inventory forecast
for a date or time period and for combinations of material, location, transport
system, batch, and valuation type. You can use the What-If functions of the
Stock Projection Worksheet to simulate different effects on the inventory.
ñ The SPW calculates the projected inventory
ñ Real-time SPW update based on nominations, orders, and TSW tickets
ñ SPW calculation takes into account

ï Starting book inventory from SAP inventory management
ï Optional use of alternative inventory figures, such as physical count
ï Scheduled items from nominations
ï SAP system documents relevant for scheduling, such as sales orders
ï Demand forecasts for rack movements using Logistics Information
System (LIS) structure
ï Uses production versions to handle seasonal grade changeovers
ï Actual postings made in the SAP system that are relevant to TSW
ï Production plan figures using LIS structure

ñ Interactive SPW with details of movements
ñ Navigation to nomination and TSW Worklist

ï The Real-Time SPW function updates the SPW based on nominations,
orders and TSW tickets.

ï You set up LIS structures to stage the data into the SPW, which also has its
own data table to store manually entered figures.

ï The SPW uses a calculation logic that ensures that the calculations are made
correctly. For example, sales orders attached to nomination line items are
consumed by the line item and not double counted.

ï In general, the more firm the data, the more likely it will override a related
figure on the SPW. That is, actual quantities take precedence over scheduled
quantities, and scheduled quantities take precedence over document
quantities.

ï Planning proposals add to whatever figure is used for the day on which the
planning proposal occurs.

ï In the SPW, you can navigate to detailed information behind certain figures.
For example, you can click on the word multiple in the batch column to
expand the line to show all the batches scheduled on a specific day.

186 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Pipeline Scenario: Stock Projection Worksheet
The SPW is the central tool for daily scheduling activities.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 187



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Figure 77: Pipeline Scenario: Stock Projection Worksheet

ï The SPW provides a projection of the inventory (physical or book) over
a specified period of time for a given location-material combination on a
definable breakdown (daily, weekly, monthly).

ï You can generate stock projection data to be as detailed as the tank-level
(integration with IS-OIL: Tank/Silo-management).

ï Real time update of SPW.
ï Status concept: You can define the influence of product movements on the

inventory.
ï You can configure the system to display TSW-relevant documents, such

as orders and contracts, already scheduled volumes and their status
(nominations), production figures, real and forecasted throughput, ticketed
volumes, and corrected volumes.

ï Through the integration of TSW with SAP Advanced Planner and Optimizer
(SAP APO), you can set up the system to transfer APO demand planning
data to TSW.

ï The SPW allows an interactive simulation of movements (what-if scenarios)
and the creation of nominations based on those simulations.

ï Flexible layout concept: You can define additional columns and tabs.
ï You can enhance the calculation logic of the SPW using Business Add-Ins

(BAdIs) provided in TSW Customizing.

188 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Pipeline Scenario: SPW Calculation Logic
The calculation logic that the system uses to generate the SPW is very complex.
You can enhance the calculation logic with customer-specific routines using
BAdIs available in TSW Customizing.

Figure 78: Pipeline Scenario: SPW Calculation Logic

ï The following example demonstrates the standard SPW logic for calculating
the inventory for the current day:
ñ Day-end inventory of current day = Starting inventory + open receipts

schedules for the past ñ open issues scheduled for the future + receipts
for current day ñ issues for current day.

ï Explanations:
ñ Day-end-logic compared with Starting-day logic:

ï End-day: Current day movements determine current day inventory.
ï Startng-day: Current day movements determine next day inventory.

ñ Receipts: Production + SAP system documents + scheduled receipts
(nominations)

ñ Issues: Rack Issues + SAP system documents + scheduled receipts
(nominations)

ñ Rack Issues: Forecasted or actual rack-issues or corrected rack-issues.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 189



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Pipeline Scenario: SPW User Interaction and Layout

Figure 79: Pipeline Scenario: SPW User Interaction and Layout

ï Selection area provided to specify the location, transport system, material,
batch and tank in the SPW

ï Various tabs available, such as stock projection, attributes, physical
inventory, and tank data.

ï You can Customize and enhance the tabstrip.
ï You can access the reference documents directly from the SPW.
ï You can display the figures using a flexible graphics tool.
ï You can download the data to spreadsheets.
ï You can perform what-if simulation to plan for additional movements.
ï Flexible column layout (show, hide, and swap columns).
ï Integrated list functions (sorting and summing up).
ï Rack issues (current data or what-if forecasts) are filled by a user exit.

190 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Pipeline Scenario: Direct Access from SPW

Figure 80: Pipeline Scenario: Direct Access from SPW

ï The integration of the SPW with other components of TSW and the SAP
System allows direct access to:
ñ Nomination
ñ Worklist and worklist update
ñ SAP system documents
ñ Tickets
ñ Master data constraints, such as location data and tank data on the

SPW tabs
ñ You can define additional tabs to store additional information

Pipeline Scenario: Simulations in SPW: What-if
Using the simulation capabilities of the SPW you can create and save different
simulations in a clipboard.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 191



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Figure 81: Pipeline Scenario: Simulations in SPW: What-if

ï You can publish the simulations, whereby the system creates ìrealî
nominations. You can also use the simulations to change existing
nominations, such as the volume.

ï You use the What-If Pop-up to create simulations, which the system applies
to the What-If column of the SPW.

ï You use the What-If Clipboard to collect the simulations you create using
the What-If Pop-up. The What-If Clipboard collects the simulations across
different SPWs, such as SPWs for different locations.

ï The What-If Clipboard is user specific. When you publish the simulated
schedules to nominations, the data becomes available for all users of the
SPW.

ï The What-If Clipboard has full Advanced List View (ALV) capabilities and
is therefore adaptable to user requirements.

192 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Pipeline Scenario: Balancing Locations in the SPW

Figure 82: Pipeline Scenario: Balancing Locations in the SPW

ï The basic concept for stock balancing in SPW is intended to support a
variety of requirements, such as:

ï Overall balancing of product receipts and product issues in terms of projected
stock figures.

ï Consumption of purchase or sale quantities by outbound or inbound
scheduled quantities.

ï If the balancing function is activated (configurable), the system creates a
balance line in the SPW in the following cases:

ï When a sale or purchase takes place at a location, but only influences the
in-transit inventory and not the location inventory (customer or vendor
locations)

ï Sales out of pipe and out of own batch
ï Purchase into pipe and into own batch

Pipeline Scenario: Location Balancing
Location Balancing is a transaction in TSW to handle the balancing of demands
and supplies at locations within the location hierarchy over a period of time

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 193



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Figure 83: Pipeline Scenario: Location Balancing

ï Location Balancing was initially conceived for crude pipeline operations, but
is applicable to other types of periodic balancing, such as gas systems

ï You can configure the SAP system to take the following documents into
account for the demand and supply calculation:
ñ Nominations
ñ Sales (purchase) contracts and sales (purchase) orders
ñ Inventory adjustment requirements
ñ Plant-to-plant transfers

ï The location balancing screen provides an overview of the supplies and
demands, as well as a summary in the header area.

ï Inventory adjustment:
ñ You can reconcile imbalances by creating Inventory Adjustment

Requisitions (IAR), either manually or using automatic routines
ñ You can set up the system to automatically generate transfers in or

out of the inventory (can also generate manually). You can manually
change existing schedules to balance the inventory.

194 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Pipeline Business: Location Balancing Interaction

Figure 84: Pipeline Business: Location Balancing Interaction

ï Location balancing allows manual opening inventory adjustments and route
assignments

ï You can make adjustments to single demand and supply items or for groups
of supplies and demands

ï You can set up automatic inventory adjustments (transfer all rule) to maintain
location balances.

ï The location balancing screen allows for flexible querying and navigation
ï Manual entry of inventory adjustment requisitions
ï From the location balancing screen, you can view contract details, including

the contract schedule.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 195



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Bulk Movement Execution

ï A ticket is an official notice sent by a partner, containing information about a
product movement.
ñ In the ticket generation process, data is entered in the system either

manually or through an automatic interface:
ï Meter or gauge readings (opening, closing, or actual quantities)
ï Quantities or inspection reports provided by external systems or
partners

ñ The system stores the data in a load ticket table and uses the data during
the actualization process

ñ Actualization
ï The system creates the required transfer documents, such as call-offs,
delivery notes, and invoices with actual figures
ï The system updates the book inventory

ñ Reversal and Correction
ï Tickets can be cancelled and corrected including the subsequent
postings in one go.

Functions in Ticketing

Figure 85: Functions in Ticketing

196 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Pipeline Scheduling and Movement Execution

Ticket Reversal

Figure 86: Ticket Reversal

Figure 87: Ticket Reversal Screen

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 197



Unit 4: Bulk Supply Chain Management (Inbound Distribution) IOG100

Ticket Corrections

ï Correcting a ticket creates a new version of the original ticket containing the
changed data. When correcting a ticket you can:
ñ Correct the quantity after the ticket has been actualized
ñ Correct the loading date and time
ñ Correct the ticket posting data
ñ Delete purchase call-offs if the ticket quantity is zero
ñ Delete sales call-offs if the ticket quantity is zero
ñ Delete outbound delivery items

Exercise Objectives
After completing this exercise, you will be able to:
ï Create the necessary master data to schedule supply chain activities and

assign materials to the transport system and locations
ï Create nominations and tickets to transport crude oil from port Triest to

the Ingolstadt refinery.

to schedule and execute bulk movements
ï Display and explain the document flow

Business Example
You enable schedulers for pipeline movements of crude to schedule the movements
from the port location Triest to Ingolstadt. To check your system configuration,
you simulate a transportation process through this supply chain and verify the
inventory situation on the Stock Projection Worksheet. You create nominations to
fulfill all the requirements of this business scenario. You process incoming tickets
manually, check the updated inventory and the document flow.

Unit 5
Refinery: Silo Management, Refining,

Internal Movements

Unit Overview
Silo Management
The unit describes silo management, refining, internal movements. The scenario
goes trough Hydrocarbon Inventory Management (HPM) to Refinery processing
and Reporting of internal movements. There are no special scripts for instructorís
demo, use the exercises for every lesson for demonstration purposes. There are
business documents already created in the master system to help the instructor
with demonstration of document flows. The document numbers are mentioned in
comments for relevant lessons.

Hydrocarbon Product Management
Tank Management
Inventory Valuation

Refinery Processing
Crude and Feedstock to Raw Material Blend
Raw Material Blend to Intermediate (semi-finished) products
Semi-finished Products Blending; Transfer to Distribution Plant

Reporting
Production, Input / Output balance for Units, Loss
Production / Consumption Intermediates
Blending
Transfer to Distribution Plant

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Explain the differences between static and dynamic quantity conversions
ï List product types that can be handled by the Quantity Conversion Interface

(QCI)

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 219



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

ï Demonstrate movements inside the refinery
ï Explain the reasons for differences between physical inventory and book

inventory
ï Demonstrate how to record physical inventory in the ERP system
ï Demonstrate how to analyze differences between physical and book

inventory and how to record gain or loss postings
ï Understand the processing at the refinery
ï Execute material movements to post the manufacturing process in the system
ï Execute material transfers to post output from production site to product

storage area
ï Understand reports for internal movements at the refinery on stages

ï Execute and explain report ñ transfer movements to Distribution Plant
