IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain the processes of goods movements in a refinery, since the
handle of quantity conversion of the crude oil through the transfer of the finished
good to the distribution plant. The lesson focuses on Hydrocarbon Inventory
Management (quantity conversion interface and silos management) and inventory
movements.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain the differences between static and dynamic quantity conversions
ï List product types that can be handled by the Quantity Conversion Interface

(QCI)
ï Demonstrate movements inside the refinery
ï Explain the reasons for differences between physical inventory and book

inventory
ï Demonstrate how to record physical inventory in the ERP system
ï Demonstrate how to analyze differences between physical and book

inventory and how to record gain or loss postings

Business Example
Master data in International Oil Company and German Oil Company (VOIL
DE) have to be created according to the companyís business, which means that
materials, customers and vendors must have the Oil specific data view in Master
records provided by the solution SAP for Oil&Gas.

Silo Management and Hydrocarbon Product
Management
Oil companies deal with materials whose quantities are not the same at every place
or every time. A gasoline can be transferred from a hot city to a colder place.
When the gasoline arrives to destination, the material seems to be in a smaller
quantity. In order to overcome this misunderstanding oil industries control their
inventories in a common unit of measure considering the same temperature. Some
countries make use of M15 (m3 at 15C) or L15 (liters at 15C) while others use
M20 (m3 at 20C). There are other units of measure for oil products, but all of
them consider temperature as a pattern. According to the product, other factors
can be considered, such as pressure, vapor pressure, calorific value and density.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 221



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

The bulk oil products and gases are stored in tanks. SAP for Oil&Gas provides the
solution ìSilo Managementî to allow tank dips and comparison between physical
inventory (what is in the silo) and book inventory.

Figure 89: Petroleum Measurement Standards

VOIL Germany processes the purchase and sale of crude oil, gasoline, jet fuel,
lubricants, liquid petroleum gas and natural gas. The inventories must be managed
in different units of measure. At the time of delivery and goods receipt the user has
to enter quantity conversion parameters in the ERP system. All the movements for
bulk products in liquid form contain more than one unit of measure, considering
characteristics such as volume, mass, temperature and density. Other factors can
be considered depending on the product, like energy, heating value and pressure.

222 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

Figure 90: Quantity conversion interface

Liquid oil products and gases are stored in a basic unit of measure, but they use
other units of measure to calculate the real volume stored or moved according to
external factors that impact this volume.
Solid products can have different units of measure for inventory, sales or
purchase, but the conversion between these units is based on a single arithmetical
calculation. The conversions between units of measures informed in the material
master are under the tab ìAdditional dataî.

Example: Base unit of measure : TO
Sales unit : KG
Purchase unit : L
Conversions : 1 TO = 1000 KG

1 KG = 1 L
1 TO = 1000 L

This kind of conversion is called static conversion, which means that the
temperature and other conversion parameters are fixed. The static conversion is
used for contracts, sales orders and purchase orders, i.e., when there is no goods
movements.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 223



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Oil products in liquid form and gases need to have their quantities calculated upon
a formula basis. This is call dynamic conversion. It allows volumes at ambient
temperature and densities at test temperature to be converted into densities,
volumes and masses at standard temperature. The oil quantity conversion is thus
used to convert the quantity of an oil product into various units of measure. The
dynamic conversion is used in documents where there is a goods movement and it
is reflected in the billing and invoice documents. Although the dynamic conversion
is performed during goods movements, it is necessary to inform a standard
conversion (like a static conversion) at Additional Data tab in Material Master.
From a technical point of view, the oil quantity conversion uses external c-code
programs, which are accessed through an interface within the Quantity Conversion
Interface (QCI). The c-code programs are usually licensed to SAP customers by
The American Petroleum Institute (API). The programs are called through fields
informed in view ìOil-specific dataî at Plant level in Material Master. These
fields are UoM Group (unit of measure group) and Conv. Group (conversion
group). The conversion group is linked to a reading group in Customizing that
calls the routine for conversion while the unit of measure group indicates in which
units of measure the movements will be stored in the system. The type of product
is identified by the conversion group, which also controls the tolerances for
differences between manual entries and values calculated by the system. Once
you fill in the Oil view to a material in a plant it becomes valid to all plants. If
the material is not linked to an UoM group and to a conversion group no dynamic
conversion is calculated.
Product types that require dynamic conversion:
ï Crude oil
ï Oil products
ï Chemicals
ï Lubricants
ï Asphalt / bitumen
ï Natural gas
ï Liquefied natural gas
ï Liquid petroleum gas
ï Water
ï Generalized gases
ï Industrial aromatic hydrocarbons
ï Raw materials
The Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI) converts volumes, masses and energy at
ambient conditions (temperature, pressure, vapor pressure, calorific value, density)
into volumes, masses and energy values at standard conditions. In addition, the
QCI calculates density and heating value at standard conditions. Example: a

224 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

company sells 15000 L of gasoline. The quantity must be converted to a quantity
in 15C if the base unit is L15 (liters at 15C), as the ambient temperature can
be different from origin to destination.
The QCI can convert quantities based on international standards for
ï Crude Oil & Petroleum Products (ISO, API, ASTM)
ï NGL /LPG (ISO, GPA, DIN)
ï Natural gas (ISO, AGA)
If the quantities of a material are always measured in mass (mass to mass
conversion), no dynamic conversion is required. However, Oil and Gas industries
usually measure their products in volume. Because the volume of an oil product
is dependent on the temperature of the product, a volume correction is needed to
calculate a standardized volume (example: 980 L of material at -15  C equals
1030 L at 60  C or 1000 Gal of material at 0F equals 1025 Gal at 70F). For gases,
the pressure under which the gas is kept plays a decisive role in the gas quantity
conversion. As a result, the volume of a gas is dependent on the temperature and
the pressure under which a specific quantity of gas is held.
Summary of Oil-specific data in Material Master
Base unit of measure: it is the unit of measure used to manage stocks. All other
units used for a material are converted to the base unit of measure.
UoM group: the unit of measure group allows inventory management in multiple
units of measure for a material. Quantities in all of the units of measure assigned
to the group are calculated during transactions, and the results are posted to
appendix tables in the Material Hierarchy Tables. Once stock is posted to the
material, the UoM group cannot then be changed.
Conv. Group: the conversion group defines the conversion routines that will be
used in the oil quantity conversion calculations.
Air Buoy. Fact: the air buoyancy factor serves to correct the calculated standard
density by balancing out the difference between the density in a vacuum and at
normal air pressure. This value is subtracted from the standard density before this
density is multiplied by the volume to calculate the mass.
Fix. Gravity: the fixed density has to be entered in the material master for
materials that are stored in the conversion group as chemical products (product
type). The fixed density is used in the IS-OIL quantity conversion, when
conversions are carried out between mass and volume units.
Conv. Coeff: the quantity conversion coefficient is used for oil materials with
'chemical' as the product type (defined in the conversion group). A fixed density is
assigned to the material and this, along with the coefficient of thermal expansion,
is used in the oil quantity conversion calculations to correct the volume to standard
temperature.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 225



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Excise duty group: the excise duty tax group to which a material belongs is a
user- defineable value. It allows materials to be treated in the same way for excise
duty purposes. The tax group to which a material belongs partially determines
the excise duty rate which applies for a movement of the material. However, it is
not applicable to all countries.
Oil content %: the oil content of the material determines what percentage of the
material moved is liable to excise duty.
Cust. Tariff nr: here you can enter a material-related customs tariff number. This
number can be used for reporting purposes.
Transfer sign: you can activate a material for two-step plant-to-plant transfer
tracking with the transfer sign. The following settings are possible:

' ' ñ no tracking available
1 ñ only statistical tracking
2 ñ tracking with gain/loss postings

It is not suitable for all countries.
Material tax group: it defines product type and tax convention applicability of a
material or group of materials only for Brazil.

Figure 91: Purchase and Sales with QCI

Oil and gas products are controlled in different units of measure that are informed
in the unit of measure group in material master. Besides the units defined in the
unit of measure group, different units of measure can be used in purchase orders
and sales orders. Thus, a crude oil can be measured in M15, L15, TO and KG but

226 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

VOIL International buys it in BB6 (barrels in 60F). The same process can happen
in the sales side, which means, the product with the same unit of measure group
can be sold in L. The oil and gas dynamic quantity conversion takes place during
goods movement. For contracts, purchase orders and sales orders the conversion
is only static.
On the purchase side, the static conversion is performed for contracts and purchase
orders. During goods receipt, the system looks for different units of measure from
those in the unit of measure group. If a different unit of measure is found, the
material document is posted with all units of measure, that is, all units from the
unit of measure group plus the one in the contract and / or purchase order. The
invoice receipt considers the value in the unit of measure informed in the purchase
order with the dynamic quantity conversion.
The same process is performed by the system in the sales cycle. In contracts and
sales order only the static conversion is performed. During the delivery process,
the dynamic oil and gas quantity conversion takes place. The system also looks for
different units of measure in the sales documents besides the ones from the unit of
measure group. The material document will be posted with all units of measure,
that is, the one from the unit of measure group plus the one from de sales order.
The billing document will be created with the unit of measure from the sales order
but with the quantity according to the dynamic oil and gas conversion.
Usually refineries do not purchase crude oil because the crude oil terminals are
responsible for this activity. In some countries refineries do not sell products
because they are all transferred to distribution terminal, while other countries
do not allow a refinery to operate a distribution terminal, so the refinery sells
the product to a distribution company.

Figure 92: Default Data

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 227



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

All oil and gas movements require the filling of parameters to convert the
quantities, such as temperature and density. In order to avoid errors during manual
input by the users, the system provides an automatic filling of those parameters.
Default data can be informed in the system considering plant, storage location,
material, date and time. The values informed in the default data will be used
during goods movements according to the date and time validity. The company
can define how often it will update the default data for certain materials. Example:
default data for crude oil can be updated every 2 hours while lubes are updated
only once a day.

Figure 93: Tank Management

Bulk liquid oil products are stored in tanks. Solid materials, like coke, are not
stored in silos or tanks. Silo Management or Tank Management is the R/3 solution
to allow a company to record physical material stocks in tanks or silos hourly,
daily or weekly. The tanks are created in the system with their calibration history.
Materials are assigned to tanks and tank dips are recorded. The physical stock
readings can be compared to the book inventories or goods movements in order
to post gains and losses periodically.

228 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

Figure 94: Physical X Book Inventory

Physical inventory is the one stored in tanks or silos. Book inventory is the posted
inventory in transactions of goods receipts and goods issues. Periodically both
inventories must be compared. Missing entries can cause differences between
physical and book inventory. When a difference is not identified, an accounting
posting is done in order to adjust the quantities.

Figure 95: Tank Characteristics

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 229



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

The tank characteristics are defined as storage object characteristics. All they are
required for tank management. The storage object type should reflect the technical
aspects (size, floating or fix roof, etc), not the service, because the service may
be switched.
General tank data are:
ï Capacity of a tank (maximum capacity)
ï Allowable impurity quantity
ï Allowed mass
ï Throughput quantities
ï Calibration history
Data for volume calculation are correction factors that affect the tank volume
calculation:
ï Floating roof correction
ï Water correction
ï K- factor calculation: correction for the thermal expansion of the tank (with

or without taking into account the thermal insulation of the tank material)
ï Innage / Ullage procedures: innage is the volume of liquid in a tank while

ullage is the capacity of the tank not occupied by a liquid.
Calibration relevant data can be:
ï Calibration data that only has an informational character (for example, name

of the person that carried out the calibration)
ï Correction-relevant calibration data
Tank strapping table represents the basis for the volume calculation including
minimum and maximum dips. Based on the depth of a product in a tank, the
conversion tables can be used to determine the corresponding volume quantity.

230 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

Figure 96: Assignment of Materials to Tanks

A tank is related to a storage location. It is possible to create:
ï One tank per one storage location
ï Two or more tanks per one storage location
ï One tank per one storage location, but different materials or materials with

different valuation types or batches or special stocks.
VOIL Germany set up each tank as a storage location under the refinery plant.
Materials are assigned to tanks in the master data for tanks. Depending on
configuration settings, one or more materials can be assigned to a tank. Multiple
materials can be in the same tank only if they have the same:
ï Base unit of measure
ï Unit of measure group
ï Conversion group
Chemicals materials need two more checks:
ï Fixed density
ï Thermal expansion coefficient

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 231



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

You can make the assignment based on the material number, batch, valuation type,
stock type and special stock, and limited to a specific time. As part of that process,
you can only assign a specific material segment per storage location to a tank once
at the same time. You can define a planned capacity for every material allocation.
If a tank is already in use and you want to assign another material to this tank, the
stock must be zero to the material segment in all units of measure (base unit of
measure plus all units from the unit of measure group for the material). Besides,
the date and time of the assignment must be after the last goods movement entered
in the system for the newly-assigned material segment.
If a material will be pumped out of the tank and it will be substituted for another
material, the old material has to have zero stock in all units of measure (base unit
of measure plus all units from the unit of measure group for the material). You
must also set the end date for the assignment of the material to the tank.

Figure 97: Measurements / Tank Dips

The main objective of silo management is volume calculation. Volumes are
usually to be calculated, either from meter readings (delta volume start versus end
reading) or from tank dip (opening dip / innage volume versus closing dip / innage
volume). Meter readings are not handled by Silos Management, but most refinery
process computers are handling this and provide the delta volume.
As refineries operate 24 hours per day and 7 days per week, the operator has to set
the time to track movements (usually at midnight or 6 a.m.). Usually a spreadsheet
is used to calculate the input and output balance for a 24 hours period.

232 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

A tank dip can be performed since that the tank strapping table is registered in
the system. Each dip is related to a tank volume. The following information is
required:
ï The dip height
ï Volume per height
ï Total volume for the dip height
The tank strapping table allows the knowledge of the minimum and maximum
dip, the tank capacity and the non-pumpable quantity according to configuration
settings.
Physical tank contents can be entered in the form of dip readings with information
on innage of product in a tank (or ullage, that is, the amount of empty space in
a tank), or enter the volume directly. Just remember that the direct input of the
volume is allowed for materials that do not require volume conversion. When
the height of material informed, the system uses the strapping table to calculate
the volume.
As more than one material can be assigned to a tank, the system looks for the first
material with default values in order to calculate the quantities in the alternative
units of measure. The height or volume refers to the whole tank, which can contain
various materials. The difference between the physical and the book inventory has
to be analyzed based on material sales volume or the number of goods movements
during the analysis period.
There are some prerequisites for entering tank dips at the time of the dip reading:
ï Calibration set activated
ï Materials assigned to the tank
The postings can be input by ecatts or they can also be automated with data feed
from process control, integration of Silo Management as volume calculator, and
a user front end for control, reconciliation and correction, and also for basic
operational reporting involving the use of BI to report and XI for data transmission
from refinery process control.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 233



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Figure 98: Reports

Analysis can be done through the following reports:
ï Display tank dips
ï Stock overview
ï Create tank analysis data
ï Tank gains and losses analysis or stock analysis based on goods movements
The tank dips report shows the following data for a tank and time period:
ï Total height of the tank dip
ï Material volume in the unit of measure of the tank strapping set
ï Material volume in the base unit of measure of the material segments

assigned to the tank
ï Book stock at the time of tank dip, considering the total of materials assigned

to the tank
ï Stock difference between physical and book inventories
The stock overview report shows the following data:
ï Cumulated book stock quantity in base unit of measure and in the volume

unit for the tank
ï Maximum tank capacity
ï Free tank capacity
The tank analysis data report allows an analysis of goods movements between
the individual dip readings. Depending on configuration settings analysis data can
be automatically updated. Run this report before analyse gains and losses.

234 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

The tank gains and losses analysis or stock analysis based on goods movements
report shows besides the tank dips:
ï Total movement dip difference: it is (the balance quantity of a material

in a tank between all previously analyzed tank dips) minus (the quantity
difference between the current and first analyzed tank dip) in base unit of
measure

ï Accumulated dip difference: it is the accumulated quantity difference
between tank dips in base unit of measure

ï Movement difference: it refers to the balance quantity of movements
between two successive tank dips

ï Accumulated movement difference: it is the accumulated balance quantity of
movements between successive tank dips or the balance of goods movements
between the current dip and the first analysed dip

ï Dip difference: it is the quantity difference between two successive tank
dips in base unit of measure

ï Movement dip difference: it is (the balance quantity of movements between
two successive tank dips) minus (quantity difference between two successive
tank dips in base unit of measure)

Double clicking a line it is possible to see the total of goods receipts and goods
issues for each material assigned to the tank. You can also drill down each material
to see all material documents created in that period.

Figure 99: Batches, Valuation Types and Special Stocks

Materials can be configured to work with batches. A batch can mean a real
batch number or a characteristic to identify the material. Example: a refinery or
a distribution plant can store materials for other companies. A specific material

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 235



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

from third parties can have the same material number, no matter if there are
many owners for the material. Each owner can be a batch to easily identify the
property of the material in reports, like material 01.000.001 batch Exxon; material
01.000.001 batch Shell.
The field ìbatchî is also used to inform a valuation type. Example: the same
material number can have two valuations, taxed and untaxed. The split valuation
is necessary to calculate taxes for oil products in some countries.
Materials can belong to special stocks, like consignment, sales order stock or stock
transfer. Thus, the system allows the display of own material which is stored in
third parties, reserved or in transit material.

Figure 100: TDP - Tariffs, Duties and Permits

Excise duties are handled in many different ways throughout the world. The
structure explained in this chapter applies to most countries. However, some
countries have so specific excise duties characteristics that SAP developed a
different solution for them.
TDP is an Oil functionality to allow the calculation and posting of excise duties
for dutiable goods. An excise duty is due when a goods movement takes place
based on the quantity of the material moved.

236 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

Excise duties can be determined in the following operations:
ï Sales
ï Purchase
ï Transfer between plants
ï Production orders
The inventory is revaluated after changes in excise duty rates. It is possible to
separate the inventory into taxed and untaxed materials through split valuation
in material master.
There are some reductions and exemptions in excise duties that must be considered
during the systems configuration.
Prerequisites to work with excise duties
Some fields must be filled in the material master in order to make possible the
calculation of excise duties:
ï Excise duty group: it is on the Oil-Specific Data view. It activates the excise

duty determination. The excise duty group defines the way a material will be
handled from a tax point of view. Some changes regarding the excise duty
group will affect all the materials assigned to that group.

ï Oil content %: it is on the Oil-Specific Data view. It indicates the percentage
of the material that will be subject to excise duty.

ï Split valuation: the material must have at least two valuation types, like
ìtaxedî and ìuntaxedî.

ï Excise duty status: it is on the Accounting 2 view. It indicates if the material
is taxed or untaxed and it is related to each combination ìdutiable material /
batchî within a plant

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 237



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Features of excise duties
ï Handling type: it is used to find the correct excise duty rate during goods

movements. In purchasing, the handling type determines the excise duty
status of the material at the point of origin (vendorís location) while in
sales and stock transfers it occurs at the destination (customerís location or
destination plant). The settings for the handling type are dependent on the
regulations of local authorities. Some examples of handling types: untaxed,
reduced tax for heating, fully taxed. The handling type is informed in the
vendor master, customer master, purchase info record and customer material
info record.

ï Excise duty inventory: the untaxed material is listed with only the inventory
value. The taxed material (when the tax has already been paid) is composed
of the inventory value plus taxes

ï Excise duty postings: a goods movement from an excise duty free storage
location to an excise duty paid storage location leads to tax liability, while
the opposite movement leads to a tax claim.

ï Determination of the excise duty rate: an excise duty rate can be external or
internal. An external excise duty rate is always used for goods issues. The
rates and units of measure on which the rates are based are determined by
local legal authorities. The internal excise duty rates are maintained with the
price condition rates in the system. There is pricing indicator to determine
whether the excise duty rate will be external or internal for an order item.
It is informed in the customer master, customer material info record and
purchase info record.

ï Quantity conversion: a quantity conversion can be carried out to calculate
taxes. For example, a material can be sold at ambient temperature, but the
taxes are calculated at a specific temperature (example: liters at 15C).
The conversion group and the unit of measure group must be filled in the
Oil-specific data view in material master.

Excise duty revaluation
Excise duty revaluation is based on physical inventory and can be carried out after
any new excise duty rate / unit of measure / base quantity. When a new excise
duty rate is implemented, the new values are stored in the valuation record. The
system updates the excise duty inventory after every material movement.
The untaxed material is listed with only the inventory value. The taxed material
(when the tax has already been paid) is composed of the inventory value plus taxes.
Inventory movements (material/ plant combination) are blocked during
revaluation.

238 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Hydrocarbon Inventory and Tank Management

Excise duty ñ Purchase
In the purchasing cycle, based on a default hierarchy, the system defaults excise
duty parameters in the purchase contract or purchase order and calculates the
excise duty based on those parameters. However, excise duty postings and
inventory postings take place at the time of the goods receipt.
For excise duty postings, it is critical to determine whether the material that is
being moved is excise duty paid or excise duty unpaid, and whether the receiving
plant/storage location has an ED-paid or an ED-unpaid status.
During goods movements (for a purchase), it is necessary to have two statuses for
excise duty calculation. The VOIL status is defined by the valuation type. The
trading partner's status is defined by the handling type. If both statuses are the
same, no excise duty posting will occur.

Excise duty ñ Sales
In the sales cycle, the system defaults the excise duty parameters, based on a
default hierarchy. The parameters are defaulted in the sales contract or in the
order. Using those parameters, the excise duty is calculated. However, excise duty
postings and inventory postings are made at the time of the goods issue.
For excise duty postings, it is decisive whether the material that is being moved is
excise duty paid or excise duty unpaid, and whether the receiving plant/storage
location has an ED paid or an ED unpaid status.
An example of sales scenario would be that a company delivers ED unpaid
material and the receiving plant/storage location is excise duty paid. That would
mean that an excise duty liability arises when a goods issue occurs. The company
pays excise duties to the local tax authority (a liability).
The company sends its customer the invoice for the gross price, meaning the
material price and the excise duty (claim).

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 239



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Figure 101: Nominations Processing with Meter / Dip Readings

Scheduling for the pipeline
The scheduling for the pipeline covers usually the transfer out of the Triest tank
into the pipeline and the transfer out of the pipeline into the refinery tank upon
arrival of the batch in the refinery. The same applies to transfers between the
refinery and the distribution plant: there is a transfer out of the tank in the refinery
into the pipeline and the transfer out of the pipeline into the tank in the distribution
plant.
A meter can be an additional parameter when a ticket arrives to SAP. The
measurements informed through the meter can make the system calculate the real
moved value, which means, the real volume into the ticket.
The measurement of a transfer between plants can also be done through tank dips.
Firstly the user creates the tank dips. While creating the ticket, the user calls
the tank dips during the gauge reading.

The ticket type PM3 - Physical Measurement - Gauge reading does not
actualize the documents, that means, it does not create a reservation,
a TD document and a material document. To do so, you will have to
create a carrier ticket. Another option is to configure a new ticket type
copying PM3 and select the actualization box. As configuration is not
covered by this course, just create a carrier ticket typing the quantities
calculated by the gauge reading ticket.

258 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Refinery processing

Lesson: Refinery processing
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain the refinery processes at the production site. It also covers
the modeling of refinery processes and manufacturing units within inventory
management (MM-IM). Next part of the lesson considers material movements in a
refinery, since the initial input of raw materials to production site until the transfer
of the finished products to the distribution plant.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Understand the processing at the refinery
ï Execute material movements to post the manufacturing process in the system
ï Execute material transfers to post output from production site to product

storage area

Business Example
As the raw material stock is at the refinery site the processing cycle is started. It is
necessary to post materials input and output by manufacturing units in the system.
After the refinery processing is accomplished the movement of finished products
from production site to product storage area to be posted in the system as well.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 259



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Refinery Processing

Figure 104: Refinery Processing

From the crude oil processing until the finished product many materials are
processed through the refinery flow plan.
The main units in a refinery are:
ï CDU: Atmospheric Distillation
ï VDU: Vacuum Distillation Unit
ï RF: Catalytic Reformer Unit
ï CC: Catalytic Cracking Unit
The material transformations, productions and losses are reported through material
movements:
ï Transfers: movement type 309
ï Goods issue / consumption: movement type 201
ï Losses: movement type 551
For a production environment new movement types should be considered, e.g. a
copy of 309 to reflect production, another copy to reflect blending, etc. This way
these refinery conversion movements can be distinguished from standard re-brand
and Bill of Material postings. The same applies to consumption and losses.

260 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Refinery processing

Figure 105: Crude and Feedstock to Raw Material Blend

The crude oil enters in the CDU (Atmospheric Distillation Pipe still) to be
transformed into a raw material blend.
Example: material ARAB_HEAVY (-) is transformed into RAW_MAT_BLEND
(+). The movement type 309 posts this process.

Figure 106: Raw Material Blend to Intermediate (semi-finished) products

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 261



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

The raw material blend is converted into the CDU (atmospheric pipestill) into
intermediate products such as gas, LPG, naphtha, kerosene and distillate.
Example: material RAW_MAT_BLEND (-) is transformed into LPG (+). The
movement type 309 posts this process.
After appointing the productive process, it is possible to post refinery
consumptions and gains / losses for the pipestill.
Example: Consumption of material TOP_GAS through movement type 201 and
loss of material RAW_MAT_BLEND through movement type 551.

Semi-finished Products Blending

Reforming of Virgin Naphta

Figure 107: Reforming of Virgin Naphta

Naphtha produced in the Pipestill is converted in the reformer into gas, hydrogen,
LPG and reformate. The postings are done through movement type 309.
The consumptions in the reformer are posted through movement type 551 while
the gains / losses are posted through movement type 201.

262 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Refinery processing

Vacuum Distillation at Atmospheric Residue

Figure 108: Vacuum Distillation at Atmospheric Residue

Pipestill vacuums are upgraded in the Vacuum Distillation Unit (VDU). Here the
atmospheric residue is transformed into materials like vacuum gasoil and vacuum
residue. The movement type 309 reflects the operations.
The gain and loss postings of the atmospheric residue in the VDU are done
through movement type 501.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 263



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Cracking of Vacuum Gasoil

Figure 109: Cracking of Vacuum Gasoil

Vacuum Gasoil produced in the Vacuum Distillation Unit is transformed in the
Catalytic Cracker.
The Catalytic Cracker unity recovers more light intermediate products, such as
cracked LPG and cracked naphtha. Like the former operations, the productive
process is posted through movement type 309, the consumptions are posted
through movement type 201 and gains / losses through 501.

264 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Refinery processing

Blending

Figure 110: Blending

Intermediate materials are blended to finished products and transferred to the
distribution plant.
Examples:
ï Blending of Regular: from CRACK_NAPHTHA (-) to REGULAR (+)
ï Blending of Premium: from VIRGIN_NAPHTA (-) to PREMIUM (+)
ï Blending of Diesel: from GASOIL 1 (-) to DIESEL (+)

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 265



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Transfer to Distribution Plant

Figure 111: Transfer to Distribution Plant

In most countries it is possible to post the transfer of finished products from
refinery to distribution plant through movement types 309 or 301. The user
informs the respective data for origin and destination: plant, storage location and
batch. Some countries have specific laws that demand the tax calculation during
transfer postings, so some localization requirements must be met, like specific
movement types.

IOG100 Lesson: Reporting

Lesson: Reporting
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain the reporting needs on processes of material movements
in a refinery, since the initial input of raw materials to production site until the
transfer of the finished products to the distribution plant. The lesson focuses on
standard reports which are available in SAP ECC 6.0 (IS-OIL 6.0) to analyze
inventory and material movements.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Understand reports for internal movements at the refinery on stages
ï Execute and explain report ñ material balance for Manufacturing Units
ï Execute and explain report ñ consumption of intermediates
ï Execute and explain report ñ materials blending
ï Execute and explain report ñ transfer movements to Distribution Plant

Business Example
After the refinery processing, represented by internal movements, is accomplished
it is required to prepare reports. The reports to be cover manufacturing balance,
consumption of intermediates, blending of products and transfer postings from
production site to product storage area.

Reporting

Figure 112: Reporting

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 291



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

The most suitable standard report for refinery movements is the one named
ìStock on Posting Dateî, accessed through transaction MB5B or menu path
Materials Management→ Inventory Management→ Environment→ Stock→
Stock for Posting Date. The user has to inform material, plant, storage location
and selection date.

Figure 113: Production, Input / Output Balance for Units, Loss

The report ìStock on Posting Dateî shows all the material documents in the
selection date. It also shows the total of goods issues and goods receipts by
material. The resulting stock within a unit must be zero.

Figure 114: Production / Consumption Intermediates

The resulting stock position is not zero; opening and closing are shown.

292 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Reporting

Figure 115: Blending

The movements in the selection date are shown with plant and storage location.

Figure 116: Transfer to Distribution Plant

The movements in the selection date are shown with plant and storage location.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 293



Unit 5: Refinery: Silo Management, Refining, Internal Movements IOG100

Some countries have specific tax laws that do not allow the usage of transfer
postings in only one step. For these situations, use also report MB5T ñ Stock
in Transit (menu path Materials Management→ Inventory Management→
Environment→ Stock→ Stock in Transit) ñ to display the dispatched material that
has not been arrived to the destination.

Unit Summary IOG100

302 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



Unit 6
Exchange Agreements

Unit Overview
This unit will explain typical business process of Exchange Agreements which
are available with SAP for Oil&Gas.
The unit focuses on logistic operations in Exchange Agreements (IS-OIL-EXG)
and illustrates document flow to be generated under this functionality. You will
study major functions of this component such as exchange agreements and
exchange related purchasing and sales contract, call-offs from the contract and
deliveries (carry out purchase assignment, check or change a quantity schedule
and process deliveries). It also covers reporting activities on existing exchange
agreements such as:
ï Overview of your receipts and deliveries that are connected to the exchange

agreement
ï Principle of logical inventory and carry out a logical inventory adjustment
ï Netting sums receivables and payables within an exchange agreement

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Create exchange agreements and describe the purchase and sale business
process flow:

ï Create exchange related purchasing and sales contract(s)
ï Process receipts and deliveries against exchange contracts
ï Carry out reporting activities (logical inventory, exchange balance, netting

and exchange statements).

Unit Contents
Lesson: Exchange Operations ... . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .304

Exercise 10: Exchanges... . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . .325

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 303



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Lesson: Exchange Operations
Lesson Overview
The lesson will be about the process under Exchange Agreements (IS-OIL-EXG)
such as creating exchange agreement between VOIL DE and our partner for like
products. To do this you will need to create an exchange agreement header and
create and link purchase and sales contracts to that agreement. It will demonstrate
the issue and receipt of material with automatic creation and review of the resulting
financial postings. You will learn how the material postings will be calculated
using ìprice reference plantî functionality. It will show how to invoice our partner
and how to receive an invoice. It will also demonstrate how LIA (logical inventory
adjustment) has been expanded to include adjustments to logical inventory which
will settle our position by transferring our balance to another active agreement.
You will execute reports showing: the exchange balance report to get an overview
of your receipts and deliveries that are connected to the exchange agreement, the
principle of logical inventory and carry out a logical inventory adjustment, how
netting sums receivables and payables within an exchange agreement.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Create exchange agreements and describe the purchase and sale business

process flow:
ï Create exchange related purchasing and sales contract(s)
ï Process receipts and deliveries against exchange contracts
ï Carry out reporting activities (logical inventory, exchange balance, netting

and exchange statements).

Business Example
One of the wholesale Customers requires VOIL DE to deliver the finished products
to its remote location under the valid sale contract. An exchange agreement gives
VOIL DE the possibility of using the terminal or depot capacity of Exchange
Partner which is allocated close to the Customer in order to deliver products.
Through exchange contracts VOIL DE can deliver products from Exchange
Partner locations and thus to keep transportation costs down. VOIL DE is able to
buy and sell finished products under the exchange agreement.

304 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

Exchange Agreements (finished products)
This component contains functions for managing exchange agreements between
companies in the oil and gas industry ñ the exchange of products at various
locations. An exchange agreement is made between two oil companies (exchange
partners), when the companies would like to exchange product at different
locations.
To support the management of exchange business transactions, you can:
ï Create an exchange agreement
ï Create quantity schedules for planning and monitoring material quantities
ï Balance differences in value of exchanged materials using fees
ï Settle claims and liabilities against one another (netting)
ï Exchange unlike products, and balance the logical inventory that results

(logical inventory adjustment)
ï Create exchange statements that reflect the current status of your exchange

activities in a specific period
ï Create additional evaluations with respect to your exchange activities (for

example, creating a list of all goods receipts and goods issues within an
exchange agreement).

Figure 117: Exchange Operations - Introduction

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 305



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Figure 118: Exchange Operations - Concept

An exchange agreement gives VOIL DE the possibility of using the terminal or
depot capacity of VOIL DE exchange partner in order to sell products. Through
exchange contracts VOIL DE can deliver products from exchange partner
locations.

Exchange Operations ñ Concept
Why do oil companies exchange?
ï To expand into marketing areas where a company does not have infrastructure
ï To exploit excess capacity where a company does have infrastructure
ï To minimize transportation costs.

306 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

Figure 119: Exchange Operations Management

R/3 supports the linking of entitlements to ìliftî (obtain) a product from an
exchange partner (purchase agreement, receipt side) and entitlements of the
exchange partner to lift a product from the oil company (sales agreement, delivery
side) under an exchange agreement.
Within the oil industry, an exchange is an agreement between oil companies
to allow lifting of products at one time and one location in exchange for the
entitlement to lift a product at another time and location.
Usually oil companies do not invoice an exchange partner after each individual
movement against a particular exchange. Such exchange agreements may be
netted and settled periodically. Oil companies usually keep track of their exchange
balance.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 307



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Figure 120: Exchange Basics

Figure 121: Exchange Agreement Structure

An exchange agreement is an agreement between two oil companies for the
exchange of a product at different locations. In the SAP ERP System, a link exists
between customer and vendor master data records, because in the system, the
exchange partner is both the vendor and customer at the same time.

308 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

The exchange agreement consists of the exchange header and of the assigned
sales contracts and purchase contracts.

Exchange Agreement Structure
The exchange header data is made up of general information for each exchange
agreement, as well as the corresponding detail information.
The evergreen type determines how quantities are handled in contracts. With the
different evergreen types you can determine the total quantity that you or your
exchange partner can call-off, the quantity that you can call off per period, or
an unlimited call-off quantity.
You can choose between internal or external posting rules: With internal postings,
material, taxes, and/or fees are posted to internal accounts. With external posting,
material, any taxes, and/or fees are charged to the exchange partner.
By selecting netting, external postings are made but the open amounts are blocked
for collection purposes or for payment. At the end of a period, the receivables
and payables are compared and only the differential amount is calculated for
billing purposes.
Contracts can be assigned to the exchange agreement, which helps to manage
exchange deliveries and receipts.

Figure 122: Exchange Agreements

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 309



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Figure 123: Evergreen Contracts - Dates

Figure 124: Evergreen Contracts - Regular

310 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

There are different kinds of exchange agreements:
ï In a borrow/loan exchange, materials are only posted internally, they are not

invoiced to the partner. A logical inventory is created. Excise duties and
fees caused by material movements are generally invoiced. A borrow/loan
exchange is also known as a ìpureî exchange. It is mainly used in the United
States. Companies in the U.S. using borrow/loan exchanges usually keep
track of the exchange balances and only charge for fees. As a result, only
fees are settled.

ï In a buy/sell exchange, materials and taxes are invoiced. Although they
might be posted internally, fees are generally invoiced as well.

There are also evergreen contracts, which are long-term exchange contracts with
no fixed end date and no fixed quantity.

Evergreen Contracts ñ Dates
An Unlimited Evergreen Contract is created so that partners can lift as much
product as they require, that is, no quantity schedule is used. There is only a
start date and a closing date.

Evergreen Contracts ñ Regular
In the regular contract a quantity per period is defined, that is, a quantity schedule
must be used. Besides the start and end date there is a review date.

The exchange delivery scenario takes place when your company delivers products
to its exchange partnerís customer.

Exchange Deliveries ñ Documents View
The documents on this slide are created when processing the loan or sale of
product against your exchange contract.
The customer (exchange partner) fulfills the contract by placing orders from the
contract (call-offs or release orders). When you create a call-off, you refer to
the corresponding contract, and the system automatically updates the called-off
quantity in the contract.
The breakdown period is to be copied from the quantity schedule to the contract
call-off, depending upon the delivery data entered. Fees for the individual items
are also copied from the contract to the call-off.
A delivery is carried out with reference to a call-off, and is thus also linked to the
exchange agreement. The goods issue has to be posted.
The account postings for goods issues are:
Buy/Sell Agreement:

Credit: PHYSICAL INVENTORY ( - )
Debit: COST OF GOODS SOLD ( + )

Borrow/Loan Agreement:

Credit: PHYSICAL INVENTORY ( - )
Debit: LOGICAL INVENTORY ( + )

Depending on the type of outline agreement (thus depending on the exchange
type), the exchange partner may only be charged for fees and taxes, or may be
charged for other things. If netting is provided in the exchange agreement, the
invoice is blocked and offset in subsequent netting.
The account postings for billing are:
Buy/sell agreement:

Exchange Scenario for Deliveries
A basic exchange scenario would be as follows: a customer of VOIL's exchange
partner receives material from VOIL's plant.
Call-offs are created based on the sales contract which has been assigned to the
exchange agreement. Call-offs are needed to reflect the physical goods flow and
the resulting exchange-related goods issues which are posted to the exchange
partnerís customer.
In order to depict the scenario in your ERP System, you create a call-off, delivery,
and an invoice. You could also place rush orders when your exchange partner's
customer receives the product immediately, or when you deliver the product to the
customer on the same day on which the order was made. The system automatically
creates a delivery for a rush order. However, the billing document is created later.

The exchange receipt scenario takes place when the company borrows or buys

partner, but it does not deliver it to your customer. This key figure expresses the
quantities processed for exchange receipts for a period (current month) in the
stockkeeping unit of measure. It is used in various reports to capture data about

partner delivered to your customer.

Exchange Receipts ñ Documents View
The documents on this slide are created when borrowing or buying a product
against your exchange contract.
Call-offs are created with reference to the purchase contract. Data from the
exchange header is copied into the call-off (for example, the number of the
exchange agreement, netting-blocking indicator, etc.). As with the purchase
contract, that data is displayed on the details screen for each item. There is a
quantity schedule for each item; the breakdown is copied from the purchase
contract. The breakdown period in the quantity schedule is based on the delivery
date. The fees for the individual items are also copied from the purchase contract
to the call-off.

When a goods receipt is posted, the system creates a material document and an
accounting document. In the material document, which serves as proof of a goods
movement, data from the exchange agreement is copied into the purchase order.
Parallel to the material document, the system creates an accounting document
which contains the accruals from the fee postings.
The account postings for goods receipts are:

Debit: EXCHANGE FEES ( + )

Invoice verification is carried out during invoice receipt based on the data
previously created during goods receipt. During goods receipt-related invoice
verification, each goods receipt is settled individually. However, open items
that still have to be settled can also be selected with reference to an exchange
agreement. You can settle goods receipts with Evaluated Receipt Settlement
(ERS) within exchange agreements directly, without having first received an
invoice. ERS automatically creates invoice verification documents according to
previously set criteria.

Figure 130: Purchase Assignments

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 317



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Figure 131: Purchase Assignment - Documents View

Another exchange scenario would be that a customer of VOIL receives material
from an exchange partner's plant.
When processing a purchase assignment, you assign a delivery quantity to a
purchase order quantity. Your customer sends you an order, but the ordered
material is to be delivered to your customer from one of your exchange partner's
locations. To do this, you send a purchase order to your exchange partner, which
details the material to be delivered to the customer.
When your exchange partner delivers the material to your customer, you create
a delivery and assign the delivery quantity to your purchase contract or your
purchase order.
The link between delivery and purchase order causes the system to automatically
post the goods receipt, as soon as you have posted the goods issue.
The system updates the quantity schedule in the following way:
ï When you create the delivery and assign the quantity to be delivered to

a purchase order (or to a purchase contract), the quantity to be delivered
appears as an intended quantity in the quantity schedule of the corresponding
item.

ï As soon as you post the goods issue (and the system automatically creates
the goods receipt for the purchase order), the delivered quantity is listed in
the quantity schedule as a goods receipt quantity.

318 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

Purchase Assignment ñ Documents View
For a purchase assignment, you have to select the item within a delivery which you
want to assign to a purchase contract or call-off. Select purchase assignment tab.
It is possible to assign the sales order item to a purchase contract item or to a
purchase call-off item. As soon as the goods issue is posted, an automatic goods
receipt is carried out for the purchase order; or - if the sales order item is assigned
to a contract, a purchase call-off will be posted before an automatic goods receipt
is carried out.

Figure 132: Exchange Settlement

When a contract expires, it is possible to perform the settlement.
When netting has been selected, the system creates a link between the customer
account and the vendor account for a specific exchange partner. The items relevant
to netting in those accounts are then offset. The difference is then a single open
item, which is charged to the exchange partner or which has to be paid to the
exchange partner.
You can send the exchange partner an ìinvoiceî, i.e., a statement, so your partner
can check all the relevant quantities moved.
Reconciliation allows you to compare your data with that of your exchange partner
and discuss how to handle differences that have occurred.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 319



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Figure 133: Netting

Movement-based netting collects receivables and payables in an exchange and
offsets them against each other. Also, movements without financial documents
are included.
Goods movements that reference the exchange agreement are used as the selection
method for selecting the documents.
The system calculates the netting balance as a sum of the receivables and payables.
You either bill the balance to your exchange partner, or your company pays the
amount.
You can create an exchange statement (printout) from the movement-based netting
document, and you can send it to your exchange partner. Your exchange partner
can then check the exchange statement. If your exchange partner reports any
changes, you can still change the movement-based netting document, as long
as you have not created a batch-input session BTCI (Batch Communication
Interface). When the batch-input session is run, the accounts are cleared and
difference postings take place.
A ìBalance Calculation Indicatorî gives you the option of including balances for
base products which have no activity for the month.
For the printout, it is necessary that you maintain an address for your sales
organization.
Split movement-based netting allows separate netting documents for fees, material
value, and taxes to be created.

320 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

Figure 134: Logical Inventory Adjustment

Figure 135: Exchange Balance

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 321



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Figure 136: Logical Inventory Adjustment - Example

When a contract expires, it is possible to adjust the exchange balance.
You determine if the imbalance between delivered and received material is to
be settled by:
ï An adjustment receipt and/or
ï An adjustment delivery and/or
ï A negotiated payment

Exchange Balance
When exchange balances are built up against ìpureî exchanges, it is usual to
value the assets and liabilities associated with the goods movements as if they
were actual inventory for financial accounting purposes. This means the logical
inventory for a material is a material quantity, and due to exchange movements that
took place it exists as payables or receivables with respect to the exchange partner.
The Logical Inventory is a quantity of product, and not accounts payable or
receivable. R/3 records and tracks the value of the inventory at the prevailing
inventory carrying price when the material movement was created.
If no ìown inventoryî is carried at a location, the receivable and payable volumes
can be valued at the current value at a ìreference plantî.
You can create an individual evaluation structure using the flexible analysis option
from the Logistics Information System.

322 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Exchange Operations

You can list all material movements and logical inventory adjustment (LIA)
transactions which are assigned to an exchange agreement and correspond to the
selection criteria. The list is sorted according to:
ï Exchange partner
ï Number of the exchange agreement
ï Material
ï Plant
ï Month
The total amount of material movements and LIA transactions is displayed
for each level; the lifts and receipts are listed in two separate columns and the
difference between the two is listed in an additional column.
The system only updates the exchange balance when the goods receipts / goods
issues are exchange related.

Logical Inventory Adjustment ñ Example
The logical inventory adjustment transaction allows the oil company to adjust the
logical inventory it has recorded against an exchange partner.
It is possible to settle the difference (imbalance) between delivered and received
material by means of a payment. Open quantities can also be moved to another
exchange agreement, which has the effect that the items in the first exchange
agreement are settled and the exchange agreement can be concluded.
No physical movement is involved, but rather only a ìlogical inventory
movementî.
The LIA transaction allows the oil company to record the swap of the ownership
of a specified quantity of one product for the ownership of a specified quantity of
another product. Note that it does not necessarily have to be a different product.
When an LIA is carried out, logical inventory accounts and the exchange balance
are updated.
Account Postings
Delivery Adjustment:

Credit: EXG BALANCING ACCT ( - )

Debit: LOGICAL INVENTORY ( + )

Receipt Adjustment:

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 323



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Credit: LOGICAL INVENTORY ( - )

Debit: EXG BALANCING ACCT ( + )

Negotiated Payment ñ Payable:

Credit: VENDOR ( - )

Debit: EXG BALANCING ACCT ( + )

Negotiated Payment ñ Receivable:

Credit: EXG BALANCING ACCT ( - )

Debit: CUSTOMER ( + )

Exercise 10: Exchanges
Exercise Objectives
After completing this exercise, you will be able to:
ï Create exchange agreements
ï Explain posting rules, administrative data and control data.
ï Assign purchase and sales contracts to an exchange agreement
ï Complete the exchanges business flow with call-offs (ìliftsî) from purchase

and sales contracts.
ï Carry out invoice verification using evaluated receipt settlement, and create

a billing document using the billing due list
ï Use the exchange balance report to provide an overview of receipts and

deliveries that are linked to the exchange agreement.
ï Carry out the logical inventory adjustment
ï Create a movement-based netting document and check the output on the

screen

Business Example
An exchange contract gives VOIL DE (CC 1100) the possibility of using the
terminal or depot capacity of VOIL DE 's Exchange partner in order to sell
petroleum products. The other reason of this exchange contract is to keep
transportation costs down when VOIL DE delivers products from Exchange
partner locations to its remote Customers.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 325



Unit 6: Exchange Agreements IOG100

Task:
VOIL DE uses exchange agreements with an oil industry partner in order to
exchange products. VOIL DE uses exchange contracts to buy products from the
oil industry partner and to sell products to that partner. VOIL DE uses quantity
schedules for the planning and monitoring of material quantities. A customer of
Exchange partner requests product and VOIL DEís Exchange partner decides to
lift the product from VOIL DE's plant. In another case, VOIL DE lifts products
from the Exchange partnerís plant and delivers that product to its own customer.
VOIL DE has to check the exchange balance report in order to adjust differences
between lifts and receipts, and carries out a logical inventory adjustment (LIA).
VOIL DE does not invoice its Exchange partner after each individual movement,
but settles the exchange agreement periodically. VOIL DE wants to offset the
receivables and payables collected in the exchange agreements against each other.
VOIL DE can create a netting statement (printout) for the movements-based
netting document, and can send it to its exchange partner. VOIL DE's exchange
partner can then check the statement. If its exchange partner reports any changes
to VOIL DE, the movements-based netting document can still be changed, as long
as VOIL DE has not created a batch-input session. When the batch-input session
is run, the accounts are cleared and difference postings are carried out.
1. Set up an exchange agreement with your oil industry partner. Create and

assign sales and purchase contracts to the exchange agreement.
2. Deliver product to your exchange partner's customer.
3. Call-off a certain quantity of product from the purchase contract. Thus you

need to create a purchase order with reference to the purchase contract.
4. To run a purchase assignment scenario, in which a Customer is calling you to

order a specific quantity of product that is to be delivered from your exchange
partnerís location, you have to create an order and assign the subsequent
delivery to an existing purchase contract linked to an exchange agreement.

5. Use the billing due list to combine the documents to be billed. On the
purchase side, use evaluated receipt settlement (ERS) to settle the goods
receipts.

6. Use the system reporting tools to examine what has happened within your
exchange agreement so far. You can settle the difference between delivered
and received material with a delivery or receipt adjustment.You can also
settle financial differences with a negotiated payment.

7. Create a movements-based netting document, examine the netting proposal,
and check the screen output.

Unit 7
Secondary Distribution

Unit Overview
The key processes of transportation within Secondary Distribution (finished
products) in SAP for Oil&Gas reflect the key steps you need to take during the
transportation process. Within each of these key processes are functions that have
been specifically tailored for the oil and gas industry.
Transportation is an essential element in the logistics chain. It affects both
incoming and outgoing goods. Effective transportation planning and processing
ensure that shipments are dispatched without delay and arrive on schedule.
Transportation costs play an essential role in the calculation of the price of a
product. It is important to keep these transportation costs to a minimum so that
the price of a product remains competitive. Efficient transportation planning and
processing helps to keep these costs down.
These transportation functions can handle planning and processing for both
inbound and outbound shipments. You can control and monitor the entire
transportation process from the planning stage to goods issue at your shipping
point (for outbound shipments) or vendor location (for inbound shipments),
through to goods receipt at the customer location or your plant.
Other available functions include: shipment costs calculation and settlement
with the service agent, transfer to accounting, credit memo creation and invoice
verification.
The vehicle definition and compartment planning functions are designed to meet
your needs in managing the shipment of large volumes of bulk materials. The
transportation and distribution capabilities work seamlessly with functions in SAP
for Oil&Gas for inventory management of hydrocarbon products, allowing you to
handle changes in the quantity of oil material due to variations in ambient pressure
and temperature. This ensures that the most accurate quantity of a product is
always used throughout the shipment process.

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Explain how bulk shipments are integrated within the supply chain and
explain the in-transit stock concept

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 345



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

ï Create the different document types that can be assigned to a bulk shipment
for purchases, sales and transfers in the SAP for Oil&Gas

ï Create a vehicle for a bulk shipment, distinguish the different kinds of meters
for loading and discharging a vehicle, describe which kinds of compatibilities
can be set up for processing a bulk shipment

ï Explain the use of routes and service providers within bulk shipments, assign
routes and service providers to a bulk shipment, assign the document items
of the underlying documents to the stages of a route

ï Process bulk shipments: schedule a bulk shipment, load a simple bulk
shipment, deliver a simple bulk shipment and post a loss during delivery
confirmation, analyze the document flow within a bulk shipment

ï Create a shipment cost document, explain how costs are calculated, settle
costs with a service provider, and invoice costs to customers.
