IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain typical business process of Secondary Distribution
(finished products) which are available with SAP for Oil&Gas.
The lesson focuses on logistic operations in Bulk Transportation and Shipment
Costing (IS-OIL-TD) and illustrates document flow to be generated under Bulk
Shipment Document. You will study major functions of this component such as
master data and in-transit stock concept, bulk shipment scheduling, bulk shipment
processing, shipment costing and reporting.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain how bulk shipments are integrated within the supply chain and

explain the in-transit stock concept
ï Create the different document types that can be assigned to a bulk shipment

for purchases, sales and transfers in the SAP for Oil&Gas
ï Create a vehicle for a bulk shipment, distinguish the different kinds of meters

for loading and discharging a vehicle, describe which kinds of compatibilities
can be set up for processing a bulk shipment

ï Explain the use of routes and service providers within bulk shipments, assign
routes and service providers to a bulk shipment, assign the document items
of the underlying documents to the stages of a route

ï Process bulk shipments: schedule a bulk shipment, load a simple bulk
shipment, deliver a simple bulk shipment and post a loss during delivery
confirmation, analyze the document flow within a bulk shipment

ï Create a shipment cost document, explain how costs are calculated, settle
costs with a service provider, and invoice costs to customers.

Business Example
VOIL DE delivers products to customers. External service agents are
commissioned to ship the materials, but the company is responsible for
organization and execution. VOIL DE organizes oil shipments by itself and
needs to record the costs for service providers like carrier, insurance, harbour
fees, agents, and so on.
In order that materials can be shipped as efficiently as possible, purchases,
deliveries, and transfers are combined where the points of departure, in-transit
locations and destinations match. Depending on the route, loading and discharge
points, distance, quantities etc. the shipment costs for the shipments are calculated.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 347



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

VOIL DE calculates and settles shipment costs with the various service agents
after the bulk shipment has been fully processed. The system automatically
calculates prices for shipment costs. Afterwards, the costs are transferred to
financial accounting (FI) and controlling (CO). The costs are settled by paying the
invoice. The costs of transportation are invoiced to VOIL DE's customers.

Secondary Distribution (finished products)
Transportation is an essential element in the logistics chain. It affects both
incoming and outgoing goods. Effective transportation planning and processing
ensure that shipments are dispatched without delay and arrive on schedule.
Transportation costs play an essential role in the calculation of the price of a
product. It is important to keep these transportation costs to a minimum so that
the price of a product remains competitive. Efficient transportation planning and
processing helps to keep these costs down.

Figure 137: Secondary Distribution (finished products)

The Hydrocarbon Products Transportation scenario supports oil and gas companies
to plan and execute bulk shipments in a timely and accurate manner at the
lowest possible cost. The scheduling and execution capabilities for loading and
unloading bulk shipments provide a consistent framework for processing and
tracking shipment of high volumes of bulk material as well as the handling of
changes that frequently occur in the oil and gas secondary distribution business.
The scenario supports freight costs calculation for bulk shipments with evaluated
receipt settlement for invoice processing with the carrier.

348 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Secondary Distribution (finished products)
You can now carry out transportation planning and shipment completion using
a new organizational unit, the transportation planning point. Basically, the
transportation planning point consists of a group of employees responsible
for organizing transportation activities. Each shipment is assigned to a
specific transportation planning point for transportation planning and shipment
completion. You must define the various transportation planning points used in
your organization in Customizing for Corporate Structure before they can be
used to perform transportation functions. You can define this organizational unit
according to your companyís needs, for example, according to geographical
location or mode of transport.
The transportation planning point is assigned to a company code, but is otherwise
independent of other organizational units.

Figure 138: Organizational Elements in Transportation

It is not necessary to assign the transportation planning point to a company code
for transportation planning purposes. However, company code assignment is
necessary for shipment costing and settlement. Internal offsetting of costs between
company codes (one company code takes care of transportation processing for all
the firmís company codes, for example) is presently not available. These must be
manually entered in the financial accounting ledgers.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 349



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Bulk Transportation Processing (IS-OIL-TD)
Transportation is an essential part of the oil and gas supply chain. The bulk
shipping document is the central element of transportation planning and
shipment completion. It contains all the information necessary for carrying
out transportation. The bulk shipment combines inbound deliveries, outbound
deliveries (shipping notifications) and transfers with matching points of departure,
in-transit locations, and destinations. Effective transportation processing is
required so that materials are shipped on time and are received on schedule at the
destination. The IS-OIL-TD bulk transportation application component allows
you to keep track of the in-transit stock during a specific transportation run.

Figure 139: Bulk Transportation Processing (IS-OIL-TD)

For example, you use the individual shipment document to plan and process the
transportation of goods from one location to another. You use the collective
shipment to move goods from one or more points of departure to one or more
destinations. Separate document types deal with inbound and outbound shipments.

350 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Bulk Shipment ñ Document Assignment
The Document Overview screen in TD bulk shipment is used to assign underlying
documents to a shipment. The Transportation and Distribution (TD) bulk shipment
component supports inbound purchases, outbound sales, and product transfers,
and is integrated with the relevant process flows. The underlying documents that
can be assigned to and processed within a bulk shipment are:
ï Outbound deliveries
ï Reservations
ï Transfer deliveries
ï Inbound deliveries
A bulk shipment requires at least one document assigned. Possible documents
are delivery (inbound, outbound, and transfer), and reservations. The document
selection report can help to find the documents number. A document has to be
load or discharge relevant. Load and discharge relevance at the same time is
also supported. The document type determines how the system processes the
underlying document. When assigning documents to a shipment, it is necessary to
select one of the following document types:
ï D ñ Delivery (Outbound Delivery)
ï R ñ Reservation
ï S ñ Shipping notification (Inbound Delivery)

Figure 140: Bulk Shipment - Document Assignment

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 351



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

During scheduling, documents are assigned to a shipment as load or discharge
relevant. For example if you mark a document as relevant to loading, the system
proposes the product and quantities from the document during the Loading
Confirmation process. If you mark the document as relevant to discharge, then the
product and quantities from the underlying document are proposed in the Delivery
Confirmation process. At least one of the indicators must be selected when the
document is assigned, or you can also select both. Alternatively, a document
selection routine can be used during scheduling to find documents for assignment
to a shipment. The document selection routine generates a list of documents that
meet the selection criteria you specified. You can select documents from this list
for assignment to the shipment.

Stock-In-Transit concept
You use intransit plant or storage locations to represent product which is being
transported on a vehicle as part of a bulk shipment. By defining intransit plant or
storage locations, you can manage and control stock after it has left the loading
plant and while intransit.
Intransit Storage Location
During loading, the product is transferred from the loading plant to the intransit
storage location. From that point on and until the delivery is confirmed, the control
and ownership of the material remains with the delivering plant. Subsequent
transactions in IS-OIL-TD that involve a shipment result the intransit storage
location being updated. As a result, you can track product while intransit and
account for gains or losses that occur between loading confirmation and delivery
confirmation.
Intransit Plant
When shipping large quantities of product over long distances such as in pipeline
and marine shipments, it can be necessary to maintain a segregated overview of
the intransit stock. This can be done by representing the vehicle as a separate
plant, known as an intransit plant. It is possible to allocate all vehicles to a single
intransit plant or, alternatively, to set up a separate intransit plant for each vehicle.
The intransit plant can consist of multiple storage locations for product tracking
purposes as it moves along its route. The allocation of the intransit plant is
specified in the underlying documents that are assigned to the bulk shipment.
You can define how the system is to determine the intransit storage location for
a bulk shipment. For example, you can determine that the system is to use the
location entered in the outbound delivery, reservation, or stock transfer order as
the intransit storage location for the shipment.

352 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Figure 141: Stock-In-Transit concept

Use of Intransit Storage Location in Sales Cycle
In the standard document flow for sales in Sales and Distribution (SD), stock
movements take place with reference to an outbound delivery through the
generation of a goods issue document. In this case, the customer takes ownership
of the stock as soon as it leaves the delivering plant, on execution of the goods
issue.
To track the stock at the point after leaving the delivering plant and prior to
arrival at the customer or receiving plant, IS-OIL-TD introduces the concept of
the intransit plant or storage location. In this case a transfer is used to move the
stock from the delivering plant to the vehicle during load confirmation. The stock
loaded on the vehicle then exists in the intransit plant or storage location. This
can be shown through the Stock Overview report. As a result, you can track
product while intransit and account for gains or losses that occur between loading
confirmation and delivery confirmation.

Transportation and Distribution Integration
The Transportation and Distribution (TD) component covers the logistics activities
related to:
ï Receipt of purchased product from a vendor
ï Transfer of product between two company-owned locations
ï Delivery of product from a delivering plant to a customer

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 353



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

These activities are carried out across the processes of scheduling, load
confirmation, and delivery confirmation.
Inbound shipments are an integral part of the process chain in purchasing and
are processed based on inbound deliveries (shipping notifications). The basis of
the purchasing process is the purchase order. The subsequent document is the
shipping notification, which is used by the vendor to confirm a delivery. The
shipping notification is the basis for creating inbound shipments, that is, the
shipment of the delivery from the vendor to the companyís plant. A goods receipt
is posted at load confirmation for the shipment, confirming the receipt of material
to an in-transit location. Invoice verification completes the purchasing process.

Figure 142: Transportation and Distribution Integration

Transfer shipments can also be used for stock transfers between plants or storage
locations. The reservation document is the basis for creating transfer shipments
between two plants within a company.
A material document is created when loading or delivery of the shipment is
confirmed. This document confirms the posting of material from an issuing
location to a receiving location.
Transfer shipments can also be carried out on the basis of stock transport orders.
Deliveries are created from stock transport orders using the delivery due list.
These deliveries can be assigned to a bulk shipment. The ERP system posts goods
issue and goods receips documents during shipment processing.

354 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Outbound shipments are part of the sales and distribution process and are
processed as deliveries. The basis of the sales and distribution process is the
sales order. The subsequent document is the outbound delivery that documents
the shipping of goods. The delivery document is the basis of creating outbound
shipments from the companyís plant to the customer. A material document is
created at loading for the shipment. This document confirms the posting of
material to in-transit stock. A goods issue is posted at delivery confirmation for
the shipment. Creation of the invoice completes the sales process.

Means of Transportation, Vehicle
A vehicle is any means by which product is transported from one location to
another. Driver master data enables driver details, such as shift period or driver
licenses to be stored in the system for information purposes within the shipment.
Drivers can be assigned to vehicles during the bulk transportation scheduling
process.
A one to many relationship exists between a vehicle and transport units. For
example, a truck can be created with a prime mover and several trailers. There
is also a one to many relationship between transport units and vehicles, in that a
transport unit can be assigned to several vehicles. Validation checks ensure that a
transport unit is not scheduled to more than one vehicle in the same shipment.
Transport units consist of none, one, or more compartments. The compartments
represent the physical storage tanks of a particular transport unit. During
scheduling and loading, product is scheduled and loaded according to the attributes
and capacity of each compartment. Therefore, each compartment requires
independent attributes to be defined, such as minimum and maximum volumes.
A weight restriction can be defined on the transport unit level.
None, one, or many vehicle meters can be assigned to compartments. Vehicle
meters are used during loading and delivery confirmation in bulk transportation
and accurately measure the quantity of product loaded or delivered.
The same concept is applicable for all kinds of transport systems like pipelines,
marine vessels, and trains.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 355



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 143: Vehicle Concept and Driver Concept

Figure 144: Vehicle structure

The Driver master data record stores driver details, such as their shift period or
drivers licenses in the system. You can assign drivers to vehicles during the
scheduling process of Bulk Transportation and Distribution. Driver master data
stores the driverís last name and first name, together with an external personnel

356 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

number. The external personnel number is not linked to the Human Resources
(SAP ERP Human Capital Management) application component, and is designed
primarily as an alternative method for identifying drivers.
Information about the types of licenses held by the driver is stored in driver master
data record. You can also enter the dates within which the licenses are valid. The
license types are defined in Customizing, and belong to the same pool of licenses
which are assigned to vehicles.
You can enter information relating to the shifts worked by the driver, together with
the periods for which the shifts are valid. The driver shift information can be used
during scheduling, where a vehicle can be scheduled for a particular shift. A shift
rota is created for the driver in Customizing for IS Oil & Gas (Downstream).

Vehicle operational characteristics
There are two kinds of meters: rack meters and vehicle meters.
ï Rack meter master data stores the attributes of meters used during the

loading or delivery transaction. Rack meters have assignments to both
storage locations and materials. Functionality exists to flush, recalibrate, and
record end readings for rack meters. These readings are shown in a meter
reconciliation report.

ï Vehicle meter master data is used to maintain vehicle meter attributes in the
system. Meters are assigned to compartments within transport units and are
then used to record loaded or delivered quantities.

Characteristics of the meter such as the unit of measure for the meter, number of
digits on the meter, and an equipment number (linked to the plant maintenance
system) are stored. The conversion factor which converts the quantity entered
into the actual quantity is also stored. The start reading of the meter, as it is first
installed, may be recorded to support meter reconciliation. The date and time of
the last meter reconciliation is also recorded in the meter master record.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 357



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 145: Vehicle operational characteristics

Compatibility checking ensures that product is compatible with the compartment to
which it is assigned, and that vehicles are compatible with customer requirements.
The characteristics of the products, compartments, vehicles, and customers are
represented in the system using compatibility indicators. These compatibility
indicators are grouped into compatibility groups. If desired, the compatibility
checking function can be turned off.
The material master contains a product/compartment compatibility field used to
assign compatibility groups to products. It is located in the shipping section of
the sales/plant view of the material master. Indicators within the assigned product
group must correspond to the indicator group assigned to the compartment.
The customer master record contains a vehicle/customer compatibility field used to
assign compatibility groups to customers. This field is located in the shipping view
of the customer master record. The indicators within the assigned customer group
determine the attributes required in order for the assigned vehicle to be compatible.
Example: A customer needs a truck with a specific logo and a long hose to unload
the product. Since the customer requires this, and the supplier's vehicle has to
meet these requirements, and therefore the attributes must be compatible.

Vehicle and material movements
External Movements

358 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Load confirmation: the process of load confirmation records the actual quantities
and products loaded for a particular shipment.
Several different processes occur within the load confirmation step, the most
important being the entry of actual loaded quantities. Quantities in scheduling are
planned quantities and are proposed at the load confirmation stage. The planned
quantities and the quantity of the products actually loaded may have changed. You
can enter these quantities in the quantity field, or you can enter readings from
Vehicle Meters or Rack Meters. In cases where product had been previously left
on the vehicle, you can record these quantities in the shipment as prior-to-load
quantities.
The concept of intransit stock is central to the loading process. A goods movement
occurs when the product is moved into the intransit plant or storage location, at
which point Quantity Conversion Interface (QCI) parameters can be calculated
and stored. In addition, any excise duty postings which are a consequence of the
goods movement are also performed.
Delivery confirmation: the delivery confirmation process is used to confirm the
delivery of actual quantities in a bulk shipment.
Delivery confirmation is the final step in processing bulk shipments. It enables
you to enter the final quantities delivered and to process the differences between
quantities delivered and loaded. Several options exist for processing product
that has been loaded but not delivered.
Delivery confirmation must be completed for each vehicle in the shipment. The
vehicles in the shipment each have an individual status, however, it is not until
the shipment has a Shipment Status of 6 that shipment processing is complete
and the final postings are made. Delivery confirmation is also a prerequisite for
Shipment Costing.
The delivery confirmation process includes functions for handling unplanned
deliveries, and several options for dealing with undelivered materials. You can
enter delivered quantities manually or by using vehicle meters during delivery
confirmation.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 359



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 146: Vehicle and material movements

Internal Movements
Corrections at Loading and Delivery Confirmation: During the loading
confirmation process it is possible to correct quantities for shipments that have
been completely confirmed (Shipment Status 6). If you change the quantities for
a shipment that has already been completely confirmed, the system carries out
correction postings. What type of posting the system carries out, depends on the
underlying document.
Prior-to-Load Quantities: With the prior-to-load quantity, you can include a
quantity left on the vehicle from a previous shipment in the next shipment using
the same vehicle.
For example, in the delivery confirmation of a previous shipment you may
have entered a left-on-vehicle quantity. For the next shipment using that same
product and compartment, the system proposes that left-on-vehicle quantity as the
prior-to-load quantity during loading.
In the Load Bulk screen, when you select Get prior to load the the system displays
for each transport unit in the shipment both the previous shipment number and any
left-on-vehicle quantity entered during delivery confirmation.
If the product cannot be delivered to the selected destination, several options exist
in the delivery confirmation process to determine where the product should go.

360 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Left-on-Vehicle Quantities: Product can be left on the vehicle in the compartment
into which it was loaded. If product is left on a vehicle, the system proposes a
prior-to-load quantity during loading for the next shipment using the same vehicle.
The prior-to-load quantity can be used to form part of the new shipment.
Return Quantities: Product can be returned to the delivering plant if it is not
to be delivered to the intended destination. This process is carried out at the
compartment level. Product can be returned either to the delivering plant or
another plant at which the material is held. The return date and time are then
used in the material movement posting.
Rebrand: You can rebrand product upon its return to the delivering plant. This
allows product which had been rebranded during loading to be returned to the
correct tank within the delivering plant.
Unplanned Rebrands: Unplanned rebrands are used to cover cases where the
underlying document and schedule are for one product, but at the loading
confirmation stage there is insufficient product. At this point product can be
substituted. The substitution product must fulfill customer requirements just as
the first product.The scheduled product can be overwritten (rebranded) in the
Rebrand/Load bulk detail screen. Rebranding results in a material-to-material
transfer and the necessary accounting adjustments.
Planned Rebrands: Planned rebrands refer to any form of rebrand that has been
planned in advance, such as in the delivery document. Planned rebrands include
bill of materials handling within shipment processing. In this case, the main item
for which the delivery has been created is scheduled. The sub-items are then
loading confirmed in the Rebrand/lLoad bulk detail screen, enabling a variation
in the loaded quantity from that which was scheduled. Finally, the main item
is delivery confirmed.
Movement on Board
You can change information about loaded stock for shipments with a shipment
status is partially loaded. To make these changes during the delivery confirmation
process, choose Movement on board on the Create/Change Delivery Confirmation
screen. You can make the following changes to the loaded shipment: Vehicle,
Compartment, In-transit plant, In-transit storage location, Batch, Material,
Quantity It is also possible to post gains/losses during shipment and change tax
status of in-transit stock.
Prerequisites:
Before you make any changes or corrections, at least one material must have
status load confirmed. The vehicle must not have status delivery confirmed. The
shipment status must be 5 or less. All quantities you entered must be confirmed. It
is not sufficient when the loading/delivery confirmation is only saved.
Vehicle Reconciliation

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 361



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

A report can be used to reconcile left-on-vehicle and prior-to-load quantities for
a specified period of time. The report displays quantities which have been left
on the vehicle and not assigned to any subsequent shipments during loading
confirmation. You can select the vehicle to be reconciled by entering the necessary
selection criteria in the TD Vehicle reconciliation screen.

Shipment Scheduling
You can record planning, loading, and delivery information in the bulk shipment
document. The aim of transportation planning is to carry out all necessary
organizational tasks before the goods are actually shipped.
After shipment has been loaded, but before shipment has been delivered, the
materials are ìin-transit.î You can use the IS-OIL-TD to keep track of your
in-transit stock.

Figure 147: Shipment Planning, Loading and Delivery

Within the shipment header, it is possible to set up planned dates and times for
the start and end of scheduling, loading, and delivery confirmation. When the
shipment is processed and the details for loading and discharge are recorded,
the actual dates and times are recorded.

Planning Tasks
During scheduling, one or more vehicles can be assigned to the bulk shipment.
The vehicle master data can be changed at that time for a particular shipment. It is
also possible to assign drivers to vehicles at that stage.

362 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Partner (for example, service agent) details are maintained in the shipment to
calculate shipment costs.
During scheduling, it is necessary to assign underlying documents to a shipment.
The materials from the loading documents can then be assigned to compartments
of the vehicles. During compartment planning, compatibility checking is carried
out. It is possible to create shipment texts which can be accessed throughout the
bulk shipment process.
As a shipment typically is handled by a number of different people, a text
processing function can be used for inter-departmental communications regarding
the handling of the shipment.
Shipment stages are used to record the geographical aspects of a shipment. After a
route has been assigned to a vehicle and compartment planning has been carried
out, it is possible to assign underlying documents to one or more stages within
a route.
During scheduling, you can maintain information on a wide range of
transport-related services such as: scheduling an inspection at loading or
scheduling cleaning services for a ship.

Figure 148: Planning Tasks I

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 363



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

The bulk shipment functions support inbound purchases, outbound sales and
product transfers, and are integrated with the relevant SAP ECC process flows.
The underlying documents that can be assigned to and processed within a bulk
shipment include:
ï Inbound Deliveries
ï Outbound Deliveries
ï Reservations
During scheduling, documents are assigned to a shipment as load and/ or discharge
relevant. For example, if you mark a document as ìrelevant to loadingî, the
system proposes the product and quantities from the document during the loading
process. If you mark the document as ìrelevant to dischargeî, then the product
and quantities from the underlying document are defaulted during delivery
confirmation. These documents are the basis for material postings.
After assigning both documents and vehicles to a shipment, it is necessary
to specify how the vehicle should be loaded. The assignment of a product is
carried out at the compartment level for the vehicles assigned to the shipment.
Product compatibility and customer compatibility checks are carried out during
compartment planning, as well as checks on weight and volume constraints.

Figure 149: Planning Tasks II

Compartment Planning
If only one vehicle is assigned to the shipment, the system proposes that vehicle as
the one to be scheduled. Otherwise, you must enter a vehicle. The compartments
of the vehicle are represented by checkboxes next to each material line item.

364 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

If the vehicle has more than ten compartments, these can be viewed by using
the scroll buttons for horizontal scrolling. The checkboxes remain blank until
product is scheduled.
Compartment Information: for each compartment assigned to a vehicle
(represented as a check box in the Compartment Planning tabstrip) there are
boxes to represent the maximum quantity for the compartment and the balance
quantity (available capacity).

Loading Tasks
The load confirmation process records the actual quantities and products loaded
for a particular bulk shipment. Quantities in scheduling are planned quantities and
are defaulted at loading stage. Manual load confirmation is an alternative to data
entry using a Terminal Automation System (TAS).
Unplanned rebrands are used to cover cases where the sales order, delivery note
and schedule are for one product, but at the loading stage there is insufficient
product (ìdowngradingî).
The in-transit stock concept is central to the loading step. A goods movement
occurs when the product is moved into the in-transit plant or storage location, at
which point QCI parameters can be calculated and stored. In addition, any excise
duty postings that are a consequence of the goods movement are also carried out.
The underlying documents are updated with the ìrealî loaded quantities.
Following the completion of a load confirmation, a bill of lading may be produced.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 365



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 150: Loading Tasks

In-Transit Stock
A major function of bulk shipments is to keep track of in-transit stock with respect
to both quantity and value. When the goods are received, a goods receipt is posted
in the receiving (in-transit) plant or in-transit storage location (within a regular
plant) for the stock. The stock remains in the in-transit location until a transfer to
the actual receiving plant or customer is started during the delivery confirmation
step.
The assignment of the in-transit plant or storage location is specified in
customizing or in the underlying documents that are assigned to the shipment.
Whenever a goods movement occurs, dynamic quantity calculations are
required. During the load confirmation transaction, the goods movement into an
in-transit location prompts the system to make this calculation. The dialog box
containing the material default values appears for every material/storage location
combination.

366 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Figure 151: In-Transit Stock

Within the Stock Overview Report, it is possible to branch to a report in which the
loaded in-transit stock is listed by material and location. All the shipments which
have stock in that location are listed with the appropriate vehicle.
If the stock in the in-transit location differs from the stock loaded (for example,
due to manual postings), the differences will be contained in that report (report
name is ROIGSM00).

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 367



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 152: Loaded In-Transit Stock

Delivery Tasks
Delivery confirmation is the final step in processing bulk shipments. It enables
you to enter the final quantities delivered and to process the differences between
quantities delivered and loaded. The underlying documents are updated with
the 'real' delivered quantities.
During delivery confirmation, movement from in-transit stock to a destination
takes place. For that, goods movement quantities in alternative units of measure
are calculated and petroleum taxes are posted based on the tax status of the
in-transit stock and the tax status of the receiving plant or customer.

368 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Figure 153: Delivery Tasks

If the product cannot be delivered to the selected destination, several options exist
in the delivery confirmation transaction for recording where the product should go.
The product can be left on the vehicle in the compartment into which it had been
loaded. The action of leaving product on the vehicle means that the subsequent
shipment using that vehicle will have a prior-to-load quantity. The prior-to-load
quantity can be used to form part of the next shipment using that vehicle.
Product may be returned to the delivering plant if it is not to be delivered to the
intended destination. This process is carried out at the compartment level. Product
can also be rebranded upon its return to the delivering plant. This allows product
which had been rebranded during loading to be returned to the correct tank within
the delivering plant.
It is also possible to post the difference of loaded and discharged quantity as a gain
or loss. This could be due to real gains or losses or due to differences in measuring.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 369



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 154: Handling of Load-Discharge Differences

Document Flow
In order to be able to plan and execute bulk shipments, it is important that you
have an overview of planned shipment activities as well as shipments already
underway at all times. You have a number of tools at your disposal for this
purpose, for instance document flow.
Document flow presents an online history of related transactions in list form.
The document flow tracks the progress of a bulk shipments in order to be able to
respond to customer inquiries. It shows all documents associated with the bulk
shipment. You can select a document to display and then return to the document
flow. From a related document which you have selected, you can also branch
to the document flow for that document. You can also display the status of the
entire document and of each line item.

370 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Figure 155: Document Flow

Shipment Costing calculation and settlement
This component contains the functions for calculating and settling shipment
costs in transportation. The following items describe how the shipment costs are
determined in the shipment, how they are transmitted to accounting, and how they
are settled with the service provider and customer.
The shipment costs are recorded in a new system document, the shipment cost
document. From within this document, you can perform the following functions:
ï Calculate the shipment costs
ï Settle the costs with the service agent
ï Transfer the costs to FI and CO
ï Billing of shipment costs to customer (only for outbound process)

The above process is just an example. Posting goods issue, goods receipt and
transfer are not displayed.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 371



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 156: Shipment Costs in the Overall Process

During a shipment, several fees for external services are to be paid. The aim of
shipment costing is to determine the amount of each fee with respect to time,
distance, and loaded quantity for an automated settlement with the service
provider.
There are up to five elements in a shipment that can be relevant for costing:
vehicle, header, leg, load transfer point, and border crossing point. The latter
three are called stages.
The bulk shipment type controls the cost relevance.

Note: Shipment cost processing for core (LE-TRA) shipments uses the
same modules and system document. Specific features of core (LE-TRA)
shipments (e.g. shipping units) or of TD bulk shipments (for example
TD vehicle) are only supported for actual processed shipment category
(LE-TRA or IS-OIL-TD). The customizing for shipment costing is not
specific to one of the shipment categories. That is you can use the same
customizing to process core (LE-TRA) shipments and TD bulk shipments.
The shipment cost document is integrated in the document flow for SD
documents. You can call the document flow from the shipment cost
document.

Route for Shipment Costing
Route assignment

372 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

A route, as the connection between a point of depature and a destination point, can
consist of several stages. A stage can be:
ï Shipment leg, connection between a starting point and an end point
ï Load transfer point, point/location where a shipment is loaded/ unloaded or

reloaded from one means of transport to another
ï Border crossing point, point/location where a shipment crosses the border
For each stage, you can record information, such as: the responsible service agent,
default service agents, deadlines, distance, and so on.
The starting and end points of a stage are defined as transportation connection
points and can have a reference to a location (for example, plant, customer).
A route can also be the target area (for example, North America, Asia, and so on)
A shipment can contain one route per vehicle, and the route is defaulted from the
vehicle master. Stages can be deleted from a route during maintaining a shipment.

Figure 157: Route for Shipment Costing

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 373



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 158: Transportation Connection Point

Document assignment
For the calculation of the fees for a shipment, the loading and unloading point
must be assigned to each document.
The shipment type controls whether the calculation is based on loaded or unloaded
quantities.
Direct Document Stage Assignment: If a document is relevant to loading, you can
enter the corresponding loading point. If the document is relevant to discharge,
you can enter the discharge point. If the same loading point or discharge point is
used more than once in a route, then a selection pop-up appears, and the correct
stage for the document must be selected. For loading points you can enter the start
point of a leg, transfer point, or a boarder point. For discharge points you can enter
the end point of a leg, transfer point, or border point.
Automatic Document Stage Assignment: Documents can be automatically
assigned to stages by either selecting Automatic stage assignment in Customizing
for the bulk shipment type, or by selecting Auto assignment in the Document
Stage Assignment screen. The system proposes stage assignments based on the
Reference to location setting in Customizing for the transportation connection
points.
Quantity assignment

374 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

After completion of a shipment (status = 6) it is still possible to assign a route
and the relevant loading points for load relevant documents and discharge points
for all discharge relevant documents. These assignments are done on item level
for all scheduled documents.
The load relevant documents are automatically assigned to the associated vehicle.
If only one vehicle is present in the shipment, the discharge relevant documents
are also assigned automatically. In the Document Item Quantity Assignment for
the Shipment Costing discharge relevant quantities are linked to load relevant
quantities: the material quantity of a load-relevant document item is, when
possible, assigned to the first discharge-relevant document item found along the
route with the same material.
The system handles unassigned document quantities according to the following
principles: If shipment costing is based on loaded quantities, unassigned
loaded quantities (lost or left-on-vehicle quantities) are assigned to the last
discharge-relevant document item of the same material in the route. In this case
the system displays a gain/loss indicator. Unassigned discharged quantities
(gained or prior-to-load quantities) are not taken into account. If shipment costing
is based on discharged quantities the opposite is true.
An automatic document stage assignment is possible.

Partners in Bulk Shipments
The partner functions on this slide are examples. In bulk transportation, partners
are maintained on the following levels:
ï Shipment header
ï Vehicle
ï Stage
During shipment costing, these partners are used as service agents to whom
payment is due. Partner assigned at shipment header level: Partners used for the
entire shipment are maintained at the shipment header.
Partner assigned at vehicle level: You can assign partners to vehicles within a
shipment. For example, the partner could be a carrier responsible for the vehicle.
A different partner can be assigned to each vehicle in the shipment. You can
also assign carriers to vehicles in the vehicle master data so that the carrier is
automatically defaulted for the vehicle in a shipment.
Partner assigned at stage level: Partners can be assigned to stages within a
shipment. You can assign a different partner to each stage. For example, partner
assignment at stage level could be used for a customs agent at a border crossing.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 375



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Figure 159: Partners in Bulk Shipments

Shipment Cost Document
You can create shipment cost documents individually in dialog mode or using
collective processing. If you create a shipment cost document, you always directly
reference a shipment document. For each shipment document, you create exactly
one shipment cost document.
The shipment cost document consists of the shipment cost header and the
shipment cost items.
The shipment cost header contains general information on the entire document.
Status, reference, and administrative information is provided.

376 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Figure 160: Shipment Cost Document

The shipment cost items contain general data for shipment cost calculation and
settlement, such as: service agent, pricing and settlement date, tax amount, and
tax base amount. Each item has its own status for the shipment cost calculation,
account assignment and transfer functions.
The shipment cost items either refer to the shipment header, to the shipment
vehicle, or to the stage.
For example, an item that refers to the header can include insurance charges for
an additional shipment insurance. An item that refers to a shipment stage can
include load transfer costs, for example.
The function of the items of the shipment cost document is controlled through the
item category. Dependent on your settings, the system automatically calculates
the shipment costs, assigns them to an account, and transfers them to financial
accounting (SAP ERP Financials ) when you create the shipment cost document.

Shipment Cost Settlement with Service Provider
When shipment cost documents are created, the shipment cost items are generated
based on a pre-defined degree of automatic processing. This means that the
shipment cost items can be created automatically, and the shipment costs are
calculated, assigned, or transferred automatically.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 377



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

During account assignment, the system determines the correct G/L account in
Financial Accounting (SAP ERP Financials) for each shipment cost item and the
assignment for Controlling. Account assignment can be carried out at different
levels, depending on how detailed you want to track costs.
Transfer to Financial Accounting to establish accruals requires that services
performed are entered.
However, each service entry sheet is based on a purchase order. You must initially
have created this purchase order for the service agent in purchasing. During the
posting process, services performed are accepted; to establish accruals, the system
generates an accounting document in Financial Accounting. The system creates
additional subsequent documents in Accounting.
Using the credit memo procedure, also referred to as the ERS (Evaluated Receipt
Settlement) procedure, you can settle the shipment costs with the service agents
without having received invoices from them. You can choose from different
settlement periods. You transfer the calculated shipment costs to Financial
Accounting. The invoices are verified by the service agent. If the service agent
discovers variances, you can post those as subsequent debits/credits.
When you verify invoices manually, you receive an invoice from the service
agent. You manually create an invoice in the system, verify the invoice, and post
it manually.

Figure 161: Shipment Cost Settlement with Service Provider

A transfer to Financial Accounting to establish accruals requires the entry of
services performed. The corresponding sheet is automatically created by the
system during a transfer.

378 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Each service entry sheet is based on an external service order. So that the costs
can be transferred to Financial Accounting and thus settled, the system must
determine a valid service order. This external service order must have been
created in purchasing. You can create the service order monthly for the service
agent. Important criteria for the service order include: service agent, purchasing
organization, purchasing group, plant, and item category.

Figure 162: Transfer to Financial Accounting

When the system has automatically determined a valid service order, a service
entry sheet is created that refers to the service order. During the posting process,
services performed are accepted; to establish accruals, the system generates an
accounting document in Financial Accounting.
Using the credit memo procedure, you can create single credit memos, that is,
you can create a credit memo for each shipment cost item (and service agent), or
you periodically create collective credit memos by service agent. The settlement
periods for periodic settlement are flexible.

Settlement of Shipment Costs with the Customer
You can bill the customer for the actual shipment costs that were calculated with
the forwarding agent in transportation and shipment processing. These shipment
costs then appear in the billing document as an additional entry.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 379



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

Shipment costs calculated from the delivery items in the shipment cost document
are assigned directly to their corresponding billing document items. Costs based
on other factors, for example, the shipment cost items, are distributed among the
billing document items according to the proportional weight of the delivery items.

Figure 163: Settlement of Shipment Costs with the Customer

You can bill shipment costs to the customer with respect to shipment-specific
parameters (distance, tariff zone). The costs are based on effective shipment costs
that were calculated and settled with the service provider using the shipment
costing function. Shipment costs are included in the bill as a separate item.
Shipment costs can represent a considerable portion of the total cost billed to the
customer. For this reason, they are not contained in the material price but are
calculated separately by the shipper to be billed to the customer.
You could invoice the customer with shipment costs by calculating them as
surcharges in SD pricing. However, this method does not allow you to take into
account all the criteria that influence transportation (such as distance, tariff zones,
means of transport, type and number of pallets). Now, you can calculate shipment
costs taking into account all transportation-specific criteria that should be included
in the customer invoice. The shipment costs appear as an additional entry in
the customer billing document. You can use all the calculation options that are
available in the shipment cost document for settlement with the forwarding agent.
Shipment costs that are calculated in the shipment cost document using delivery
items are assigned to the corresponding billing item directly. Costs with a different
calculation basis, such as on the basis of shipment cost items, are distributed
proportionally among the billing items.

380 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Transportation and Shipment Costing

Exercise 11: Transportation Processing
Exercise Objectives
After completing this exercise, you will be able to:
ï Create Transportation Master Data to keep the vehicle fleet in the system
ï Create Bulk Shipment to schedule transportation of petroleum products to

the customer location
ï Process Bulk Shipment to arrange loading and discharging of petroleum

products.
ï Analyze the Document Flow created under the Bulk Shipment in the system.

Business Example
VOIL DE (CC1100) commissions external service agents (vendor 400018) to
deliver the petroleum products to the Customer location (3400XX - Retail West),
but is responsible for the organization and execution of bulk shipments. Although
VOIL DE (CC1100) does not have its own fleet of trucks, VOIL DE maintains
master data records for trucks in the system. This is because the company wants to
schedule shipments at the vehicle/compartment level.

Task:
When scheduling a bulk shipment, vehicle selection is based on the carrier
(vendor 400018) that VOIL DE chooses. A specific vehicle (TRAILER-XX)
normally drives the same route (2TDRDU), so the route is defaulted from the
vehicle master data into the bulk shipment. The main task of the scheduler is to
assign delivery documents items to the bulk shipment based on the departure and
destination points of the vehicle. The scheduler also assigns petroleum products to
the compartments of the vehicle.
When the truck arrives at the distribution terminal (Plant 1103) for loading,
petroleum product is filled into the compartments of the vehicle. During loading,
quantities may differ from the quantities that were scheduled.
After delivery, the delivered quantities are entered in the system. Again, the
delivered quantities could differ from the quantities scheduled or loaded. You can
post the difference as a gain or loss or as left on vehicle. You can also book the
difference in quantity as a return to the depot.
1. Your Customer (3400XX - Retail West) allocated in Dusseldorf requests for

Diesel to be delivered at the customer location. You are planning to deliver
the material item by truck from your Plant (1003) in Dresden. Create a sales
order and a delivery for DIESEL-XX for your customer's ship-to location.

Continued on next page

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 381



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

With the first step you have to create a document for the sale of product
to a Customer.

2. Create an Outbound delivery for the sales order (created at the previous step)
3. Create two transport units, a truck mover and a trailer, and assign them to

one vehicle. With the first step you have to create a truck mover.
4. You want to create a bulk shipment with schedule dates, a vehicle. You

can select the outbound delivery (from the previous step) that you want to
schedule and carry out compartment planning.

5. Loading a Bulk Shipment. After scheduling the bulk shipment, the next
step is to record the loading data in the system. Process the bulk shipment
(created on the previous step) to post the loading quantities. You can run
your Sock Overview report to check the in-transit stock loaded.

6. Delivering a Bulk Shipment. After loading your truck, the next step is to
record the delivery data in the system.

7. Analyzing the Document Flow. The document flow displays the history of
the bulk shipment documents and therefore provides information about the
status of a shipment.

vehicle master data into the bulk shipment. The main task of the scheduler is to

the compartments of the vehicle.
When the truck arrives at the distribution terminal (Plant 1103) for loading,
petroleum product is filled into the compartments of the vehicle. During loading,
quantities may differ from the quantities that were scheduled.
After delivery, the delivered quantities are entered in the system. Again, the
delivered quantities could differ from the quantities scheduled or loaded. You can
post the difference as a gain or loss or as left on vehicle. You can also book the
difference in quantity as a return to the depot.

Continued on next page

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 383



Unit 7: Secondary Distribution IOG100

With the first step you have to create a document for the sale of product
to a Customer.
a) Create a sales order:

Unit 8
Service Station Retailing

Unit Overview
This unit gives brief overview of the typical structure of SAP Service Station
Retailing (SAP SSR) solution of SAP for Oil&Gas and main components of the
SSR solution. Wet stock handling (fuels pricing, meter and dip reading, payment
cards, and invoicing the service station partner). Provides an understanding of the
SSR concept, data upload, error handling, and Customizing.

Unit Objectives
After completing this unit, you will be able to:

ï Explain what is Service Station and Convenience Retailing (SSCR) solution
ï Which parties are involved in the Service Station and Convenience Retailing

(SSCR) business?
ï Which data is transmitted from and to the parties involved?
ï Explain the master data concept
ï Create a business location
ï Create master data at the general level
ï Assign a material handling group and a processing profile to a location
ï Create master data at the business type level
ï Explain the flexibility of pricing within SSR
ï Maintain relevant pricing master data
ï Maintain prices based on the competitor prices
ï Describe network and group pricing
ï Explain the reports on fuels pricing.
ï Describe the meter reading process
ï Maintain meter reading master data
ï Describe the performed checks during the upload process
ï Explain the meter reading error maintenance
ï Perform meter reading maintenance
ï Describe the dip reading process
ï Maintain storage object master data

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 399



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

ï Describe the checks during upload process
ï Explain the dip reading error maintenance
ï Post stock corrections
ï Execute and control the payment card process including complaint processing

ï Explain the splitting concept
ï Display, change, and create payment card transactions
ï Describe clearing house and fleet card company settlement

400 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain fuel sales process, different business types which
supported by SSCR solution. Also lesson gives you an overview on master data
for Service Stations. Depending on how the station business is organized, an
oil company can deal with service station partners, clearing houses and fleet
card companies.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain what is Service Station and Convenience Retailing (SSCR) solution
ï Which parties are involved in the Service Station and Convenience Retailing

(SSCR) business?
ï Which data is transmitted from and to the parties involved?
ï Explain the master data concept
ï Create a business location
ï Create master data at the general level
ï Assign a material handling group and a processing profile to a location
ï Create master data at the business type level

Business Example
German Oil Company (VOIL DE) delivers fuel to the service stations. Fuel sold
at service stations is owned by VOIL DE. Service station partners sell VOIL
DE products and their own products. You work in the VOIL DE Companyís
retail network department. You wish to register one new company owned and
dealer operated service station in your ERP System. You do this by creating a new
location master record. The service station partner acts as an agent and all fuels
stocks remain the property of your company until they are sold to consumers. As
a prerequisite for the processes used for invoicing the dealer using sales meter
readings and updating book stock, you need to register the locationís tanks and
sales meter devices and link the partner to your location.

Supply Chain Overview
The handling of the dry stock and wet stock supply chains is based on different
requirements. The replenishment of fuels is handled in a different way than the
replenishment of shop products.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 401



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 164: Supply Chain Overview

SAP for Oil&Gas enables the customer to manage the entire supply chain, from
Exploration and Production to Service Station Retailing. Handling of the dry stock
supply chain and wet stock supply chain are the key processes in Service Station
and Convenience Retailing (SSCR).

SSR Functions In SAP for Oil&Gas
SSR is a module of SAP for Oil&Gas. SSR is the fuels retailing functionality for
the management of wet stocks and payment card handling at a service station.

402 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Figure 165: Overview: SSR Functions In SAP for Oil&GAS

The following functions for wet stock handling are available:
ï Meter reading transmission
ï Dip reading transmission
ï Competitor prices upload
ï Location master data display
ï Payment cards management

SSCR Business Types
The relationship between the oil company and service stations can be based on
different concepts:
ï COCO Company owned / company operated
ï CODO Company owned / dealer operated
ï DODO Dealer owned / dealer operated

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 403



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 166: SSCR Business Types

The oil company is the owner of the products sold at the service stations, such as
fuels and lubes. The oil company is responsible for:
ï Uploading sales information on these products. This is done once or several

times a day.
ï Pricing the products and downloading the prices to the service stations.
ï Collecting the payment card transactions centrally for settlement with the

service station partner and the clearing houses.
In some cases, the service station partner is owner of other products (convenience
store products) sold at the service station, such as magazines, beverages, sweets,
and accessories for cars. The service station partner is responsible for:
ï Transmission of competitor prices whenever they change.
ï Correct handling (that is, black list check or online authorization of payment

card transactions).
ï Transmission of dip readings in the event of technical problems.

Data Exchange Overview
SSCR is designed to handle large volumes of data transmitted from one party to
another. Some data is exchanged periodically, on a regular basis, while other data
transmissions are triggered by an event.

404 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Figure 167: Data Exchange Overview

Periodically transmitted data includes:
ï Payment card transactions sent daily from the service station to the oil

company.
ï Meter readings and dip readings sent daily or weekly from the service station

to the oil company.
ï Credit card transactions sent daily from the oil company to the credit card

clearing house.
ï Fleet card transactions sent (the frequency depends on the fleet card

company) from the oil company to fleet card companies.
Data transmitted after a user-initiated event:
ï Competitor prices sent from the service station to the oil company
ï New prices sent from the oil company to the service station
ï Black list sent from the clearing houses to the oil company

Technical Concepts
SSR allows direct communication between the oil company system and the
point-of-sale (POS) system or an integration system for data exchange between oil
company and service station systems.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 405



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 168: Technical Concepts

To enable the transfer of data between company headquarters and business
locations in the retail network, interfaces based on Business Application
Programming Interface (BAPI) technology have been developed. This allows
external systems to access data in the SAP for Oil&Gas system synchronously.
Intermediate document (IDoc) technology provides asynchronous data access in
an additional asynchronous layer around the BAPI interfaces.

406 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Master Data

Figure 169: Master Data

Defining a business location
Explanation of the following concepts:
ï Location type
ï Business type
ï Processing profile
ï Material handling group
ï Master data at the general level
ï Master data at the business type level

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 407



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Location types

Figure 170: Location types

The location type is the primary means of categorizing business locations. You
therefore have to select a location type when you create a business location master
record. The business location type typically describes the:
ï Function of the business location (for example, depot or service station).
ï Nature of the relationship of the business location to your own organization

(for example, company-owned, dealer-operated service station or dealer-
owned, dealer-operated service station).

You use this categorization to control which processing parameters apply to the
business location, and to control the screen output for maintaining and displaying
master data.

Business Type
The business type is used to identify the different types of business in the SSR
environment. These can include, for example, Fuels or Convenience store.

408 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Figure 171: Business Type

You can assign a retail network business type to a business location to supplement
the control of screen output and processing options provided by the business
location type.
Specifically, the assignment of a business type to a location allows you to:
ï Simplify maintenance and display of business location master data by linking

screen output to the type of business
ï Control object links to align objects with the type of business
ï Set user authorization to display and maintain master data at business type

level
For example, if you require bulk fuel processing functions for a location, you can
assign the corresponding business type to that business location. You can then
authorize display and maintenance of fuel-related business location master data
to those responsible for this business.
By accessing the business location master using that business type, employees can
then display or maintain data relating to the fuels business (for example, meter
data, competitor list, and price control data.). If further lines of business, such as
convenience store retailing, are carried out at the location, you can assign the
corresponding business types to enable the appropriate processing and master data
maintenance activities.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 409



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Location Master Data at General Level
The following business location master data can be displayed and maintained at
the general level:

410 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Figure 172: Location Master Data at General Level

ï Address, history, and object status information.
ï Organization ñ Location area assignment of persons responsible at

headquarters for a region, area or sub-area.
ï Partner role assignments ñ When you assign a partner to a location, you

define both a location partner role type and a start time. This assignment to a
customer master record allows the SD billing process to bill your process.

ï Payment card data ñ Including the payment cards accepted at the location
and related information.

ï Storage object characteristics (SOC) ñ The dimensions and other attributes
that may influence logistical processes associated with storage objects.

ï Site control parameters (SCP) ñ Site-specific parameters that influence bulk
replenishment planning.

ï Object links ñ Each business location can be linked to other application
objects in your system. You can assign objects (plant, storage location, profit
center, cost center) to each business location.

ï Control data ñ The process control group controls the execution of the daily
claim, meter reading, and invoicing processes for a business location. The
conversion group determines how the system converts field values received
through interfaces to external systems.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 411



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Location Master Data at Business Type Level
As certain business location master data is related to the type of business carried
out at a business location, you must enter such business-specific data at the
business type level.

Figure 173: Location Master Data at Business Type Level

The following business location master data can be displayed and maintained at
the business type level:
ï Competitor locations
ï Sales meters
ï Object links
ï Control data, such as:

ñ Material handling group
ñ Processing profile
ñ Price control groups
ñ Invoicing block indicator (used to stop automatic invoicing for this

location, for example, during a changeover of partner)
ï Status, such as the location status for the fuels business
ï Long texts

Material Handling Group
The material handling group is set up as master data and is linked to a location.

412 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Fuel Management

Figure 174: Material Handling Group

You assign material handling groups to business locations to enable the system to
determine the materials that are relevant for processing at a location, and:
ï Whether uploaded meter readings should be used to create invoicing

documents
ï Whether a material is owned by the oil company
ï Whether the upload of meter readings or POS data creates goods movements

for a material
ï Whether a bill of material explosion should occur when goods movements

are created for the material
Example: A material handling group may include a fuel product for which billing
documents are to be created, using meter readings to calculate invoiced amounts.
If you assign this material handling group to a business location, and a process
control group that includes the processes required to enable billing of the service
station partner, the system can create billing documents for sales of this material
when the service station partner invoicing process runs.

Processing Profile
Most processes in the service station retailing business run automatically in the
background. The processing profile is a flexible tool that contains parameters for
automatic processing and for settlement with service station partners.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 413



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 175: Processing Profile

The processing profile is defined in Customizing and is assigned to a location.
The processing profile specifies default parameters for processing. These relate to:
ï Partner role (relevant for invoicing)
ï Meter reading (sales unit, price change tolerance, meter reading calendar

schedule)
ï Dip reading (tolerance level for warning and error messages during

adjustment of logical and physical stock)
ï Invoicing (invoicing calendar, payment method, partner bank type)
ï Logistics documents (parameters such as temperature and density)
