2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 429



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Lesson: Service Station Retailing
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain how to handle complex pricing structure within the
SSCR retail network. Display and maintain target prices at the location level for
defined groups of materials and material /service type combinations and track
price changes.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Explain the flexibility of pricing within SSR
ï Maintain relevant pricing master data
ï Maintain prices based on the competitor prices
ï Describe network and group pricing
ï Explain the reports on fuels pricing.

Business Example
You work in the VOIL DE Companyís retail network department. You are
responsible for fuels pricing. You receive competitor prices for the fuels sold at
competitor locations. You want to enter these prices and have the system propose
new target prices for your own station. You change the prices for the service
station.
In addition to maintaining and updating prices based on individual locations,
location clusters, and competitors, network/group price update also allows
free-form price changes to be made to any single one or set of locations the
user selects.

Fuels Pricing ñ Process Overview
This graphic shows an overview of the business processes involved in pricing
management.

430 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Retailing

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 431



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 176: Fuels Pricing - Process Overview

ï Before the fuels pricing process starts, some prerequisites have to be
considered. At the oil company, service station data is maintained in location
master records. Specific data that relates to pricing maintenance includes:
definition of the location cluster that the station belongs to (optional),
material price differences group, service type differences group, and
competitors. In addition, price differences between materials, service types,
competitors, and locations are maintained. Standard pricing and network
pricing are also maintained at the oil company.

ï Using intermediate documents (IDocs), service stations send actual prices
(which are transmitted with the regular meter readings) and competitors' fuel
prices to the ERP System. The information may first be integrated into
a separate system at the oil company and then sent to the ERP System, or
the individual stations may send data directly to the ERP System. For those
locations that are not electronically linked to head office, these prices can be
entered into R/3 manually.

ï Price checks compare the inbound actual prices with the target prices in
R/3, to see if they are the same or if they fall within the defined acceptable
tolerance.

ï Competitor prices are uploaded to the pricing table and are used as the basis
for price proposals. Two dimensional pricing proposals based on the user's
entries are then made. The user can copy and save the proposals, which
then become target prices.

ï Finally, the new target prices are sent to the service stations' POS system
using IDocs.

Price Upload / Download
SSR offers automatic inbound and outbound processing of prices between the oil
company and the service stations using IDocs. SSR also offers inbound processing
using the SSR Store.

432 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Retailing

Figure 177: Price Upload / Download

To update service station target prices, you create and send an IDoc to an external
system. You can choose from the following:
ï A general update
ï An update of prices that have changed
ï You can use job control to update prices automatically.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 433



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Price Differences ñ Material

Figure 178: Price Differences - Material

ï Within material and service type price difference groups you can maintain
differences in relation to the defined reference material and service type.
When you copy a price using the two-dimensional price maintenance tool,
the difference is included in the new price proposal.

ï Here, regular gasoline is used as the basis for the price differences. All
other materials have their price differences based on the price for regular
gasoline. For each material differences pricing group, a different referential
material within the group can be maintained, but only one from each group
can serve as the reference.

434 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Retailing

Price Differences ñ Service Type

Figure 179: Price Differences - Service Type

ï This example shows price differences by service type. Here, self service
is the basis for the price differences. All other service types have their
price differences based on the price for self service. For each service type
differences pricing group, a different service type within the group can be
maintained, but only one from each group can serve as the reference.

Price Differences: Location Cluster
A location cluster is a group of service stations that share characteristics that allow
them to be grouped together for pricing purposes. For example, a cluster may
include all locations within a region, or locations that share the same competitors.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 435



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 180: Price Differences: Location Cluster

ï SSR provides a price maintenance screen that allows you to display and
maintain prices for a location and copy changes for the location to the other
locations in the cluster, applying any differences defined in pricing master
data maintenance.

ï You can create a group of locations with price differences based on
comparisons between locations, at a general and material and service type
level.

436 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Retailing

Price Differences ñ Competitors

Figure 181: Price Differences - Competitors

ï You define differences between prices at your location and its competitors to
enable the two-dimensional price maintenance tool to propose prices based
on a fixed offset between your prices and those of your competitors.

ï You can maintain differences at a general level for all materials or for each
material sold at your location.

ï Business background: in general you assign several competitors to one
location of your cluster. Those competitors are in competition with the
whole cluster.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 437



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Price Differences ñ Competitors and Material

Figure 182: Price Differences - Competitors and Material

438 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Retailing

Competitor Pricing ñ Business Case

Figure 183: Competitor Pricing - Business Case

ï Each service station partner is obliged to monitor and check prices of
competitors in the vicinity of its own location. New competitor prices are sent
to the oil company using the IDocs (ALE), manual entry, or another medium.

ï At the oil company, new prices are calculated using the two-dimensional
pricing tool and the competitor prices sent.

ï New prices are then sent back to the service stations using IDocs, or in some
cases using fax or telephone.

Competitor Pricing ñ Price Calculation
SSR provides a price maintenance screen that allows you to display and maintain
prices at competitor locations and copy these to your locations, applying any
differences defined in pricing master data maintenance.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 439



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 184: Competitor Pricing - Price Calculation

ï In this example, competitor differences are maintained on material level so
the new fuels prices for your own location show differences of:
ñ EUR -0.01 for Regular-SSR
ñ EUR -0.01 for Super-SSR
ñ EUR -0.01 for Midgrade-SSR
ñ EUR -0.02 for Diesel-SSR

Network and Group Pricing
In addition to maintaining and updating prices based on individual locations,
location clusters, and competitors, you can use a network or group price update
for widespread and free-form price changes for any single location or a set of
locations that the user selects. You can change any prices for any material and
location combination selected.

440 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Service Station Retailing

Figure 185: Network and Group Pricing

ï This tool is useful where there is a standard price change for all stations
within a company, country, region, or city, for example, for one or more
materials and/or service types. An example would be a price rise of EUR
0.06/liter due to higher taxes on fuels.

ï The tool is also useful for making individual changes to materials at locations
where the price change is independent of the pricing differences defined for
a material and service type, location cluster, or competitor.

ï In the price change proposal, you can specify price ranges in which the new
price must fall before it is accepted.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 441



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Reports on Fuels Pricing (1)

ï Price History Report
ñ Allows you to view price changes within a specified period, and shows

you whether actual prices received with meter readings are different
from the valid target price.

ï Price Check Report
ñ Allows you to view price changes within a specified period, and shows

you whether the last actual prices received with price upload were
different from the valid target price.

ï Network Prices at a Special Time
ñ Allows you to view prices at a specified date and time across the whole

network (all locations, all materials, all service types).
ï Network Price Changes

ñ Allows you to view the number of price changes for a specific period
for the whole network.

Reports on Fuels Pricing (2)

ï Network Average Price By Date
ñ Allows you to view network average prices by date.

ï Network Average Price By Location
ñ Allows you to view network average price by location.

ï Price Change For Location Network
ñ Allows you to view prices that have changed for a given location

network.

Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain how the Oil companies use sales meter readings to
calculate fuel sales volumes and dip readings to calculate stock levels of bulk fuels
within the service station network. You also will see how to use that data to correct
current stock levels and run billing process based on meter reading to calculate the
amount to claim from service station partners for fuel sold at a location.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Describe the meter reading process
ï Maintain meter reading master data
ï Describe the performed checks during the upload process
ï Explain the meter reading error maintenance
ï Perform meter reading maintenance
ï Describe the dip reading process
ï Maintain storage object master data
ï Describe the checks during upload process
ï Explain the dip reading error maintenance
ï Post stock corrections

Business Example
You work in the VOIL DE Companyís retail network department. You will:
ï Receive meter reading data from the service station, which must be checked

and uploaded
ï Update meter readings manually
ï Check and release meter reading errors
ï Reprocess the remaining meter readings
ï Create subsequent material movements to update stock levels
ï Receive dip reading data from the service stations which must be uploaded

and checked
ï Process the errors contained in the data and update the dip readings history
ï Analyze the deviation between physical and book stocks to generate

correcting material movements
ï Post the material movements

458 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Meter Reading Process Overview
From the meter readings, quantities of fuel sold are calculated and used as the
basis for recording material movements, stock levels, and service station partner
(SSP) invoicing.

Figure 186: Meter Reading Process Overview

ï Business location master data maintenance: Each business location has
meters assigned to it according to material or material and service type.

ï Meter readings upload: Meter readings with the corresponding sales prices
are uploaded electronically from the service station through an integration
system or from individual service stations. If service stations have no
electronic link to the oil company, the meter reading data can be transmitted
using the SSR Store. Mandatory checks and user-defined checks are
performed on the readings.

ï All correct and reprocessed meter readings are then uploaded to the meter
reading history table and are assigned a link number to link the business
transaction to the subsequent processes.

Master Data Maintenance
ï You can assign the meter access profile and maintain the parameters of each

meter in the business location master data screen for meter assignments.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 459



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 187: Master Data Maintenance

ï The meter access profile selected under the meter definition defines the
criteria used to differentiate the incoming meter readings, for example, by
date, time, or material.

ï The parameter you define can include the length (number of digits) in the
meter reading, conversion factor, volume measure, meter serial number,
and model number. If a location changes or adds meters, you can define a
validity period to the meters. You can also specify whether more than one
meter is being accessed for each material at a location.

Periodic Upload and Checks of Meter Reading Data
When the meter reading data is uploaded, the system carries out mandatory and
user-defined checks.

460 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Figure 188: Periodic Upload and Checks of Meter Reading Data

ï User-defined checks prevent further processing of meter readings until you
review the data and then release it for reprocessing. User-defined check are
maintained in Customizing using Business Add-Ins (BAdIs).

ï The mandatory check location basic data consists of a set of basic checks,
such as:
ñ Do the locations exist?
ñ Does the station exists for the business type?
ñ Are meters linked to the location?

Meter Reading Process Overview ñ Errors
This process overview shows uploaded meter readings with errors.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 461



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 189: Meter Reading Process Overview - Errors

ï Errors can be reprocessed in a background process that rechecks the
erroneous meter readings. This is useful, for example, when the oil company
receives incomplete meter readings (only 4 of 5 meters) and the missing
meter readings are transmitted with the next upload. The background process
can process the complete meter readings.

ï Manual meter reading error maintenance is a dialog process that allows you
to analyze, release, delete, and correct the meter readings that have not been
processed. You can update or simulate the non-processed meter readings.

ï All correct and reprocessed meter readings are then uploaded to the meter
reading history table and are assigned a link number to link the business
transaction to the subsequent processes.

ï From the meter readings, quantities of fuel sold are calculated and used as
the basis for recording material movements, stock levels, and SSP invoicing.

ï Authorized users can clear the last meter reading received from the history
table. This may be necessary, for example, if the same readings have been
received twice, if there is an error with the upload, or if the previous dayís
upload was missed. This allows the previous dayís meter reading to be
re-uploaded.

462 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Meter Reading Error Maintenance

Figure 190: Meter Reading Error Maintenance

ï All readings that meet one or more criteria defined in the mandatory or
user-defined checks are rejected and require user action. There are three
options available for each rejected reading:
ñ Reprocess
ñ Release (for user-defined checks)
ñ Delete

ï The error maintenance screen allows you to review the rejected meter
readings and to drill down for further detail to determine the cause of the
rejected reading.

ï Errors from the mandatory checks are assigned a red light.
ï Errors from the user-defined checks are assigned either a yellow light (for

blocking type errors) or a red light (for all other errors).
ï The status lights indicate the following:

ñ Yellow light errors can be either deleted or released.
ñ Red light errors can either be reprocessed (once the cause of the

problem has been fixed, for example, with Customizing or master
data errors) or they can be deleted.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 463



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Meter Reading Process Overview ñ Manual

Figure 191: Meter Reading Process Overview - Manual

ï If meter readings cannot be received from service stations through the
interface for meter reading upload, you can enter meter readings manually.

ï The system processes manually entered readings in the same way as meter
readings uploaded from service stations.

ï All correct and reprocessed meter readings are then uploaded to the meter
reading history table and are assigned a link number to link the business
transaction to the subsequent processes.

ï From the meter readings, quantities of fuel sold are calculated and used as
the basis for recording material movements, stock levels, and SSP invoicing.

Dip Reading ñ Process Overview
Oil companies use dip readings to get the physical stock levels of bulk fuels within
the service station network. You can use this data to correct the logical book
stock levels.

464 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Figure 192: Dip Reading - Process Overview

ï Dip readings are received electronically from the service station, through an
integration system or from individual service stations.

ï All correct and reprocessed dip readings are then uploaded to the dip reading
history table.

ï Post stock corrections: The physical inventory, represented by incoming
dip readings, is compared with logical inventory, which is calculated using
standard material movements. If there are any differences, you can post the
differences with or without changing them into the document base table
(DBT).

ï Material movements: You can define and generate material movements
out of the DBT to adjust the differences between the logical stocks and the
dip readings.

Storage Object Characteristics
Storage object characteristics (SOC) are attributes that may influence logistical
processes associated with storage objects.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 465



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 193: Storage Object Characteristics

ï Bulk distribution requirements planning (BDRP) master data objects appear
in the system as sub-objects of other master data objects.

ï For each storage object, there are screens for basic specifications, time
dependent assignments, maintenance data and linear/ volumetric conversion
data.

466 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Master Data Maintenance

Figure 194: Master Data Maintenance

ï In the business location master data, general level, the following are assigned:
ñ The storage objects (tanks) are assigned to the locations
ñ The materials are assigned to the objects, as well as details about the

objects themselves.
ñ Further details are added for each tank including the material,

dimensions, and tank number.
ï A link to plant maintenance is also provided.

Checks During Dip Reading Upload
The system carries out the checks configured for the dip readings upload process.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 467



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 195: Checks During Dip Reading Upload

ï The mandatory and user-defined checks are performed when the dip reading
data is uploaded.

ï In Customizing, you can define your own checks as a control before the dip
reading data is processed. User-defined checks prevent further processing
of dip readings that meet the check criteria. You can first review the data
and then release it for reprocessing.

Dip Reading ñ Process Overview (2)
SSR allows you to process dip readings that have been rejected because they have
failed the defined plausibility checks.

468 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Figure 196: Dip Reading - Process Overview (2)

ï The errors can be reprocessed by a background process that re-checks the
erroneous dip readings.

ï Manual dip readings errors maintenance: This is a dialog process that allows
you to analyze, authorize, delete, and correct the dip readings that have
not been processed. It is possible to update or simulate the non processed
dip readings.

ï All correct and reprocessed dip readings are then uploaded to the dip reading
history table.

ï Post stock corrections: The physical inventory, represented by incoming
dip readings, is compared with the logical inventory, which is calculated
using standard material movements. If there are any differences, you can
post the differences with or without changing them into the document base
table (DBT).

ï Material movements: You can define and generate material movements
out of the DBT to adjust the differences between the logical stocks and the
dip readings.

ï Dip readings clearing: You can delete dip readings received from the
location in the past. This is only possible for dip readings not already used
to create goods movements.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 469



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Dip Reading Error Maintenance

Figure 197: Dip Reading Error Maintenance

ï All dip readings that meet one or more criteria defined in the mandatory or
user-defined checks will be rejected and will require user intervention. You
have three options available for each rejected reading:
ñ Reprocess
ñ Release (user-defined checks)
ñ Delete

ï The error maintenance screen allows you to review the rejected meter
readings and to drill down for further detail to determine the cause of the
rejected reading.

ï Errors from the mandatory checks are assigned a red light.
ï Errors from the user-defined checks are assigned either a yellow light (for

blocking type errors) or a red light (for all other errors).
ï The status lights indicate the following:

ñ Yellow light errors can be either deleted or released.
ñ Red light errors can either be reprocessed (once the cause of the

problem has been fixed, for example, with Customizing or master
data errors) or they can be deleted.

470 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Dip Reading ñ Process Overview (3)
In case of problems during the automatic transmission of the dip readings, the
service station partner can send the dip reading using fax or telephone.

Figure 198: Dip Reading - Process Overview (3)

ï If the dips are received using fax or telephone, the data has to be created
manually in the SAP system. For this purpose, the dip readings maintenance
function is used. It is a dialog process to update the dip readings manually.

ï All correct dip readings are then uploaded to the dip reading history table.
ï Post stock corrections and material movements are handled as in Process

Overview.

Stock Adjustment
You use dip readings received from business locations to determine the current
level of bulk fuel stocks held at those locations.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 471



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Figure 199: Stock Adjustment

ï If there is a difference between the physical and book stock level, which the
system determines from goods movements to and from the storage location,
you can save a stock adjustment to:
ñ Correct current stock levels in inventory management
ñ Create a goods movement based on dip readings

Fuels Dip Reading ñ Stock Report
The fuels dip reading stock report gives an overview of dip readings that were
different from the relative stock level at the time that they were received.

472 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Meter and Dip Reading Management

Figure 200: Fuels Dip Reading - Stock Report

ï You can display:
ñ A status indicator. This has three possible colors:

ï Green indicates that the difference is less than the warning tolerance.
ï Yellow indicates that the difference is greater than the warning
tolerance but less than the error tolerance.
ï Red indicates that the difference is greater than the error tolerance.

ï These tolerances are assigned to the processing profile in Customizing.
ï Stock level data:

ñ Dip reading (physical stock)
ñ Relative (book) stock level at the time that the dip reading was received
ñ Difference between dip reading and book stock level
ñ Percentage deviation of dip reading from relative stock level, for

instance, for the last 30 days of sales flow. The parameters for the
percentage calculation are defined in a BAdI.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 473



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Every dip reading is qualified with a status based on the difference between

ï Warning tolerance for gains

ï Warning tolerance for losses
ï Error tolerance for losses
The status light is:
Green when the deviation is less than the warning tolerance.
Yellow when the deviation is greater than the warning tolerance but less
than the error tolerance.
Red when the deviation is greater than the error tolerance. A minus sign
indicates a loss.
Otherwise the deviation is a gain.

Answer: The access profile is defined in: IMG→ Industry Solution Oil&Gas
(Downstream)→ SSR→ Fuels Processing→ Process configuration→
Define access profile
You link the business location to a meter access profile to:
1. Assign meters to a specific object combination (access type)
2. Define whether key duplicates are allowed or not for the selected

access type (key type).
3. Define whether the meter assignments are date and/or time dependent

(Date/time relevance)
2. Where are the defaults for the meter reading process defined?

Which end period meter event type is defaulted?
Answer: The defaults for the meter reading process are defined in the
processing profile. IMG Industry Solution Oil&Gas (Downstream)→ SSR
→ Basic settings→ Define Processing profile
The End period meter event type A is defaulted. This means that we expect a
meter reading of a normal sales flow from the service stations.
The time frame for the incoming end period meter reading is from 20:00 to
04:00.

Task 8:

to check the Customizing settings for the material documents within your ERP
System.
1. Where is the logistics document schema for the MM documents for meter

and dip readings defined?
What is defined by the logistics document schema?
Which logistic document type is defaulted?
Answer: The logistics document schema for the MM documents for
meter and dip readings is defined in: IMG→ Industry Solution Oil&Gas
(Downstream)→ SSR→ Fuels Processing→ Logistics document creation
→ Logistics document schema→ Define document schema
The logistics document schema defines the:
ï Logistics document type
ï Movement types to be used for material document creation
ï Fields to be filled for the document creation process (the document

key field indicates whether a new document or a new line is created
in a document)

The logistic document type ìWAî for goods issue is defaulted.
2. How is the logistic document definition schema determined?

Where is the location indicator for the logistics document schema derived
from?
Answer: The logistic document definition schema is determined in: IMG
→ Industry Solution Oil&Gas (Downstream)→ SSR→ Fuels Processing
→ Logistics document creation→ Logistics document schema→ Assign
document schema
The logistics document schema is assigned to the location indicator and to
the process. You can assign each logistics document schema to more than
one location indicator/process combination.
The process derives the location indicator from processing profile (Logistic
documents section) of the location. It uses this indicator to derive the
logistics document schema.

500 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner
Invoicing
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain how the oil companies handle service station payment
cards transactions, settle with clearing houses on behalf of service station partners
and with fleet card companies directly, invoice service station partners and reverse
service station partner billing documents.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Execute and control the payment card process including complaint processing
ï Explain the master data ñ three level concept
ï Describe the transaction upload process
ï Explain the splitting concept
ï Display, change, and create payment card transactions
ï Describe clearing house and fleet card company settlement
ï Create the service station partner invoice
ï Reverse the service station partner invoice
ï Analyze the service station partner invoice.

Business Example
The VOIL DE Company is responsible for maintaining payment card master
data and checking the uploaded payment card transaction data from the business
locations. After the upload the data should be checked with a report. Errors
during the upload can be corrected using a transaction. If the connection to a
service station breaks down, the payment card transactions can be manually
entered into the ERP System. The VOIL DE Company settles with clearing
houses and fleet card companies on behalf of the service station partners. For
company owned/dealer operated service stations it is usual to invoice the service
station partner for the cash sales of oil company owned products. The service
station partner receives payment from the customer for the sale of fuels and is
then invoiced by the oil company for the quantity sold. Payment card handling is
a service provided by the oil company to the partner. The oil company receives
the payment card transactions through the POS system and will deal with the
clearing houses on the partnerís behalf. Fleet card companies are invoiced as
normal customers by the oil company.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 501



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Payment Cards Overview

Figure 201: Payment Cards Overview

ï An end-customer purchases a product or a service at the service station
and wants to pay with a payment card, such as a fleet-card or credit-card
(arrow 1).

ï At the cashier, an authorization check is performed (arrow 2).
ï The black list may be sent from the clearing house to the oil company and

then distributed to the service stations. The black list is stored at the service
station or at the clearing house. For Eurocheque (EC) card transactions,
an online connection is made to the clearing house and the transaction is
checked. A new black list is sent by the clearing house regularly (a new list
is sent every month with corrections every week) to the oil companies.

ï If the result of the authorization is positive (arrow 3), the end customer
receives the products or services (arrow 4).

502 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Business Background ñ Upload and Settlement

Figure 202: Business Background - Upload and Settlement

ï All the payment card sales information (individual transaction data) is sent
periodically (daily) from the service station to the SAP ERP System of the
oil company (arrow 5).

ï At settlement time, the individual transaction data is sent from the ERP
System to the clearing house (arrow 6).

ï The clearing house validates the card transaction. Some clearing houses send
a summary of the settlement data to the oil company (arrow 7).

ï The clearing house then pays the purchase amount minus the clearing house
fee to the oil companyís bank account (arrow 8).

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 503



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Business Background ñ SSP Invoicing

Figure 203: Background - SSP Invoicing

ï The oil company sends an invoice to the service station partner for the sales
of oil company owned products by cash (arrow 9 ).

ï The oil company sends an payment request (arrow 10 ) to get the money
from the service station partners bank/account. (Usually the oil company has
direct access to the bank account of the service station partner).

ï The actual money transfer from the service station bank/account to the oil
companyís bank/account is shown by arrows 11 and 12.

The Clearing House as a New Object
The clearing house object is the central repository for all the information required
to execute clearing house and fleet card company settlement, and is used in the
payment card settlement processes. Different settlement runs are used for each
clearing house and payment card type combination.

504 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Figure 204: The Clearing House as a New Object

You can define the following for the clearing house object:
ï Customer master (SD) data.

Customer master data is used for SD documents (fee billing document, fleet
card company invoice) to link the ìSold-toî partner role and the sales area.

ï Financial accounting (FI) data.
Accounts that are used for automatic processing during the settlement run
and company code has to be assigned to each clearing house object. In the
case of credit card and bank debit card (such as EC cards) clearing houses,
you specify which CH receivables account and which cash clearing account
(both are general ledger accounts) are to be used in the settlement process.
Fleet card company settlement is not on the level of general ledger accounts.
During the settlement process, a SD invoice is created for the customer that
is linked to the clearing house object.

ï Controlling (CO) data.
You assign a CO distribution cycle to each clearing house so that the costs
associated with payment card handling can be distributed correctly.

ï Central address master data.
Central address data is used to store information about contacts.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 505



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Three Level Payment Card Concept
Payment card master data, such as card type and accepted payment card types, is
defined at three levels.

Figure 205: Three Level Payment Card Concept

ï At R/3 client level, there is a general definition for payment card types.
ï As settings for a payment card type often vary from country to country, card

types are further defined at company code level. This allows you to create the
same payment card type with different settings in different company codes.
Additional settings can also be made at the company code level, for example,
for purchase limits, material restrictions, and splitting indicators.

ï At the business location level, you can maintain the following data:
ñ Time frame that defines when the payment card type is accepted.
ñ Reason code explaining why the card type is temporarily not accepted.
ñ Amounts for when a purchase should be checked against a black list or

directly with the clearing house that is specific to the location.
ñ Location of the black list (required for complaint processing).

Payment Card Transaction Upload
Payment card transactions are uploaded from the service stations to the oil
company. This makes it possible to send the transaction data in several smaller
incoming IDocs.

506 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Figure 206: Payment Card Transaction Upload

After data is received at the oil company, the following checks and processes are
or can be started:
ï Basic checks such as checking that the card type is specified. Process control

checks are also performed at this time.
ï Validations based on different criteria defined by the oil company are also

performed.
ï If splitting is relevant, then split processing is executed and the split result is

stored with the transaction.
ï The clearing house object is determined, in order to prepare the transaction

for the settlement.
ï Finally, the process status is updated as ìfinished successfullyî.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 507



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Payment Card Splitting

Figure 207: Payment Card Splitting

In addition to normal clearing house determination using the condition technique,
it is also possible to use the payment card splitting function to determine a clearing
house based on specific splitting criteria. In some European countries, bank debit
cards can be settled with more than one clearing house, where for instance, the
clearing house is determined based on the card number and/or bank number.
The splitting criteria are customer definable, and are used during processing in the
splitting routine to evaluate the transaction, and obtain a splitting result.
Examples of splitting criteria are bank number, payment card number, business
location number and/or a fixed transaction amount.
The splitting result is stored in the detailed transaction file (DTF) and specifies the
result of the splitting processing, thus determining the clearing house to where
the transaction should be settled and/or transmitted.

508 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Manual Creation of Payment Card Transactions

Figure 208: Manual Creation of Payment Card Transactions

If the payment card transactions data cannot be sent automatically, for example,
because there is a failure of the POS system, payment card transaction data can be
created manually.
In this case, the service station partner sends the POS data using fax, mail, or any
other method to the oil company. At the oil company, the data has to be entered
manually into the SAP ERP System.
All functions or checks that are performed during normal upload are also carried
out.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 509



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Service Station Partner Invoicing ñ Overview

Figure 209: Service Station Partner Invoicing - Overview

SSR settlement and invoicing functionality allows an oil company to:
ï Create the billing documents required to invoice service station partners on

the following bases:
ñ Meter readings from pumps and payment card transactions received

from the POS system, or system.
ñ Cash information and payment card transactions received from the POS.

ï Create the billing documents required to settle cash and credit card
transactions with the service station partners.

ï Create the billing documents required to settle fleet card transactions with
the service station partners.

510 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Created Documents ñ Cash and Credit Cards

Figure 210: Created Documents - Cash and Credit Cards

Debit the dealerís account for the total cash sales of oil company owned products.
Debit the clearing house accounts for total credit card sales. The oil company will
be reimbursed for this amount during the credit card settlement when it claims
the money back from the credit card clearing house.
Credit the dealer for commission on his credit card and cash sales of oil company
owned products.
Charge the dealer a participation fee on credit card transactions. The participation
fee is the amount that the oil company charges the dealer for handling the credit
card transactions on their behalf.
In our template, the amount of company owned products sold by cash is calculated
as the difference between meter readings, and credit and fleet card transactions
per product.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 511



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Cash and Credit Card Document

Figure 211: Cash and Credit Card Document

The sales revenue for fuels sold by fleet cards (here 1,000.- EUR) is posted in
the fleet card settlement (see unit 7).
The participation fee for credit cards sales may differ between oil company owned
products and dealer owned products.
The follow on documents created may include:
ï FI accounting document
ï Profit center documents
ï CO-PA (profitability analysis)

512 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Created Documents ñ Fleet Cards

Figure 212: Created Documents - Fleet Cards

Credit the dealers' account for the sales of dealer owned products since, in the case
of fleet cards, the oil company has to buy the dealer owned products from the
dealer and ìsellî it to the fleet card company. The oil company will be reimbursed
for this amount during the fleet card settlement when claiming the money back
from the fleet card company.
Credit the dealer for commissions on oil company owned products sold by the
dealer on behalf of the oil company by fleet cards.
Charge the dealer a participation fee on fleet card transactions. The participation
fee is the amount that the oil company charges the dealer for handling the fleet
card transactions on their behalf.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 513



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Fleet Card Document

Figure 213: Fleet Card Document

The invoice to the service station partners contains two documents: one for sales
by credit card and cash and one for sales of dealer owned products by fleet card.
The service station partner is not invoiced for fleet card sales.
The service station partner invoice for fleet cards is only used to:
ï Credit the commission on sale of oil company owned products
ï Charge the participation fee for fleet cards
ï Credit the sales of dealer owned products paid for using fleet cards

Material Handling Group - Ownership of Products
Various characteristics, such as product ownership, are determined using the
material handling group attached to the business location.

514 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Payment Cards and Service Station Partner Invoicing

Figure 214: Material Handling Group - Ownership of Products

The billing treatment indicator is set for oil company owned products.
You assign material handling groups to business locations to enable the system
to determine whether a material is owned by the oil company (important for
a CODO relationship):
ï If Billing treatment is selected, the material is owned by the oil company, for

example, fuels.
ï If Billing treatment is not selected, the material is not owned by the oil

company, for example, shop products.

Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

Analyzing the Service Station Invoicing

Figure 215: Analyzing the Service Station Invoicing

ï Display data from billing documents created by the service station partner

invoicing process
ï Navigate to the billing documents themselves
Use the tree on the left side of the SAP screen to display:
ï Summarized billing data for:

ñ Period overviews (monthly)
ñ Daily overviews

ï Detailed daily information for a specific day for each service station partner,
such as:
ñ Fuels information
ñ Payment cards information
ñ Daily summary

ï Billing documents

is also stored in the SAP system but flagged with an error. The relevant
transactions need to be corrected to include them in the normal payment card
transaction process (SSP invoicing and CH settlement). The POS system
at your business location has failed, so the service station partner has sent
you the paper receipts of the relevant purchases.

Note the numbers of the invoices.
Two invoices are created because in this scenario the oil company
defines a difference between credit cards and fleet cards. Credit card
handling is a service provided by the oil company to the partner. The
oil company receives the credit card transactions through the POS
system and will deal with the credit card clearing house on the partnerís

Continued on next page

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 537



Unit 8: Service Station Retailing IOG100

behalf. The oil company reduces the partner invoice by the value of the
credit card sales and will receive reimbursement for this amount from
the clearing house using the clearing house settlement process.
In this scenario fleet card companies (fleet card clearing houses)
are treated by the oil company as customers. Oil company owned
products purchased at the service station by fleet card are bought from
the service station partner by the oil company and then sold to the
fleet card company. The partner is not charged for the oil company
owned products purchased on fleet cards and the fleet card company is
invoiced as part of the fleet card settlement process.
The difference in handling between credit cards and fleet cards requires
at least two separate billing documents for the service station partner.
The first document contains the cash and credit card sales (called the
cash and credit card document) at the service station and the second
document contains the fleet card sales (called the fleet card document).
The cash and credit card document behaves as a ìtrue invoiceî, as its
purpose is to bill the partner for the sale of oil company owned products.
The fleet card document behaves as a ìcredit noteî, as its purpose is to
credit the partner for the sale of dealer owned products.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 545



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics
Lesson Overview
This lesson will explain the fundamental basics of a business warehouse solution
and how SAP Business Intelligence supports a user to perform analytical and
reporting tasks. It will outline the architecture of the SAP Business Intelligence
solution and briefly discuss the functionality available to present reporting and
analytical results to an end user.

Lesson Objectives
After completing this lesson, you will be able to:
ï Describe the architecture and major components of the SAP BI architecture
ï Describe the reporting features available to support end users
ï Describe oil and gas business scenarios available out of the box for SAP

Business Intelligence

Business Example
Your company has identified a need for users to access and receive reports from
one integrated Business source. In addition to the reports which are already
available for past and present data, you are also looking for other analytical
possibilities to enhance the future of your business.

546 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

Data Warehouse System

Figure 216: Data Warehouse System

A data warehouse system serves primarily to stage information of important
business processes and areas extracted from various data sources.
Data from mostly heterogeneous systems and with different degrees of detail are
brought together in order to provide this data in a scalable form to the whole
organization.
By using personalized and predefined reports or freely definable queries this data
can be analyzed for deviations and significant facts.
Areas of concern:
ï Comparison between forecasted and actual demand of products in a region
ï Tank usage in different plants
ï Performance of transportation systems
ï Comparison of planned vs. real budget
In brief, a data warehouse can
ï pool data from different, mostly heterogeneous sources,
ï overcome this heterogeneity on different levels (system, schema, and data),
ï stage data in the form required by the user.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 547



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Decision-makers urgently need reliable information from Production, Purchasing,
Sales and Distribution, Finance, and Human Resources departments. They require
an up-to-date and comprehensive picture of each individual business area and of
the business as a whole. This places considerable demands on data staging from
the underlying data sources.

Figure 217: What we expect from BI

The information must be stored in a homogeneous and consistent form at a central
location where it can be called up. Therefore, modern data warehouses require a
separate database that an independent application environment can use to provide
the required services objectively.
Efficient analysis techniques with powerful multi-dimensional visualization are
indispensable on the presentation side of the data warehouse. The system must be
able to cope with the information needs of the various user groups.
The demands made on the source systems are not so high. What is needed here
is an economic and comprehensive preparation of the data that is required by
the data warehouse.

548 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

The following demands are made on a data warehouse:
ï standardized structuring and presentation of all company information,
ï an easy-to-use, single-point of access to all company information,
ï sophisticated business reporting methods for self-service analysis at all

levels,
ï fast and cost-effective installation,
ï a high performance environment,
ï data staging from heterogeneous environment,
ï release of source systems and IT organization,
ï data access independent of the source system, and
ï analysis of data over a specific period of time, and the storage of historical

information (time-dependent master data).

Figure 218: SAP Business Intelligence

SAP BI allows you to analyze data from operational SAP applications or any other
business application. You can also extract and analyze data from external sources
such as databases, online services, and the Internet.
The system (data storage, loading and reporting), which is pre-configured for
core areas and processes, allows you to examine the relationships in every area
of your company.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 549



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

The realization of SAP BI is aimed for the following:
ï data warehousing system with optimized data structures for reporting and

analysis,
ï separate system,
ï OLAP engine and tools
ï comprehensive data-warehousing architectural base,
ï automated data warehouse management, and
ï pre-configuration using SAP global business know-how.
With these goals in mind, SAP has opted for a separate data-warehousing solution
that handles reporting activities as an autonomous business component, even
providing a separate server with its own database and SAP system: SAP Business
Intelligence.
All of the requirements and objectives mentioned so far have been met in the
conception and architecture of SAP BI.
Having implemented SAP BI and its metadata repository (description of data), the
customer has the clear advantage of being able to use the entire SAP know-how
built up over the many years of experience in developing business software
solutions. All SAP systems can be configured as source systems, and provide data
for all preconfigured core-areas and processes.

Terminology and Objects in SAP BI
To get an overview of important terminology used within SAP BI important terms
will be introduced on the following pages.

550 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

Figure 219: Terminology (I)

InfoObject
Business analysis-objects (customers, sales volumes, and so on) are called
InfoObjects in SAP BI. These InfoObjects can be divided into characteristics and
key figures. Characteristics can be further divided into units, time characteristics,
and technical characteristics (for example, request ID). Key figures are all data
fields that are used to store values or quantities (sales volumes, net sales, costs,
and so on). Characteristics describe the affiliation of key figures.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 551



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Figure 220: Terminology (II)

InfoCube.
The central data containers that form the basis for reports and analyses in SAP BI
are called InfoCubes. They contain key figures (sales volumes, incoming orders,
actual costs, and so on) and a link to the characteristics (master data of the SAP
BI system such as cost centers, customers, materials, and so on). Key figures
and characteristics are InfoObjects. Each individual InfoCube should contain a
self-contained dataset, since queries refer primarily to one InfoCube.
Master data in the BI system consists of attributes of a characteristic (for example,
the person responsible for a cost center), as well as hierarchies and texts of a
characteristic.
An InfoCube consists of several database tables that are linked according to the star
schema. They include a fact table that contains the InfoCube key figures, as well
as several surrounding dimension tables that store the links to the characteristics.
ï Each InfoCube has one fact table and a maximum of 16 dimension tables.
ï Each fact table can contain a maximum of 233 key figures.
ï A dimension can contain up to 248 freely available characteristics.
InfoCubes are stored in structures in the SAP BI system. If you want to store an
InfoCube, you create a new folder or use an existing one. This is similar to the
method used when storing data on your PC: These folders are called InfoAreas in
SAP BI.

552 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

Figure 221: Terminology (III)

InfoProvider
InfoProvider is the super-ordinate term for an object that you can use to create
reports in Business Explorer (BEx). InfoProviders are objects or views that are
relevant to reporting.
InfoProviders include various database meta-objects that deliver data for query
definitions. The type of data procurement differs depending on the InfoProvider
used. However, the type of data procurement has no influence on reporting.
InfoProviders deliver data that can be analyzed using a query.
There are two types of data stores. Physical stores include:
ï BasicCubes,
ï Data Store Objects, and
ï InfoObjects.
Logical views of physical data stores include:
ï InfoSets,
ï RemoteCubes,
ï VirtualInfoCubes, and
ï MultiProviders.
The previous figure gives an overview of SAP BI reportable objects, divided into
data targets that contain physical data, and InfoProviders that only contain logical
views. From the BEx view, only InfoProviders are accessed. The way in which
the data is modeled is inconsequential to the BEx toolset.
DataStore Object

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 553



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

A DataStore Object stores data at the basic level (document level). It is normally
used to resolve and consolidate datasets. These datasets are often from various
data sources and/or source systems
Data Warehousing Workbench
The Data Warehousing Workbench is a workplace for SAP BI administrators.
Data Warehousing Workbench functions are used to configure, control, and
administrate SAP BI.
SAP BI enables the analysis of data from operative SAP applications as well as all
other business applications and external data sources such as databases, online
services, and the Internet.

Figure 222: SAP Business Intelligence Architecture

As shown above, the SAP BI architecture provides for the acquisition,
transformation, storage, analysis, access and distribution of data from both SAP
and non-SAP sources.
Data Warehouse Layer
The Data Warehouse Layer is responsible for the cleansing, loading, storage, and
the management of the data needed for the enterprise.
Through different interfaces it is possible to extract data from operative SAP
applications as well as all other business applications and external data sources
such as databases, online services, and the Internet.
BI Platform Layer

554 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

The BI platform layer contains BI services to support complex analysis tasks and
functions. It contains the Analytic Engine, which processes the data requested
through BEx analysis navigations and supports the interface that allows for the
entry and manipulation of data as part of BI Integrated Planning. Finally, special
analysis tools such as the Analysis Process Designer (APDE) and the Data Mining
provide the analysts at your company with the tools to merge, mine, preprocess,
store, and analyze data without support from your technical team.
Business Explorer Suite
The Business Explorer Suite provides flexible reporting and analysis tools targeted
at both power users and end users. You can use these tools for strategic analysis
and to support the decision-making process in your organization. These tools
include query, reporting, and analysis functions. BEx enables a broad range of
users to access BI information using the SAP NetWeaver Portal, intranet/Internet
(Web Application Design), or mobile devices (WAP or i-mode-enabled mobile
telephones and personal digital assistants). Many analysis features are available;
slice and dice (pivot like functions is only the beginning. In addition, many
outputs options are supported, including formatted Microsoft Excel, Web cockpits,
formatted Web output (BEx Reports) and Adobe PDF documents.

Figure 223: Different User Types in SAP BI

New studies have shown that up to 70 percent of all OLAP system users are basic
users. Compared to the advanced users and query developers, basic users only use
the analytical functions of the system on a very small scale. This is because the
basic users usually carry out predefined queries with fixed datasets. Therefore,
most of SAP users need a simple user interface.
However, the experienced users and query developers who design and carry out
information analyses on several levels must be able to use a comprehensive and
effective range of tools for their analyzing options.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 555



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

SAP catered to these various user needs when developing the Business Intelligence.

Figure 224: BI Business Explorer Suite

The Business Explorer Suite provides flexible reporting and analysis tools targeted
at both power users and end users. To analysis, access and distribute the data
following tools are available:
The BEx Query Designer is the tool for creating query definitions. These query
definitions structure how data from a variety of sources will be structured for
presentation to the user. Power users can use the BEx Query Designer to create
queries based on data stored in BI data providers in an easy and intuitive manner
using Drag and Drop. Analyses and reports can draw on components that need to
be created only once but can be reused in many queries. BEx queries and query
views are the basis for analyses, reports, and planning scenarios in the BEx Web
Application Designer, BEx Report Designer, and BEx Analyzer (Excel Add-in).
Within the BEx Web area, the Web Analyzer provides for web-based execution
of queries as well as ad hoc analysis of data from a wide array of sources.
The BEx Web Application Designer is a complete toolset for designing and
deploying custom web applications within the organization. These applications
often contain data from queries, but could also provide access to other structured
and unstructured data. The BEx Report Designer allows for a high degree of
control over the formatting of query output. They can change the layout of reports
individually, add headers and footers to reports and pages, integrate texts, pictures,
and charts, enter page breaks, etc. The Web Item Report enables power users to
include formatted reports in BEx Web applications.
Queries can be executed within several different user interfaces. The BEx
Analyzer makes use of Microsoft Excel to provide a well-understood interface
for viewing and analyzing data. Information Broadcasting is accomplished by the
BEx Broadcaster that provides all the functions necessary to distribute queries,

556 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

reports and analyses to end users and to the Enterprise Portal. In addition, the
BEx Broadcaster provides a wide range of functions such as alerting and the pre
calculation of results.
The SAP NetWeaver Portal serves as the main interface for users wanting to
access business information. With powerful Knowledge Management features
for a wide range of collaboration and feedback activities, the SAP NetWeaver
Portal integrates the reporting and analysis tasks of users of all types. BEx Web
Applications and BEx reports are deployed in SAP NetWeaver Portal. They easily
converted into PDF format and printout.
ï Empower business users
ï Design queries in an easy and intuitive way and use as the basis for a

user-oriented presentation of information and effective analysis
ï Design presentation-quality, print-optimized formatted reports
ï Wizard-based creation of Web applications for all user types - no coding

necessary
ï Provides BI data in an user-oriented and flexible way
ï Information is provided for all types of BI users
ï Personalized access to BI information in SAP NetWeaver Portal supports

quick and efficient decision making
ï Simple conversion of reports and Web applications to PDF files allowing BI

information to be printed as required.

Figure 225: Query Designer I

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 557



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Using the SAP BI reporting functions, you can evaluate a dataset from an
InfoProvider according to various characteristics and key figures. To do this, you
define a query for your chosen InfoProvider in the BEx Query Designer.
To support you in your query definition the BEx Query Designer contains the
following main functions:
ï Definition of queries in the BEx Query Designer for OLAP reporting and

also for tabular reporting.
ï Definition of reusable restricted key figures
ï Definition of reusable calculated key figures
ï Definition of conditions
ï Definition of exceptions
ï Definition of variables

558 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

The query designer contains many different panes of which some are only
displayed when a function button is pressed. The following key panes are
available under ìRows/Columnsî.
1. Directory tree of selected InfoProvider

Once you selected the relevant InfoProvider for your query, all available
objects (dimensions, key figures, structures) display in the directory tree in
the left screen area of the Query Designer.

2. Free Characteristics:
You transfer those characteristics into the free characteristics area that do not
display in the initial view of the results when you execute the query in the
BEx Analyzer or on the Web. You can then integrate these characteristics
into the results through navigation steps. You can also use free characteristics
for selecting filter values in the report

3. Rows:
You define the rows of your report in this area via drag and drop

4. Columns:
You define the columns of your report in this area via drag and drop

5. Preview:
This area gives a preview of the initial query results area depending on the
arrangements set in pane for columns and rows.

6. Tasks:
A list of suitable tasks related to the highlighted query object are displayed
here. You can click on any of the tasks in the list to go directly to the settings.

7. Where-used:
This pane provides information relating to the use of the query object.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 559



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Figure 226: Query Designer II

Via ìFiltersî following panes are available in addition:
1. Characteristic Restriction

Here you define the characteristic filter values which apply to the entire
result set.

2. Default Values
In this pane you define the characteristic filter values which should be used
for the initial view of the result set. The user may choose to modify these
filters in the result.

3. Properties
Here is where the settings relevant to the currently highlighted query object
are displayed. You can also make changes to the setting here. Often there
will be multiple tabs used to organize the settings in this pane.

4. Messages
This pane is where informational or error messages are displayed

560 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

To create a query, you can expand or collapse the InfoProvider directories by
choosing the plus or minus symbol. By expanding the key figure node in the
InfoProvider tree, for example, you can display a list of all the key figures for
the InfoProvider.
ï Use Drag&Drop to transfer the characteristics, key figures, and structures

of the InfoProvider into the various panes within the Query Designer. You
can also include characteristic attributes and variables in the query definition
in this way

ï You can use the right mouse button to call all of the valid functions that
are in the current context menu. To do this, first select the required query
component, then, select a menu entry from the context menu.

ï By double-clicking on an element in the query designer, you call a dialog
box that offers the default function for that element. For example, if you
double-click on a characteristic, the dialog box for restricting characteristics
appears

ï If you click on an element you will notice that the suitable tasks are also
displayed in the Task Pane. Simply click on one of the tasks to open up
the dialog box to make the settings.

Figure 227: Restricted Key Figures

Defining Restricted Key Figures

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 561



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Restricted key figures are (basic) key figures of the InfoProvider that are restricted
(filtered) by one or more characteristic selections. The key figure that is restricted
by one or more characteristic selections can be a basic key figure, a calculated key
figure, or a key figure that is already restricted.
By using restricted key figures, you can focus the query result on certain values.
Unlike a filter, whose restrictions are valid for the entire query, for a restricted key
figure, only the key figure in question is restricted to its allocated charateristic
value or characteristic value interval. Scenarios such as comparing a particular
key figure for various time segments, or plan/actual comparison for a key figure
if the plan data is stored using a particular characteristic can be realized using
restricted key figures.
You can create restricted key figures at the InfoProvider level, or locally in the
query definition. Restricted key figures that are defined at the InfoProvider level
are available in every query definition of the InfoProvider in question.

Figure 228: Calculated Key Figures

In the Query Designer, you can use a formula to calculate key figures that are not
in the InfoProvider by using basic key figures, restricted key figures and existing
calculated key figures in the formula definition.
Defining Calculated Key Figures at the Query Level
You can use all basic key figures of the InfoProvider in question, as well as the
newly defined restricted and calculated key figures of the InfoProvider, to define
new calculated key figures. You can define calculated key figures at both the
query level and the InfoProvider level. At the query level, the calculated key

562 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

figure is valid only for the query in question. If you create a calculated kea figure
at the InfoProvider level, you can use it in all queries that are based on the same
InfoProvider.
Defining Calculated Key Figures at the InfoProvider Level
To define calculated key figures at the query level, you can include all types of
key figures which are defined at the InfoProvider level, these include basic key
figures, restricted key figures and, of course, calculated key figures. However you
must remember that you do not have access to all operators as some operators
only make sense at the query level. Dońt forget that once you have defined the
calculated key figure at the InfoProvider level it is not automatically included in
your query, you must drag and drop it to where it should be used.

Figure 229: Conditions

Conditions are used for a flexible restriction of a report so that only the most
important information is displayed. This enables a more efficient analysis of data
when large amounts of data are analyzed.
If a condition is applied to a query, no figures are changed. Instead, the numbers
not relevant for display are hidden.
Conditions have no effect on the values displayed in the results rows. The results
row of a query with an active condition is the same as the results row of a query
without this condition.
It is possible to define multiple conditions for a query. A characteristic value is
only displayed when it fulfills all (active) conditions of the query. The result set
is therefore independent of the evaluation sequence.
Examples for Conditions:

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 563



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Top N, Bottom N:
Customers: Top 3 with bottom 5 sales volumes
A list of the three customers with the strongest sales and the five customers
with the weakest sales is displayed, that is, the union of both condition rows
Top 3 Sales and Bottom 5 Sales.

Top Percent, Bottom Percent:
Material: Top 25% of sales revenue
You receive a list of the strongest materials ñ with respect to revenue ñ until
25% of the total revenue is attained.
Material: Bottom 25% of sales revenue
You receive a list of the weakest materials ñ with respect to revenue ñ until
25% of the total revenue is attained

Figure 230: Exceptions

The functions in exception reporting enable you to select and highlight unusual
deviations of key figure values in a query. You can see deviations from predefined
threshold values or intervals in the query result displayed in different colors if
the exception is active. Early spotting of these deviations provides the basis for
timely and effective reactions.

564 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

Exception reporting is made up of three functional areas:
ï Defining exceptions

ñ Determining threshold values or intervals that are given a priority
(bad, critical, good). The priority given to an exception corresponds
to pre-assigned colors that become more ëintenseí the greater the
deviation.

ñ Determining the characteristic/key figure combination(s) that the
exception is to affect.

ï Evaluating exceptions online
ñ The cell areas of the table of an executed query for which the defined

exceptions were exceeded or fallen short of are highlighted in color
according to the definition.

ñ Evaluating exceptions in the background
With the BEx Broadcaster, it is possible to check queries for exceptions
in the background. If a threshold value for an exception is exceeded or
not reached, a document is created immediately and distributed to a
predefined list of recipients by e-mail, to the portal, or as an alert.

Exceptions for a query defined in the Query Designer are globally valid for a
query in all workbooks and Web applications.

Figure 231: Variables

Variables are used to create flexible reports with free selection of characteristic
values. Variables serve as place holders within a query that are filled with values
when the query or a Web application containing the query is executed.
ï The variable type specifies where a variable can be used:

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 565



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

ñ Characteristic value variables
Characteristic value variables represent characteristic values and can be
used wherever characteristic values can be used.

ñ Hierarchy variables
Hierarchy variables represent hierarchies and can be used wherever
hierarchies can be selected.

ñ Hierarchy node variables
Hierarchy node variables represent a node in a hierarchy and can be
used wherever hierarchy nodes can be used.

ñ Text variables
Text variables represent a text and can be used in descriptions of
queries, calculated key figures, restricted key figures and formulas.

ñ Formula variables
Formula variables represent numerical values and can be used in
formulas and for selecting exceptions and conditions.

ï The processing type determines how a variable is filled with a value for the
runtime of the query or Web application:
ñ Manual Entry/Default Value

Values can be entered manually. It is also possible to select a default
value, which can be specified when defining a variable.

ñ Replacement Path
Characteristic value variables with the processing type Replacement
Path can be replaced with the results of another query.

ñ Customer Exit
A function module exit can be used to fill variables.

ñ SAP Exit
SAP delivers a number of variables. There are variables that are
processed via automatic replacement using a predefined replacement
path.

ñ Authorizations
The processing type Authorization enables variables to be filled with
values automatically from the authorization of a user.

ï Variables are not dependent on the InfoProvider, only on the InfoObject. A
variable that has been defined for an InfoObject is available in all queries
that use this InfoObject.

566 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

Figure 232: Exchange With

To analyze business key figures (for example, total quantity) within existing
BI reports, BEx (Web) Analyzer offers different navigation functions to create
various views of the query data. The initial data view after the query is executed
has been specified during the query definition.
Navigation options within a query are accessible through context menu
(right-click) or can be executed via drag and drop of query elements.
On the following pages some of the most common navigation techniques using
drag and drop functionality will be explored.
Any time you want to swap the location of one object in the analysis with another
object, you may simply drag one item on top of the other and the change will be
made automatically. Above, the user swaps Storage Location for Plant. The user
could have also brought up the context menu for either characteristics and selected
Exchange ... with ... to effect the swap.

2006 / Q2 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 567



Unit 9: Analytics with SAP Business Intelligence IOG100

Figure 233: Drill Down

One of the most common navigation functions is the Drill Down (or Drill Across).
In the graphic above, the user drags Storage Location from the navigation area
and drops it on top of the values for Material. This has the effect of adding an
additional level of detail for Storage Location to the analysis.

Figure 234: Keep Filter

568 © 2007 SAP AG. All rights reserved. 2006 / Q2



IOG100 Lesson: Bulk Supply Chain Reporting and Analytics

You can select as filter value directly from the results area of an executed report.
To do this, you could position the cursor on the filter value required, and choose
Keep Filter Value from the context menu. The filter value is then displayed in
the report and the report results are restricted to the filter value in questions. Or
you could as the graphic shows simply drag the characteristic value you want to
use as a filter to the right side of the navigation area and drop it. The value will
automatically be used as a filter for the analysis.

Figure 235: Best Practice - Business Content

SAP Best Practices for Business Intelligence supports the fast and smooth
implementation of predefined scenarios that handle the most important business
requirements in the area of Business Intelligence.
The Business Content includes reporting models for SAP standard business
processes and support them out of the box.
To meet your requirements Business Content objects can be installed, altered
and enhanced easily with the objects needed. By using the Business Content
implementation time can be reduced significant.
